### AC-1 — Policy and Procedures (Control)

This requirement is about making sure everyone in the organisation understands the rules for who is allowed to access systems and information, and how those rules are followed in practice. Without clear, written guidance, the wrong people could gain access, access might not be approved or removed when it should be, and sensitive information could be misused or exposed. This could lead to financial loss, disruption, and breaches of legal or regulatory requirements.

The organisation must create and publish an organisation-wide access policy and supporting procedures. These must be written in plain language for all relevant roles, including all staff, contractors, and privileged users. They must explain the purpose of the policy, what it covers and does not cover, roles and responsibilities, leadership commitment, how different parts of the organisation work together, and how compliance will be checked—while also aligning with applicable laws and the organisation’s own rules.

The Chief Information Security Officer must be responsible for producing, maintaining, and sharing these documents. The policy and procedures must be reviewed at least every year and updated after any significant change, security incident or breach, audit finding, major organisational change, or change to relevant laws and regulations.

##### CISO-owned access control policy & procedures with review triggers

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Draft organisation-level **Access Control Policy** (purpose, scope, inclusions/exclusions, roles & responsibilities, management commitment, security/privacy coordination, compliance assurance, AC-family alignment, review triggers) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Draft **Access Control Procedures** runbooks (step-by-step) covering: identity lifecycle, access request/approval, privileged access handling, access reviews, exceptions, emergency access, contractor access, and deprovisioning | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Define **governance & ownership model**: confirm CISO as official owner, approval workflow, RACI for security/IAM/system owners/OT/ICS engineers, and escalation paths for exceptions | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Establish **controlled document lifecycle** in the repository (versioning, approval states, audit trail/change history, explicit review dates, event-driven update triggers for policy and procedures) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Create **dissemination packs** and communication plan: policy distribution to all personnel/contractors/privileged users; procedures distribution to system owners/network admins/OT-ICS engineers/IAM admins; include acknowledgement mechanism | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 12h | — |
| Implement **security & privacy collaboration evidence**: documented review/sign-off checkpoints in the workflow, including privacy impact considerations and recorded outcomes | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 12h | — |
| Validate **acceptance criteria & audit readiness**: tabletop review with stakeholders, ensure procedures describe “how” implementation occurs, confirm annual cadence and event triggers are mapped and evidenced | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 10h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 130h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Draft an organisation-wide access control policy, owned by the Chief Information Security Officer (CISO), including its purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, coordination arrangements, and how compliance will be checked.
- [ ] Draft access control procedures that set out, step by step, how to manage: user identity throughout its life cycle, requests for system access and how they are approved, privileged access (high-level permissions), access reviews, exceptions, and emergency access.
- [ ] Get documented approval (review and sign-off) from both the security programme and the privacy programme for the policy and procedures.
- [ ] Publish and share the policy with all staff, contractors, and privileged users through approved channels, and keep proof that it was distributed.
- [ ] Share and distribute the procedures with system owners, network administrators, operational technology (OT) and industrial control systems (ICS) engineers, and identity and access management (IAM) administrators through approved channels, with proof that they were sent.
- [ ] Set up a controlled document process that includes version numbers, a formal approval step, and a clearly stated date each year for review.
- [ ] Record when event-driven updates are triggered, and make sure the relevant policies and procedures are updated after incidents or breaches, audit findings, major organisational or system changes, or changes to applicable laws and regulations.


---

### AC-2 — Account Management (Control)

This expectation is about making sure that every person’s (and approved service’s) access to your system is set up correctly, clearly documented, and removed quickly when it is no longer needed. If this is not done, the wrong people may keep access after leaving or changing roles, accounts could be created without proper checks, and permissions could be broader than necessary—raising the risk of unauthorised access and misuse of data.

The organisation must define and record which types of accounts are allowed, and must specifically forbid shared, group, emergency, anonymous, temporary and guest accounts. It must also appoint an account manager, and record who is authorised, which groups or roles they belong to, and the exact permissions for each account. This includes which parts of the system or data they can use, whether additional identity checks are required, and any time limits.

New accounts must be approved by the system owner and the senior information security officer. Accounts must be created and changed only through a documented process that includes a request record, approval, and an audit trail. Any account changes triggered by events must be disabled within 24 hours.

Account use must be monitored and reviewed at least quarterly. The account manager and system owner must be notified within 24 hours when accounts are no longer required, when staff are terminated or transferred, or when someone’s “need to know” changes. If shared or group accounts are used, login details must be changed when members leave, and account actions must match the organisation’s termination and transfer processes.

##### IAM-enforced account lifecycle with prohibited account types

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define prohibited/authorised account types for the application and publish the IAM policy configuration requirements (individual + service only; block shared/group/emergency/anonymous/temporary/guest) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement IAM provisioning constraints and validation rules to prevent prohibited account types from being created/enrolled (including group/role membership restrictions and provisioning workflow guards) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Build the application entitlement model (role catalogue) mapping each application role to privilege set, access scope, MFA requirement, and time-of-day/day-of-week restrictions; include least-privilege and need-to-know alignment | System Design Authority | Business Unit | 32h | — |
| Configure IAM-to-application entitlement provisioning (e.g., SSO/SCIM/connector mapping) so recorded entitlements are enforced and exportable for audit (privilege set, access scope, MFA, time restrictions) | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 56h | £8,000 |
| Implement approval-backed lifecycle workflow integrated with the ticket/change system for create/enable/modify/disable/remove, capturing approver evidence (system owner + senior agency information security officer) and linking outcomes to IAM/app entitlements | Project Manager | Enterprise | 48h | £6,000 |
| Automate lifecycle triggers (HR termination/transfer and need-to-know changes) to disable accounts within 24 hours, and ensure application consumes IAM state to make disablement effective | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 64h | £10,000 |
| Configure 24-hour notifications to account managers (and required stakeholders) for no-longer-required, termination/transfer, and need-to-know changes; include notification logging and correlation IDs for audit | Operations Lead | Department | 24h | £2,500 |
| Deliver quarterly account review capability with evidence pack and attestation workflow (report generation, attestation capture, storage/retention, and review against role catalogue/least-privilege rules) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 320h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £26,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set up identity and access management (IAM) provisioning rules so this application can use only individual accounts and service accounts. Block all other account types, including shared, group, emergency, anonymous, temporary, and guest accounts.
- [ ] Define the application role catalogue, including for each role: what it can access (systems and data), the minimum permissions needed (least privilege), whether multi-factor authentication (MFA) is required, and any limits on when access is allowed (time of day and day of week).
- [ ] Set up the identity and access management (IAM) account process so that creating, enabling, changing, disabling, or removing an account requires approval from the system owner and the senior agency information security officer, using the ticketing system.
- [ ] Set up automatic “need-to-know” change triggers for hiring, leaving, and role transfers so that any affected accounts are disabled within 24 hours, and ensure the application follows the current identity and access management settings (single sign-on (SSO) and system for cross-domain identity management (SCIM)).
- [ ] Set up automated notifications to the account manager (and the system owner where required) within 24 hours for changes that are no longer needed, changes related to termination or transfer, and changes that are only for people who need to know or for usage updates.
- [ ] Schedule quarterly reviews of each account and keep evidence that shows active accounts match the approved role catalogue.


---

#### AC-2.1 — Automated System Account Management (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that system accounts are created, updated, paused, and removed in a controlled, automated way, and that the right people are informed immediately. Without this, staff could accidentally leave accounts active after someone changes role or leaves, and unauthorised access could go undetected for too long. It could also mean unusual account use is not noticed.

The organisation is expected to use built-in system features to manage the full account life cycle (create, enable, change, disable, remove), automatically monitor how these accounts are used, and automatically send email notifications to the account managers whenever an account is created, enabled, changed, disabled, or removed, and when a person is terminated or transferred. It should also automatically flag unexpected account activity and report it to the responsible account managers, keep records of what happened and when, and document the procedures, responsibilities, system design, and settings that enable these automated actions and notifications.

##### Event-driven system account lifecycle with automated alerts

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define system-account ownership mapping model (authoritative source, versioning, change control) and notification target resolution logic | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design and implement event-driven lifecycle workflows for system accounts (create/enable/modify/disable/remove) using internal system functions only; include workflow triggers and guardrails to prevent ad-hoc changes | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 80h | — |
| Implement automated email notification service for lifecycle events (templating, correlation IDs/message IDs, audit-record links, multi-recipient support) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Implement user termination/transfer trigger handling for system account ownership/usage (disable/remove or entitlement update as applicable) with end-to-end audit correlation | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Integrate telemetry ingestion for system-account authentication/activity into SIEM/monitoring; implement atypical usage detections (rules, thresholds, maintenance-window logic) and alert routing to SOC and account managers | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 72h | £25,000 |
| Build auditability and evidence generation package: lifecycle event audit records, workflow configuration exports, notification template/config exports, sample audit records per event type, and sample atypical-usage alert evidence | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Testing, hardening, and operational readiness: unit/integration tests for workflows, notification verification, SIEM rule validation with test data, runbooks, and change-management sign-off | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 352h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £25,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep an official record that maps each system account to its account manager who is responsible for it.
- [ ] Set up automated lifecycle processes for system accounts to handle account creation, activation, changes, suspension, and deletion, using internal system functions.
- [ ] Set up event-based triggers so that every stage change produces a unique reference number (correlation ID), making it easier to track and verify actions for audit purposes.
- [ ] Send automated email notifications based on templates to account managers for every stage of the customer lifecycle, and for termination or transfer triggers.
- [ ] Send system account authentication and activity logs into the security information and event management (SIEM) system and set up rules to detect unusual usage.
- [ ] Set up alert routing so unusual-usage notifications are sent to the relevant account manager(s), linked to the corresponding lifecycle audit records.
- [ ] Test the full end-to-end process using test cases that cover every stage of the lifecycle, plus at least one unusual way the system might be used.


---

#### AC-2.2 — Automated Temporary and Emergency Account Management (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that short-term and emergency user accounts do not remain active longer than agreed. If temporary or emergency access is left enabled after its agreed end time, it increases the risk that someone could continue using it by mistake or misuse it, even after the original need has ended.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must automatically disable any temporary and emergency accounts after 24 hours. This should be done using built-in automated account-management features, rather than relying on an administrator to switch them off manually.

The organisation should also have clear account-management rules and procedures, with documented system settings and design. It must be able to provide system-generated records showing which temporary and emergency accounts were disabled and the date and time they were disabled. These records should be supported by audit records and relevant internal documentation.

People responsible for account management and system administration must ensure the automated process is in place and working as intended.

##### Automate 24-hour disablement for temporary/emergency accounts

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Confirm in-scope IdP/IGA account types and map “temporary” vs “emergency” to concrete identity objects (expiring role assignment, group membership, time-bound account) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Define lifecycle data model and workflow stamping: enablement timestamp + expiry timestamp (enablement + 24h) written by the provisioning workflow as the single source of truth | IAM/IGA Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Configure IdP/IGA automated lifecycle rules to revoke sign-in/disable accounts at expiry (no admin intervention) and ensure correct handling of edge cases (renewal, manual overrides blocked, time drift) | IAM/IGA Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement auditable evidence: enable lifecycle event logging, create/extend reporting query to list temporary/emergency accounts with enablement time, expiry time, and disablement/revocation timestamp | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Build non-production test plan and execute timing validation at the 24-hour boundary (including acceptable timing window and verification of no manual steps) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Operational monitoring: implement scheduled job/alerting to flag any temporary/emergency accounts with expiry older than 24 hours and confirm they are disabled; integrate alerts to SOC workflow | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 20h | £3,000 |
| Documentation and runbook for operations and audit: control description, configuration references, evidence locations, and escalation steps for failures | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 12h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 140h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £3,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define temporary and emergency access as identity records that automatically expire (for example, a time-limited role, group, or account) and that use a consistent identifier.
- [ ] Set up the organisation’s identity provider (IdP) and identity governance and administration (IGA) workflow to record the time when access is enabled, and to set the access expiry time to 24 hours after it is enabled.
- [ ] Set up automatic disablement (or sign-in revocation) when temporary or emergency accounts expire.
- [ ] Turn on and keep audit logs for key lifecycle events (creation, setting an expiry date, disabling or revoking) and check that the logs are complete.
- [ ] Create an audit report that lists any temporary or emergency accounts that have been disabled, and the date and time they were disabled.
- [ ] Run a timing test in a non-production environment to confirm the disablement happens automatically at the 24-hour mark.
- [ ] Set up a scheduled check to identify any temporary or emergency accounts that have passed their expiry date, and confirm that they are disabled.


---

#### AC-2.3 — Disable Accounts (Enhancement)

This requirement is about quickly turning off old or suspicious access accounts so they can’t be used after they should no longer be active. If expired accounts, accounts that are no longer linked to a real person, accounts found to have broken organisational rules, or accounts that have been unused for 90 days are left running, they can become an easy way for unauthorised access or misuse—even if nobody is currently using them.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must identify these accounts and disable them within 24 hours of confirming the trigger. The trigger could be the account expiry date, the point it becomes unlinked from a user or person, the point a policy breach is identified, or the point 90 days of inactivity is reached.

The organisation should also keep clear records showing when each account was disabled and the reason why, so it can demonstrate that the 24-hour timing was consistently followed.

##### Automate account disablement within 24h using IdP/IGA triggers

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Map authoritative trigger sources (expiry/termination, HR/IGA orphan/unlinked signals, policy/anomaly flags, inactivity telemetry) and define trigger timestamp semantics (T0) and disablement SLA (24h) | IAM/IGA Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design IdP/IGA lifecycle workflow rules for each trigger type (expired, orphaned/unlinked, policy-violating/anomalous, 90-days inactivity) including idempotency, retry logic, and failure modes | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement disablement action with session/token revocation (force re-authentication, revoke refresh tokens, invalidate active sessions) and verify across supported IdP/IGA flows | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Configure SLA enforcement and alerting: record trigger reason, trigger timestamp, disablement timestamp; generate SLA-at-risk alerts and automated incident/ticket creation on delay | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Integrate audit evidence pipeline: persist workflow run identifiers and reason→timestamps mapping; forward to SIEM with retention alignment and searchable fields | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £6,000 |
| Build and execute test suite for acceptance criteria (per trigger type) including timing validation (≤24h), authentication denial, and evidence completeness; produce audit-ready test report | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort | 192h |  |
| Total Estimated Cost |  | £6,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and document the approved source systems and the specific date/time fields used to determine: expiry, whether a record is orphaned or not linked, whether it has any policy-violation flags, and inactivity after 90 days.
- [ ] Set up identity provider (IdP) and identity governance and administration (IGA) lifecycle automation to disable user accounts as soon as each trigger condition is met
- [ ] Put in place workflow controls to ensure any disablement happens within the ac-02.03_odp.01 time limit (24 hours), and raise alerts if there is a risk of missing the service level agreement (SLA).
- [ ] When the feature is enabled or disabled, it should revoke or end any active user sessions and make any existing access tokens for the application invalid.
- [ ] Integrate identity provider (IdP) and identity governance and administration (IGA) disablement logs with security information and event management (SIEM) to keep auditable records showing the time the action was triggered, the reason for it, and the time it was disabled.
- [ ] For each type of trigger, run and record test cases to show that disablement happens within 24 hours and that access is blocked after disablement.


---

#### AC-2.4 — Automated Audit Actions (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that every time an account is created, changed, enabled, disabled, or removed, the system automatically records what happened, when it happened, and who (or what system) made the change. This is important because changes to accounts are a common way for unauthorised access to be gained or for legitimate access to be misused. Without reliable records, it is difficult to spot mistakes, investigate suspicious activity, or confirm what was done and by whom.

To meet this expectation, your organisation must ensure the system automatically generates audit records for all account-management actions in a consistent format, keeps those records for the period your organisation has decided, and then regularly reviews, analyses, and reports on them in line with your internal audit review and reporting procedures.

##### Automate audit events for account lifecycle changes to SIEM

| Implement/enable audit event emission from the identity/access layer and/or application admin APIs for all five lifecycle actions, ensuring only supported provisioning/deprovisioning pathways are used | IAM Engineer | Business Unit | 56h | — |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and enforce the supported account start-to-finish processes for the application, using identity provider (IdP) and identity and access management (IAM) set-up and the application’s administration programming interfaces (admin APIs).
- [ ] Set up identity provider (IdP), identity and access management (IAM), and application audit logs to record when an account is created, changed, enabled, disabled, or removed.
- [ ] Set up security information and event management (SIEM) to standardise incoming event data, so each event is matched to the organisation’s AU-02 audit record fields: actor, target, action, timestamp, and source.
- [ ] Set up automatic, tamper-evident delivery of logs to the central security information and event management (SIEM) system, and check that all components have matching time settings using the Network Time Protocol (NTP).
- [ ] Set up security information and event management (SIEM) searches and alerts, and make sure account lifecycle events are included in the AU-06 review workflow.
- [ ] Run automated end-to-end tests that carry out every step in the system’s lifecycle and confirm that the related audit records are collected and can be retrieved.


---

#### AC-2.5 — Inactivity Logout (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure people do not leave their accounts logged in when they step away. If a user’s session remains active after 15 minutes with no activity, another person could potentially use that unattended access to view or change information, which could lead to financial loss, exposure of data, or disruption to services.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly explain a simple rule to users: after 15 minutes of inactivity, they must log out (sign out) if they expect they will be away for longer than 15 minutes. Users should do this using the normal log-out option, not by relying on automatic timeouts.

The organisation must also:
- include this rule in account and user guidance
- make sure the system is set up to support user log-out
- document how this will be handled
- keep records showing that users logged out when they followed the 15-minute expectation

##### Expectation-based manual logout guidance and reliable sign-out flow

- Category: Software
- Priority: High

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Draft and approve expectation-based logout wording for **ac-02.05_odp** (after 15 minutes inactivity, users must log out when they expect to be inactive longer than 15 minutes) and publish in the access control / acceptable use policy | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Update application security help and UI text to include a clear “Log out/Sign out” instruction plus a short “Step away safely” message near the logout control (linking to the expectation-based rule) | Project Manager | Business Unit | 12h | — |
| Implement reliable sign-out flow: integrate application logout with enterprise IdP sign-out (OIDC/SAML), ensure session/token invalidation and verify no residual authenticated session remains | Software Lead | Department | 40h | — |
| Validate logout behaviour end-to-end across supported browsers/devices and environments (dev/test/prod where applicable), including edge cases (back button, multiple tabs, token refresh, SSO re-entry) | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 24h | — |
| Configure audit/event forwarding for logout/sign-out: ensure IdP and application logout events are sent to SIEM with evidence fields (user, application, timestamp, event type, correlation identifiers) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Create SOC/helpdesk workflow for suspected non-compliance: intake form, triage steps, evidence checklist, and escalation path; include guidance for investigating “left logged in” reports | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Produce audit-ready evidence pack (policy extract, user guidance screenshots/links, sign-out integration test results, SIEM query examples, and workflow documentation) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 12h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 140h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Update the access control and acceptable use policy to clearly state the exact time-based expectation for ac-02.05_odp (15 minutes), and link to it from the application security help.
- [ ] Implement identity provider (IdP)–integrated sign-out (OpenID Connect (OIDC) and Security Assertion Markup Language (SAML) sign-out) so that the application’s **“Log out/Sign out”** option reliably ends user sessions and clears stored tokens.
- [ ] Add user guidance inside the product next to the logout button (and in onboarding materials) telling users to log out when they expect inactivity to last longer than 15 minutes.
- [ ] Set up audit logging so that identity provider (IdP) and/or application sign-out events are sent to the security information and event management (SIEM) system, including the user, application, time of the event, and the type of event.
- [ ] Set up a security operations centre (SOC) and helpdesk process to record suspected cases where users are left logged in, and to keep records from audit logs so they can be reviewed later.


---

#### AC-2.6 — Dynamic Privilege Management (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure people’s access rights change immediately when their job role or situation changes, rather than staying the same until they log out and back in. Without this, someone who is reassigned, working outside permitted hours, or who should no longer have access could continue using privileges they no longer deserve. In urgent situations, the organisation may also be slow to reduce access when it matters most.

The organisation is expected to run access checks using up-to-date information about the person and their circumstances. It must keep re-checking during use and immediately block or adjust access whenever the rules say it should change. This includes when communications encryption keys are updated, so the new key status is reflected right away. The organisation must document how this works, maintain clear procedures for updating the information that drives access, configure the systems to support these changes, and keep audit records showing when access was changed and why, including the effect of key updates.

##### Implement ABAC with real-time privilege revocation and key-epoch checks

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define authoritative attribute model for ABAC (job function/assignment, eligibility time windows, emergency/duress flags, communications key epoch/version) including data sources, ownership, and attribute semantics | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design ABAC policy set and enforcement strategy (request-time checks vs short-lived tokens with maximum staleness interval; fail-closed rules for high-risk actions) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement runtime ABAC evaluation at the central decision point (policy engine integration, attribute-to-decision mapping, deny/adjust semantics for active operations) | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Build real-time attribute propagation pipeline to the decision point (event-driven updates from HR/IAM/incident/duress workflows; propagation delay handling and fail-closed behaviour) | DevOps Lead | Business Unit | 48h | £18,000 |
| Implement key-epoch/version propagation into access decisions (bind communications-protected operations to current key epoch; deny operations bound to old epoch without session restart; define enforcement behaviour during propagation lag) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Add continuous re-evaluation enforcement in application services (request-time checks for sensitive actions; token re-check scheduling; maximum staleness implementation; integration tests for attribute-change scenarios) | Software Lead | Department | 64h | — |
| Implement audit evidence and monitoring (log attribute inputs, decision outcomes, revocation/denial events during active use, key-epoch changes; SIEM dashboards/alerts; retention and tamper-evidence alignment) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Execute security testing and assurance (ABAC policy verification, revocation timing tests, duress/emergency drills, key-rotation simulation, performance/load validation, and evidence pack for AC-2(6)) | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 48h | £12,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 352h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £36,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the official attribute set for attribute-based access control (ABAC), including job or assignment, time eligibility, emergency or duress status, and the communications key “epoch” or version, and identify the systems that are the single source of truth for these values.
- [ ] Set up attribute-based access control (ABAC) rules in the central access decision system, using policy-as-code with version control and review.
- [ ] Set up runtime enforcement so that access decisions are made for each individual request, or—during active sessions—no later than a documented maximum time interval before the decision information becomes outdated.
- [ ] Set up automatic, event-based sharing of user details from human resources, identity and access management, and duress (emergency) processes to the system that makes access decisions, and make sure that high-risk actions are blocked if the process fails.
- [ ] Update the communications key version used for access decisions when key-rotation events occur, and confirm that attempts to use the old key version are denied.
- [ ] Enable audit logging for changes that dynamically remove or block privileges, including the effects of key changes, and send the logs to security information and event management (SIEM) to provide evidence.


---

#### AC-2.7 — Privileged User Accounts (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that only the right people are given extra, high-impact access needed to run and protect key parts of the organisation, and that this access is kept under close watch. Without it, someone could keep powerful permissions after their job changes, or the wrong permissions could be granted and not be noticed—making it easier for mistakes or misuse to cause serious harm.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set up and manage privileged user accounts using its role-based access control (RBAC) scheme, so privileged access is granted based on defined roles. It must continuously monitor which privileged roles (or role features) each person has, track any changes to those roles or features, and regularly check whether the privileged access is still appropriate. If it is no longer appropriate, the organisation must promptly remove that privileged access, and keep clear records of what was changed and when, supported by audit and monitoring information that can be reviewed.

##### RBAC-governed privileged access with continuous role-change monitoring

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define privileged RBAC role catalogue and mapping to authoritative IdP groups/entitlements (including role taxonomy for key/account/db/system/network/web administration) | IAM/Identity Engineering Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Configure IdP/authorisation enforcement so privileged permissions are derived only from approved RBAC roles/groups (remove/disable supported direct/manual privileged grants) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £6,000 |
| Implement identity governance entitlement lifecycle for privileged roles (approval workflow, time-bounded access/expiry where supported, joiner/mover/leaver integration hooks) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 64h | £18,000 |
| Build continuous monitoring pipeline: stream IdP audit + group/entitlement change events to SIEM/monitoring; implement detections for add/remove/update and out-of-window privileged grants | SOC / SIEM Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | £12,000 |
| Automate prompt revocation on lifecycle triggers (termination/role change) with auditable evidence (actor/system, timestamp, reason) and ensure revocation propagates to target apps/admin surfaces | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £10,000 |
| Create and maintain system-generated privileged account list (authoritative query of privileged roles/groups, correlation to application/admin identifiers) and set up periodic review evidence packs | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Produce audit-ready reporting and retention controls (monthly high-risk reports, evidence retention verification, runbooks for responding to alerts and revocation failures) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | £2,500 |

Total Estimated Effort: **336 Hours**  
Total Estimated Cost: **£48,500**

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define role-based access control (RBAC) roles with elevated permissions for the application’s security-critical administration functions, and link each role to identity provider (IdP) groups and entitlements.
- [ ] Set up the identity provider and authorisation layer so that elevated permissions come only from approved role-based access control (RBAC) roles. Where possible, remove or disable any direct assignments of privileged access.
- [ ] Set up an identity governance process to approve requests for membership of privileged roles, and allow access only for a limited period of time.
- [ ] Send identity provider (IdP) privileged role and group change events to the security information and event management (SIEM) system, and set up alerts to detect when privileged roles are added, removed, or updated.
- [ ] Set up human resources lifecycle events (joiner, mover, leaver, and termination) so that privileged access is automatically removed when it is no longer appropriate.
- [ ] Create and store a system-generated list of privileged accounts based on the identity provider’s (IdP) official roles, and schedule regular reviews with supporting evidence packs.
- [ ] Check that audit logs are kept for the required period, and confirm that revocation events record who or what caused the change (actor or system), the date and time, and the reason.


---

#### AC-2.8 — Dynamic Account Management (Enhancement)

This requirement is about automatically creating, turning on, updating, and turning off the special accounts that on-premises systems and integrations use to do their work—exactly when they are needed. Without this, accounts can be created late, left enabled after they are no longer required, or given more access than they should have. This increases the risk of unauthorised access, misuse, and lingering access that is difficult to trace.

The organisation is expected to define which service accounts and privileged system accounts are included, document how this “account on-demand” process works, and include it in its security planning and day-to-day procedures. It must use automated controls to create, enable, manage, and disable these accounts while the system is running, including for previously unknown integration entities, but only after confirming that the request is properly authorised and that the approved level of access is granted or removed.

The organisation should also keep an up-to-date list of these accounts and record what the automation did, so that all actions can be audited.

##### JIT service account lifecycle automation with authorisation checks

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define in-scope dynamic system account model (metadata schema, lifecycle actions, privilege template identifiers, state model, deactivation triggers) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define and govern privilege templates (least-privilege mapping to groups/roles/entitlements per entity type; approval/exception rules; template versioning) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Establish authoritative entity registry and trust boundary (registry data model, eligibility rules, API access controls, onboarding workflow for entities) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Design and implement policy-as-code authorisation engine (validation of entity eligibility, lifecycle action permissions, template allowance, approval reference checks; deny-by-default) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Build runtime provisioning workflow and provisioning API (create/activate/manage/update/deactivate orchestration; idempotency; state transitions; integration with on-prem account targets) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Implement audit evidence pipeline (structured audit events for each lifecycle action; before/after privilege representation strategy; SIEM ingestion validation; retention/search fields) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Testing, security assurance, and operational readiness (unit/integration tests, negative/abuse cases, performance checks, runbooks, incident/rollback procedures, monitoring dashboards, pilot rollout) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £12,000 |
| Deployment and change management (release packaging, configuration management, environment rollout plan incl. DR considerations, operational handover, compliance sign-off) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | £3,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 328h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £15,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the required information (metadata) structure and the approved access levels (privilege templates) for the in-scope system accounts used by service accounts and privileged system accounts (ac-02.08_odp).
- [ ] Set up and manage an official register of integration entities and the access permissions they are allowed to have, so the automated provisioning process can look them up.
- [ ] Set up a provisioning service and workflow that handles live requests to create, activate, update, or deactivate an entity. Each request must include the entity’s ID and the requested set of permissions (privilege template).
- [ ] Before any lifecycle action is carried out, check that the authorisation rules defined in policy-as-code are approved against the entity registry and the privilege templates.
- [ ] Set up the target on-premises systems so that account status changes happen automatically when accounts are created or activated or deactivated. Specifically: create accounts in a disabled state, enable them when they are activated, and revoke access when they are deactivated.
- [ ] Set up structured audit and event records for every step in the lifecycle, including the result of each authorisation decision and the privilege level before and after the change, and send these records to the security information and event management (SIEM) system.
- [ ] Define the roles and responsibilities for handling exceptions when an entity is not listed in the registry or when an authorisation request is refused.


---

#### AC-2.9 — Restrictions on Use of Shared and Group Accounts (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that shared or group logins are only used when there is clear responsibility and actions can still be traced back to a specific person. Without these safeguards, the wrong person may use the account, mistakes or changes may go unchallenged, and investigations after an incident may be delayed because no one can be held accountable.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must only allow shared or group accounts when each one has a named custodian assigned, and that custodian’s responsibility is recorded. Access must be limited to only the approved tasks the organisation has documented for these accounts.

The organisation must also ensure individual accountability, either by linking each user to the shared or group account in a way that clearly shows who did what, or, if that linking is not used, by putting in place alternative measures that provide the same level of traceability. Before allowing such accounts, the organisation should consider and document the additional risk created by reduced accountability.

##### Custodian-governed shared/group accounts with per-user attribution

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define custodian-governed shared/group account data model (registry schema, approved-function taxonomy, lifecycle fields, validation rules) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Build/extend authoritative shared/group account registry integration (IAM/PAM/CMDB) with create/enable gate requiring named custodian + approved functions | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 64h | £15,000 |
| Configure application/admin console least-privilege and approved-function allow-lists for shared/group account usage (including any integrated admin consoles) | Security Engineer | Department | 48h | — |
| Implement PAM/access broker unique user-to-account/session attribution flow (user-authenticated sessions mapped to shared/group backend identity; session context propagated to actions) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 72h | £25,000 |
| Enforce “no direct use” controls: block or neutralise direct shared/group account authentication paths and ensure attempts generate non-attributable/no-action outcomes | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Configure audit logging and SIEM forwarding with required fields (user identity, shared/group account identifier, session ID, action, timestamp) and validate end-to-end audit trail | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £8,000 |
| Produce governance evidence pack: risk acceptance rationale, periodic review procedure, and reporting dashboards for custodian assignment + approved-function scope + mapping effectiveness | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 320h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £48,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set up a shared or group account register that records the account custodian, the approved uses, and the account’s lifecycle information.
- [ ] Set up an identity and access management (IAM) and privileged access management (PAM) approval step so shared or group accounts cannot be created or turned on unless the custodian is involved and the request is within the approved function scope.
- [ ] Limit application and administrative access so that shared or group accounts can only be used for specific, documented, approved purposes (least privilege and allow-list approach).
- [ ] Ensure each action can be traced back to the specific user by routing access to shared or group accounts through an access broker. The broker must record the link between the user, the account, the session, and the action taken.
- [ ] Set up and centralise audit logs in security information and event management (SIEM), including the user’s identity, the shared or group account identifier, the session ID, and the action that was carried out.
- [ ] Record and get approval for the risk assessment for using shared or group accounts, and schedule regular reviews of the account custodian and any approved functions.


---

#### AC-2.11 — Usage Conditions (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that special automated work accounts are used only in the correct way, at the correct time, and for the correct purpose. Without these limits, an account intended for routine system administration or automated batch jobs could be misused outside planned work periods, used as if a person were logging in directly, or left running for too long. This increases the risk of unauthorised changes, hidden misuse, and incidents that are difficult to trace.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set clear rules for every in-scope service account so that it:
- can be used only during approved maintenance windows
- cannot be used for interactive logons (no direct user-style sessions)
- can only run in time-limited sessions that never exceed 8 hours

The system must enforce these rules, record what happened, analyse any misuse, and raise alerts when an account is used outside the approved conditions. The alerts must include enough detail to identify the account and the specific rule that was broken.

##### Enforce service-account usage windows and block interactive logons

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Create/maintain authoritative inventory of in-scope service accounts, including metadata mapping to AC-2(11) usage conditions | Identity & Access Management (IAM) / Privileged Access Management (PAM) engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement “no interactive logons” enforcement via controlled access path (PAM broker/jump host/PAG) with identity-based deny for in-scope service accounts | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £25,000 |
| Configure audit logging for interactive attempts and enforcement denials (account identity, source, attempted action, rule outcome, timestamps) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement maintenance-window-only enforcement using machine-readable schedule source and policy-as-code/config automation; deny outside window with explicit denial reason | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £10,000 |
| Implement time-bounded session enforcement (terminate/suspend at ≤ 8 hours) aligned to the actual session mechanism used by the access path | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £5,000 |
| Create SIEM detection rules and SOAR/alert workflows for three violation types (outside window, interactive attempt, session duration breach) with required fields for accountability | Security Operations (SOC) / SIEM engineer | Enterprise | 32h | £8,000 |
| Run end-to-end validation and evidence pack for acceptance criteria (test cases, screenshots/log extracts, rule outcomes, retention settings, change-window verification) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 220h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £48,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a complete, authoritative list of all in-scope service accounts, and label or group them so they can be enforced under AC-2(11).
- [ ] Set up a controlled access route (privileged access management (PAM) / jump host / connection broker) for these service accounts, and turn off any direct ability for them to log on interactively.
- [ ] Set the policy to block interactive logins for the in-scope service account identities, and record (log) each blocked attempt.
- [ ] Add the maintenance schedule to the access enforcement process, and block access outside the approved time windows, recording the reason for each denial.
- [ ] Set session time limits for these service accounts so their sessions are ended or suspended after 8 hours or sooner, and record the start time, end time, and total duration for each session.
- [ ] Set up security information and event management (SIEM) and security orchestration, automation and response (SOAR) alerts to detect rule violations (attempts outside the allowed time window, interactive attempts, and sessions longer than eight hours), and check that the alert message includes the correct data fields.

#### AC-2.12 — Account Monitoring for Atypical Usage (Enhancement)

This requirement is about closely monitoring system accounts so you can quickly spot suspicious logins—especially logins that happen outside normal working hours or from locations or network areas that are not approved for that system. Without this, a malicious insider, stolen access, or an ongoing attack could go unnoticed while someone uses system accounts in ways that do not match normal behaviour.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- define what counts as unusual use (for example, out-of-hours activity and activity from an unapproved location or network segment)
- monitor all system accounts for these signs
- record enough information to identify which account was used, when it was used, and where it was used from

Whenever unusual use is detected, it must be reported to the Security Operations Centre incident response lead and the system owner.

Because this monitoring can reveal sensitive behaviour patterns, the organisation must complete and keep up to date a privacy risk assessment, and ensure the approach matches its privacy plan—including how the data is limited and protected.

- [ ] Maintain an inventory of all system accounts, and match each account to where it is authenticated (identity provider (IdP) versus local or legacy authentication) to ensure full coverage in the security information and event management (SIEM) system.
- [ ] Set up and standardise authentication logs in the security information and event management (SIEM) system so they record: the user account identifier, the time of the event, the source Internet Protocol (IP) address, and location and network-segment indicators.
- [ ] Set up security monitoring rules in security information and event management (SIEM) to detect system account sign-ins that happen outside approved hours or from unapproved locations or network segments.
- [ ] Set up security orchestration, automation and response (SOAR) playbooks so that every detection is escalated to the security operations centre (SOC) incident response lead and the system owner (routing map per ac-02.12_odp.02).
- [ ] Carry out a privacy impact assessment for unusual use monitoring, and set up privacy-aligned rules for how long the collected login information is kept and who can access it.


---

#### AC-2.13 — Disable Accounts for High-risk Individuals (Enhancement)

This requirement is about acting quickly to stop dangerous access by turning off the accounts of people assessed as high risk. If a person is credibly linked to an intention to cause harm using their authorised access, or if there is credible evidence that an attacker could cause harm through them, keeping their account active could allow unauthorised actions, damage the company’s systems and assets, harm other organisations, or harm individuals.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- define what counts as credible evidence of this kind
- identify the affected individuals
- disable their system accounts within 24 hours of discovering the evidence

The organisation must also:
- keep clear, verifiable records showing which accounts were disabled and when
- maintain a list of risky user activities to help identify affected people
- document the approach in its account-management procedures and related system plans

Finally, it must coordinate promptly with system administrators, information security staff, human resources, legal advisers, and the authorising officials to ensure the correct accounts are disabled properly, with appropriate oversight.

##### 24-hour high-risk account disablement via case-to-IdP workflow

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define structured “credible evidence / significant risk” criteria and evidence-tag taxonomy for case intake (including mapping to AC-2(13) 24-hour SLA) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Update SOC/insider-risk/HR/legal case template and workflow fields to capture discovery timestamp, evidence tags, affected identity attributes, and required approvals/override rationale | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design case-to-IdP identity mapping model (person → IdP user → directory accounts → federated app identities) including data contracts and error-handling for ambiguous matches | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement IdP admin automation to disable accounts and revoke sessions/tokens via APIs, producing audit-ready disablement records with start/end timestamps | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £12,000 |
| Implement downstream access cascade: SCIM deprovisioning triggers, federation group removal, and conditional access/session blocking to ensure sign-in is denied during propagation | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 260h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £26,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish clear, structured criteria for what counts as a “significant risk”, aligned with the organisation’s requirements, to provide credible evidence that there is an intention to cause harm or that the individual poses a threat to an adversary.
- [ ] Create a standard case or ticket template that records the exact time the issue was first identified and includes the required evidence labels for AC-2(13) decisions.
- [ ] Connect the case system to the organisation’s identity provider (IdP) to identify the affected users and list any linked accounts.
- [ ] Set up an automated process to disable an identity provider (IdP) account by turning off the account and cancelling any active sessions or access tokens, with a strict 24-hour service-level agreement (SLA) from the time the issue is identified.
- [ ] Add automatic removal of access for integrated applications, including SCIM deprovisioning and/or removal from federation groups, and block access using conditional access controls
- [ ] Store audit-ready records that link, for each disablement event, the time it was discovered, the evidence labels, the identity of the person who approved it, and the identity provider (IdP) audit log references.
- [ ] Run tabletop exercises and technical checks to confirm that account disablement happens within 24 hours, and that any exceptions must be approved by an authorised official.


---

### AC-3 — Access Enforcement (Control)

This requirement is about making sure that people and automated tasks can only access the correct information and systems, and only in the specific ways that have been formally approved. Without this, unauthorised access could happen, sensitive data could be viewed or changed by the wrong people, and mistakes or unauthorised changes could go unnoticed—leading to real financial, legal, and reputational harm.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set clear rules for who can access what, document how access is approved, granted, reviewed, and changed, and configure systems so these rules are enforced at the main system level and, where needed, within specific applications or services. The organisation must keep an up-to-date list of approved permissions, grant access using only those approved permissions, block anything outside the rules, and record access enforcement activity so it can be checked later.

Responsibilities must be assigned, and the approach must be included in security and privacy planning where applicable.

##### Enforce approved access via IdP-driven RBAC and app authorisation checks

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the authoritative authorisations catalogue schema (roles/privileges → resources → allowed actions) including exception model (owner, expiry, justification) and mapping rules to IdP claims | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement IdP integration for server-side RBAC/ABAC (validate tokens/claims, deny-by-default when required claims/roles are absent, support service accounts) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 64h | — |
| Build/implement application/service enforcement points for all sensitive functions (UI routes, API endpoints, background jobs, admin actions) with pre-authorisation checks before data access/business actions | Software Lead | Business Unit | 72h | — |
| Develop provisioning automation to derive role/group assignments strictly from the approved authorisations catalogue (SCIM or equivalent), including controlled time-bound exceptions and removal on de-provisioning | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £12,000 |
| Configure audit logging for authorisation outcomes and provisioning/role-change events (success/failure decisions, denied actions, assignment changes) with correlation IDs and structured fields | Security Engineer | Department | 40h | — |
| Integrate audit logs with SIEM (forwarding, indexing, retention alignment, dashboards/alerts for repeated denials and provisioning anomalies) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Create environment evidence pack and run enforcement test suite across test/stage/prod (unauthorised 403/denied verification, authorised least-privilege verification, evidence linking catalogue ↔ IdP mappings ↔ enforcement config) | Quality Assurance Lead | Business Unit | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 328h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £18,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and get approval for an official authorisations catalogue that links job roles and permissions to the relevant application resources and the actions each role is allowed to take.
- [ ] Set up the organisation’s identity provider (IdP) to send the required role-based access control (RBAC) and attribute-based access control (ABAC) permissions for the application, and link the IdP groups and roles to the approved authorisations catalogue.
- [ ] Set up automated user onboarding and offboarding (for example, system for cross-domain identity management (SCIM)) so that access to applications is granted only when users are assigned to approved roles or groups.
- [ ] Set up server-side authorisation checks for every sensitive user interface (UI), application programming interface (API), background job, and administrative function, using a “deny by default” approach.
- [ ] Turn on audit logs for authorisation decisions and for any provisioning or role changes, and send the logs to security information and event management (SIEM) with the required retention period.
- [ ] Run tests in each environment using both authorised and unauthorised access to prove that access is denied when it is outside the approved policy—for example, returning “HTTP 403” and blocking business actions.


---

#### AC-3.2 — Dual Authorization (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure that important, high-risk changes are never carried out by just one person working alone. Any privileged action or other step that changes who can access systems, changes security settings, or makes administrative changes to Secret/Confidential information must be approved first and then carried out by two different authorised people.

Without this “two-person” approach, a single insider, or a compromised account, could quietly change permissions or security settings and lead to unauthorised access, data exposure, or other serious harm.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define and document which specific commands and actions require two approvals, keep an up-to-date list of them, and state which people are allowed to give those approvals. The system and its procedures must prevent the change from running unless two separate authorised approvals are recorded before it happens, and must keep evidence showing who approved what and when.

The organisation should also consider how to reduce the risk of collusion and how to handle urgent situations where immediate action may be needed.

##### Two-person approval gate for privileged access/security changes

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Build authoritative in-scope privileged action catalogue (action identifier, category mapping, target environments, required approval types, emergency classification) and publish version-controlled governance documentation | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define and implement authorised approver roles/groups and identity separation rules (no same person twice; approver eligibility per action category; pairing/rotation constraints) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Design and implement two-person approval workflow integration with the execution/change path (ITSM workflow or automated approval service), including request binding to action identifier + parameters | Project Manager | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Implement execution gate in the privileged execution mechanism (block unless two distinct authorised approvals exist; verify request/action match; enforce “approved-before-execution” semantics) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Develop audit evidence model and tamper-evident logging pipeline (store initiator + both approvers + timestamps + parameters + execution result; forward to SIEM; ensure queryability) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £12,000 |
| Create emergency/safety exception process (if required): workflow, constraints, post-incident retrospective dual-approval evidence requirements, and audit reporting | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Execute end-to-end testing and control validation (unit/integration tests; negative tests for single approval/same approver/mismatched parameters; evidence review; SOC/SIEM validation) and produce acceptance sign-off pack | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 248h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £12,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep an up-to-date, authoritative list of the privileged commands and actions that are in scope, mapped to access control, security settings, and the administration of Secrets and Confidential information.
- [ ] Set up authorised approver roles and groups in the organisation’s identity system, and make sure approvers are different people (or groups) from the people who submit the requests.
- [ ] Set up the change and approval process so that it needs two approvals from two different authorised people, with a rule that the same person cannot approve twice.
- [ ] Use the privileged execution mechanism (pipeline, administration application programming interface (API), or infrastructure as code (IaC) runner) to check the workflow status and confirm the approved action identifiers before running.
- [ ] Set up tamper-evident records of who started the request, both approvers, the date and time, the approved settings, and the result of the execution, and send these records to the security information and event management (SIEM) system.
- [ ] Add measures to reduce the risk of collusion (for example, rules that limit how and when people or accounts are paired or rotated), and document the process for any emergency or safety exceptions, including a review after any incident.


---

#### AC-3.3 — Mandatory Access Control (Enhancement)

This requirement is about preventing misuse of information after someone (or an automated service) has access. It does this by enforcing clear, strict rules on **who** can receive the information and **what** they can do with it. Without these controls, confidential material could be copied or shared into more sensitive areas, leaked to unauthorised colleagues, or used to quietly increase someone’s permissions. It could also be used to change how information is labelled, or even to change the rules that control access—creating a serious risk of data breaches and improper access.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set a clear confidentiality policy that states:

- information cannot be passed to anyone or anything with a lower security level (**no write up and no read down**);
- access privileges cannot be passed on;
- security labels cannot be changed;
- new or changed items cannot be given new labels; and
- the access rules cannot be altered.

The system must apply these rules consistently to all covered users, service accounts, and trusted processes, and to all covered resources labelled **Confidential** or **Secret**. Only explicitly approved trusted identities may be allowed the limited exceptions for reading, writing, and executing that are defined in the policy.

##### Enforce Bell-LaPadula MAC with non-bypass reference monitor

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

| Design and implement the non-bypassable reference monitor boundary (OS/kernel/managed platform mediation point) and document all mediated access paths (UI, API, batch, background jobs, admin tooling) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement label-aware enforcement in the data access layer (label propagation rules, mandatory decisioning on read/open and write/modify operations, deny-by-default for covered Confidential/Secret objects) | Software Lead | Department | 72h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 376h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £8,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Choose and standardise a mandatory access control (MAC) enforcement boundary (for example, an operating system or kernel MAC framework, or an equivalent trusted enforcement layer) for all covered computing environments.
- [ ] Define how the Bell–LaPadula model links a user’s security level (subject security context) to the levels they can access, and how it labels information (objects) as **Confidential** or **Secret**, then implement this as a version-controlled “policy as code” programme.
- [ ] Apply system-controlled labels to all covered items (files, records, and messages) so users cannot set or change labels on newly created or modified items.
- [ ] Set enforcement rules to block “no-read-down” and “no-write-up” access across every way users or systems can access data, including the user interface, application programming interface (API), batch jobs, and administrative tools.
- [ ] Set up separate security permissions for only explicitly authorised trusted processes, and limit what they are allowed to do (and which types of objects they can access) to the minimum needed.
- [ ] Strengthen the policy and label management controls so only the trusted policy-management component can change mandatory access control (MAC) rules and labels, with audit logging enabled.
- [ ] Put label-aware export and integration controls in place at system boundaries so that any mandatory rules stay effective even when data leaves the system’s control.


---

#### AC-3.4 — Discretionary Access Control (Enhancement)

This requirement is about preventing people from quietly sharing sensitive information or changing access permissions in ways that put it at the wrong level of importance. Without it, someone who is authorised to access a document or part of a system could share it with others, transfer their access rights, or change security settings so that higher-importance information reaches the wrong audience, or so that access rules are weakened.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must define, document, and follow a clear discretionary access policy. This policy must allow authorised users to share information, grant their privileges, change security settings, set security options for new or updated items, and adjust access rules only when both the sender and the receiver (or the target part of the system) are authorised at the same impact and classification level.

The organisation must apply this policy consistently to all relevant users and all relevant system resources, configure the systems so they enforce it, and keep records showing when the system allowed or blocked these actions.

##### Enforce same-level discretionary sharing and privilege/attribute changes

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define discretionary access control level model (impactLevel/classificationLevel) and authoritative covered-set mapping for subjects/objects/system components | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Design PDP policy-as-code for discretionary actions (share/delegate/grant privilege/change attributes/change ACL/rule changes) including same-level evaluation logic and consistent deny responses | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement PDP integration and enforcement middleware at all discretionary workflow entry points (UI/API/service endpoints) with pre-commit checks for direct and indirect transfer mechanisms | Software Lead | Business Unit | 120h | — |
| Implement step-up/reauthentication workflow for privilege/attribute/rule changes and re-run same-level PDP check after step-up | Cyber Security Lead | Business Unit | 48h | — |
| Standardise error handling and response mapping to ensure cross-level denials do not leak sensitive details; add contract tests for each action type | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 32h | — |
| Implement audit evidence generation for allow/deny decisions (acting/target identifiers, evaluated levels, action type, policy rule identifier, correlation IDs) and ensure SIEM/observability ingestion | Operations Lead | Department | 40h | £8,000 |
| Create test plan and execute validation (unit/integration tests, negative cross-level cases, regression across environments) and produce audit-ready implementation evidence pack | Project Manager | Enterprise | 48h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 384h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £8,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and document the specific subjects and objects that are covered for AC-3(4) enforcement, using the `impactLevel` and `classificationLevel` attributes.
- [ ] Set up a decision point that checks whether a user has the same level of permission for each discretionary action type, including: sharing, delegating, granting, changing attributes, choosing attributes, and changing access-control rules.
- [ ] Add the “PDP check” to every application endpoint or workflow that can handle data or change privileges, labels, or access control lists (ACLs), including indirect transfer methods.
- [ ] Set a default “deny” rule for any discretionary action where the person or role taking the action and the person or role being acted on do not match exactly.
- [ ] Add “step-up” authentication and re-check access rights for actions that change privileges, attributes, or rules, where this is supported by the enterprise identity provider (IdP).
- [ ] Enable audit logging of decisions to allow or deny access, including the person who made the decision, the target person or object, the type of action, the access levels that were checked, and the identifier of the policy rule used.


---

#### AC-3.5 — Security-relevant Information (Enhancement)

This requirement is about keeping the most sensitive “security settings” locked away from everyone except when the system is intentionally not operating normally. These security settings include permission lists, the rules that decide what network traffic is allowed or blocked, the configuration details for security services, and the information used to manage encryption keys. If unauthorised people could view or change these items during normal day-to-day operation, they could weaken protection, expose private information, or cause security safeguards to fail.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define which information is security-relevant, identify where it is stored, and block access by default using appropriate access permissions and safeguards. Access must be allowed only during secure, non-operational periods such as maintenance, start-up, troubleshooting, or shutdown, and only for authorised roles with a legitimate need.

The organisation must also keep records showing who attempted to access these items, when the attempts occurred, what was targeted, and whether access was allowed or denied. This approach must be included in the organisation’s system security planning and supporting documentation.

##### State-gated access to security-relevant config and key info

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Create authoritative inventory of security-relevant information (ACLs, firewall/router filtering rules, security service config parameters, cryptographic key management info) mapped to storage/management locations and resource identifiers | Security Architect | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Define state-gated access policy model (approved non-operable states, decision logic, default-deny for normal operation, least-privilege roles, JIT/time-bounded sessions, re-validation rules) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Design and implement enforcement integration: route all reads/exports of identified resources through the access gateway/PAM, removing or blocking direct/bypass paths (admin UIs/APIs/filesystem/automation endpoints) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Integrate access gateway with operational state source of truth (ITSM maintenance ticket status + host reachability/maintenance flags, or orchestration signals) and implement “deny unless confirmed approved state” checks at session start (and periodically where supported) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Configure PAM/session controls for authorised roles and actions (read-only where feasible, action-level authorisation for view/export, session timeouts, periodic state re-checks) | Privileged Access Management (PAM) Administrator | Enterprise | 40h | — |
