**Total Estimated Effort:** 312h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £6,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an inventory that lists every security-relevant information item—such as access control lists (ACLs), firewall and router filtering rules, security service configuration settings, and key management information—and shows where each one is stored and managed, including the system host where it resides.
- [ ] Set a “default deny” rule so that normal-operation privileged groups cannot directly access resources that contain security-relevant information.
- [ ] Set up “state-gated” access approval in the access gateway and privileged access management (PAM) so access is only granted after the target system is confirmed to be in an approved, secure state and is not currently running or operating.
- [ ] Integrate the privileged access management (PAM) policy into the information technology service management (ITSM) maintenance workflow, using signals from each host’s current state (online, offline, booting, troubleshooting, or shutting down) to provide clear, enforceable proof of that state.
- [ ] Limit system access to roles that have been explicitly authorised, using the minimum permissions needed, and use time-limited sessions that require re-checking the user’s status at the start of each session.
- [ ] Turn on and send audit records for every access attempt (allowed or blocked), including the user, the resource being accessed, the target system, the decision made, the date and time, and evidence showing why the system was not able to operate.


---

#### AC-3.7 — Role-based Access Control (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure people can only access and do what their job requires in the systems they use. It does this by linking access to clearly defined job roles, rather than granting permissions to individuals one by one. Without this, the wrong person could view or change sensitive information, or someone could take on a more powerful role without proper approval. This increases the risk of data misuse, mistakes, or unauthorised changes.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- define which users are covered and which parts of the system are protected
- create and document roles such as Information System Security Officer, Information System Owner, identity and access management (IAM) Administrator, Data Steward, System Administrator, and Helpdesk Analyst
- record what each role is allowed to do

Users must be assigned to these roles. Any role change must only be allowed after the person’s approved role assignment is verified using authorised human resources (HR) or contractor records.

The organisation must also:
- keep role and permission records up to date
- ensure the system enforces these rules for all covered users and functions
- keep audit records showing role changes and access decisions

Where relevant, this approach must be included in security and privacy planning.

##### Enforce RBAC roles and role assumption via approved HR/contractor records

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define RBAC authorisation model: covered subjects, covered objects/functions, and role-to-privilege mapping for ISSO/ISO/IAM Admin/Data Steward/System Admin/Helpdesk Analyst | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement central authorisation enforcement in IdP/authorisation service: create roles, map roles to application privileges, and remove/disable any ad-hoc per-user grants for covered functions | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £8,000 |
| Integrate HR/contractor authoritative source for role eligibility: build/validate data flow (API/export/workflow), define “approved and current” criteria, and implement provisioning gating for covered roles | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £12,000 |
| Implement role assumption workflow controls: enforce deny-by-default for assume/step-up actions when HR/contractor eligibility is absent/expired; record decision outcomes | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Update application access checks and admin/API authorisation: ensure all endpoints and admin consoles use role membership (not local flags), including least-privilege for workflow actions | Software Lead | Business Unit | 48h | — |
| Enable audit evidence and SIEM-ready logging: role assignment/provisioning events, role assumption attempts (allowed/denied), and access denials; configure retention and correlation identifiers | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £6,000 |
| Execute test, validation, and operational readiness: unit/integration tests, negative tests (expired/absent HR record), runbook updates, and go-live verification | Quality Assurance Lead | Business Unit | 32h | — |
| Establish periodic review control: automated reconciliation job/reporting between HR/contractor records and IdP role membership; define review cadence and exception handling | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | £4,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 280h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £30,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define which people (users) are allowed to take on specific roles, and which system parts (application resources and actions) those roles can access for this system.
- [ ] Set up role-based access control (RBAC) roles—information system security officer (ISSO), information security officer (ISO), identity and access management (IAM) administrator, data steward, system administrator, and helpdesk analyst—and assign a role-to-permission mapping for every covered object or function.
- [ ] Use the approved human resources (HR) and contractor records as the official source for who is eligible for each role, and only add someone to a role when an approved record exists.
- [ ] Configure the application, administration consoles, and application programming interfaces (APIs) to allow requests only when the user is in the correct role under role-based access control (RBAC) and has the matching permissions (deny by default).
- [ ] Set up role-assumption and step-up controls so that “assume-role” is allowed only when the user’s approved job role (from their human resources record or contractor approval) is up to date.
- [ ] Enable and centralise audit logs for role set-up, role use, and access denials. Keep these logs for audit purposes.
- [ ] Carry out an initial and regular check to confirm that the people listed in the authorisation system match the latest approved records from Human Resources (HR) and contractor documentation.


---

#### AC-3.8 — Revocation of Access Authorizations (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that when someone’s access rights should change, the system removes their access to anything they should no longer be able to reach. Without this, a person or an automated task could keep access for too long after their status changes, or after a file, folder, or record is reclassified. This creates a real risk of unauthorised viewing, changing, or misuse.  

To meet this expectation, the organisation must define and document clear rules for removing access whenever either a person’s or a resource’s security details are changed. If the change is a security-label change, access must be removed immediately. Otherwise, access must be removed at the earlier of: the next time the resource is opened, or the next time the person tries to access it.  

The organisation must configure its systems to enforce these timing rules, ensure the relevant staff understand their responsibilities, and keep records showing that access was removed at the correct time, with enough detail to confirm whether it was immediate or delayed.

##### Immediate revocation on security-label change; event-triggered otherwise

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Design the attribute-change classification mechanism (label vs non-label) and define the deterministic tagging rules in the authorisation data model (incl. schema changes and update semantics) | System Design Authority | Department | 24h | — |
| Implement immediate revocation path for security-label changes: IdP/session/token invalidation strategy and application-side authorisation state invalidation (incl. cache purge + hard re-check) | IAM/authorisation architect | Enterprise | 40h | £8,000 |
| Implement event-triggered revocation enforcement for non-label attribute changes at the earliest boundary (object-open and subject access attempt): refactor authorisation decision calls to occur at those boundaries and remove reliance on long-lived entitlements | Software Lead | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Implement auditability and evidence capture: attribute-change event logging, enforcement decision logging with AC-3(8) timing reason codes, and boundary-trigger correlation identifiers (object-open vs subject access attempt) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Create automated tests and timing verification harness: integration/unit tests that simulate attribute changes and assert denial timing (immediate for label changes; earliest boundary for non-label changes) with audit evidence assertions | Quality Assurance Lead | Business Unit | 40h | £3,000 |
| Operationalise and document the solution: runbooks for classification logic ownership, revocation trigger monitoring, log retention expectations, and change-management guidance for future attribute taxonomy updates | Operations Lead | Department | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 216h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £11,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and implement a way to classify every change to a subject or object, and tag each update as either a security label change or a non-label change.
- [ ] Work with the organisation’s identity provider (IdP) and session management system so that, when a security label changes, any affected user sessions and access tokens are cancelled immediately.
- [ ] Ensure the application checks whether a user is authorised both when an object is first opened and again at the start of any protected operation whenever changes are made to non-label attributes.
- [ ] Remove or skip any saved authorisation or entitlement information so that label-change cancellations take effect immediately, without waiting for the next access check boundary.
- [ ] Set up audit logs for any changes to user attributes and for the enforcement decisions that follow. Include the date and time of each event, and record a reason code showing whether the action was taken immediately or at the earliest boundary for revocation.
- [ ] Set up automated tests that change security settings and check how quickly access is blocked for both cases: (1) when the label changes immediately, and (2) when the label does not change, using the earliest allowed timing boundary.


---

#### AC-3.9 — Controlled Release (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure information leaves your organisation only when the outside recipient can be trusted to protect it properly. Without this, sensitive details could be sent to the wrong place, handled in a weaker way than you expect, or exposed to unauthorised people—leading to legal, financial, and reputational harm.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must first decide which external systems or contractor-controlled devices are allowed to receive information. It must then share information only if the recipient provides security and privacy protections that are equivalent and suitable for their approval status and for how they will handle the data.

Before sending, the organisation must check that the recipient is appropriate using:
- contractual commitments,
- periodic independent evidence (such as inspection or test results), and
- a documented match between the information’s protection needs and the recipient’s safeguards.

The organisation must keep records of the recipient’s safeguards, the checks carried out, and the supporting agreements and assessment results.

##### Attribute-mapped controlled release gate for external recipients

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

| Implement recipient registry service/data store (CRUD, versioning, approval workflow, audit logging) and integrate it with the outbound workflow for recipient eligibility checks | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £6,000 |
| Define attribute mapping model and equivalence/appropriateness rules (attribute set per outbound release type; mapping versioning; rule engine inputs; handling for “unknown/insufficient evidence”) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Build and integrate attribute mapping validation into the release gate (evaluate recipient-recorded controls vs mapped required attributes; produce pass/fail + denial reason codes) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 64h | £10,000 |
| Implement contractual assurance and periodic assessment evidence verification (evidence reference capture, expiry checks, retrieval links, and “current evidence” enforcement) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £8,000 |
| Develop exception workflow for blocked releases (risk acceptance/approval, required evidence capture, time-bound approvals, and audit trail) and integrate it with the gate decision outcomes | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement audit-ready evidence generation and reporting (per-decision log, stored references: recipient safeguards record, contractual reference, assessment evidence expiry, mapping version, decision outcome; export to SIEM/GRC reporting) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £5,000 |
| End-to-end testing, security testing, and rollout (test cases for allowed/blocked paths, performance impact, failure modes, and change management release to production) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 56h | £3,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 376h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £32,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and maintain an official register of approved recipients for external receiving systems and contractor-controlled devices.
- [ ] Define the attribute mapping model that converts each type of outgoing data release into the security and privacy attributes that are required.
- [ ] Record the contract assurance reference and the expiry date for each eligible recipient and each type of data.
- [ ] Set up an outbound release checkpoint in the application, application programming interface (API), and export process to confirm that each item is eligible, meets contractual assurance requirements, is up to date based on scheduled reviews, and matches the required attribute mapping.
- [ ] Set up an exception process for releases that are blocked, so they can only proceed with documented approval and recorded supporting evidence.
- [ ] For every release decision, turn on audit logging and keep the supporting evidence. This includes recording the version, linking to the evidence used, and documenting the outcome of each approval gate.


---

#### AC-3.10 — Audited Override of Access Control Mechanisms (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that emergency access changes are allowed only when they are genuinely needed, and that they are properly authorised and recorded. Without this, staff could bypass the normal access rules during a crisis by mistake or for convenience, which could expose sensitive information or allow the wrong people into systems. This could seriously harm people or prevent the organisation from carrying out critical work.

The organisation must clearly set out the only situations where an override is allowed:
- when there is a threat to human life, or
- when it is needed to prevent the loss of mission-critical capability during an active incident or declared emergency.

Any override must be approved before it happens by both the Information System Security Officer and the designated duty officer. Only they (or people explicitly authorised to act on their behalf) may carry out the override.

Every override must be recorded in the system’s audit records with enough detail to show what was changed, who was involved, and when. This ensures it can be reviewed afterwards.

##### Dual-approved break-glass access with immutable audit trail

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define “Emergency Override Eligibility” policy artefact (conditions, required request fields, incident status rules, justification mapping) and publish for governance sign-off | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Design dual-approval break-glass workflow (ISSO + designated duty officer), including separation-of-duties controls and request/approval state machine | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement technical eligibility gate (incident reference validation, status enforcement, justification category validation) integrated with enterprise incident/ticket system | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Configure execution authority and scoped, time-bounded elevation (resource/policy scoping, automatic expiry, extension requires re-approval) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement immutable/tamper-evident audit event generation for every override execution (required fields, integrity controls, append-only/WORM strategy) and integrate with SIEM/logging pipeline | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £25,000 |
| Develop automated audit evidence retrieval package (query templates, retention mapping to AU-2/AU-12, and audit-ready export format) for later review | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Run end-to-end testing and tabletop exercises (positive/negative cases, single-approver prevention, expiry/extension, audit completeness) and produce release readiness evidence | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 200h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £25,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish the emergency override eligibility rules for the two permitted conditions, including the required proof of incident status.
- [ ] Set up a “break-glass” process in the organisation’s identity and access management (IAM) and privileged access layer. This process must require separate, independent approvals from the information system security officer (ISSO) and the designated duty officer.
- [ ] Set up the system so that only the incident security system officer (ISSO) or the duty officer (or explicitly approved delegates acting under their control) can carry out the override.
- [ ] Set up override permissions that are limited to a specific scope and time period, automatically expire, and require re-approval if an extension is needed.
- [ ] Integrate the override action with central logging to produce tamper-evident audit records. These records must include the approval details, the person who carried out the override, the affected resources or policy identifiers, the date and time, and the related incident reference.
- [ ] Update the system access control procedures and the system security documentation to reference the override process, the conditions for using it, the roles responsible, and the audit evidence that must be kept.


---

#### AC-3.11 — Restrict Access to Specific Information Types (Enhancement)

This expectation is about protecting the most sensitive parts of your systems so that only the right people can access them. This specifically includes data storage areas that hold cryptographic keys, login and authentication information, and selected system information. If these are not protected, unauthorised staff or attackers could steal the keys that protect your data, gain access to accounts by using login-related information, or view sensitive details about the system. This could lead to fraud, data theft, or a wider compromise of the system.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must:
- define which types of information are protected
- publish an access rule stating clearly that only authorised personnel may access those storage areas
- create clear written steps for how access is granted, checked, and blocked

The system must be designed and configured to enforce these restrictions through how permissions are set. The approach must be recorded in the system design and security plan. Finally, the organisation must keep audit records as evidence that access attempts are logged and that only authorised access is permitted.

##### Repository access rules for protected information types

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Create authoritative protected-repository scope mapping in the data/asset catalogue (repository inventory, object boundaries, and mapping to ac-03.11_odp information types) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define standard repository/type-level authorisation patterns per platform (DB schema/table/view, object storage prefix, secret path, config store path) including deny-by-default and least-privilege rules | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement repository/type-level permissions for protected repositories (create/adjust dedicated DB roles, storage bucket/prefix policies, secret read policies; remove any broad “read all” grants) | Infrastructure Lead | Department | 56h | — |
| Integrate protected-repository access with enterprise identity (group/role provisioning, step-up requirements for privileged roles, service account handling) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Enable and validate audit logging for protected repository access attempts (allowed and denied), configure retention, and confirm SIEM ingestion and alerting | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Produce policy-as-code/config exports and audit evidence pack (repository/type rules, enforcement configuration, and audit log references) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Establish operational governance: access approval workflow, periodic review cadence, and exception handling process for protected repository/type access | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 232h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep up to date an official inventory that links each repository to the protected information types defined in **ac-03.11_odp**.
- [ ] Set up repository and type-level permissions using a deny-by-default approach, including database roles, schema and table or view permissions, object prefix rules, and secret path rules.
- [ ] Limit access to protected repositories to only explicitly authorised user groups or roles that are connected to the organisation’s enterprise identity provider.
- [ ] Turn on audit logging for every attempt to access protected repositories, and make sure the system records and keeps the results (whether access was allowed or denied).
- [ ] Keep records of configuration evidence (either policy-as-code or platform configuration exports) that show the access rules are being enforced.
- [ ] Set up a process to approve access and to review it regularly for authorised roles and groups for each protected repository and type, including how to handle exceptions.


---

#### AC-3.12 — Assert and Enforce Application Access (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure every app only has the access it genuinely needs, and that it cannot quietly take additional access after it is installed. Without this, an app that looks harmless could still read or use sensitive information such as your contacts, location, camera, microphone, keyboard input, network details, phone functions, or other files. This could lead to privacy breaches, spying, or misuse of company information.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must require that, during installation, each application clearly states what access it needs for user contacts, global positioning systems, cameras, keyboards, microphones, networks, phones, and other files. The organisation must also be able to enforce those stated permissions so that any unauthorised access is blocked immediately after installation. Finally, any later changes to an installed app’s access must be paused until they are reviewed and approved before the new access is allowed.

##### Enforce install-time app permission profiles with update approval gates

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the approved permission profile schema and mapping rules for ac-03.12_odp categories (including version/platform handling, default-deny behaviour, and drift comparison logic) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Create/extend the authoritative app record in the enterprise app catalogue (ingest declared permissions from managed store/metadata, normalise to the schema, and establish ownership/approver assignments) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement endpoint/OS management enforcement for install-time permission profiles (managed deployment only; deny any category not in the approved profile; ensure no first-run bypass) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |

| Configure approval workflow and change control integration (ticket/workflow triggers, evidence capture, role-based approvals, and controlled rollout after approval) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement audit-ready logging and SIEM integration (store declared permissions, applied approved profile, enforcement outcomes, drift/blocked-update events; alerting and retention) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £12,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an official application catalogue entry for each app, version, and platform. In each entry, record the permission categories that are declared from the **ac-03.12_odp** set.
- [ ] For each application, define and keep an approved list of permissions that sets out which categories of access are allowed.
- [ ] Set up managed deployment (MDM) and the enterprise app store so that, when an app is installed, the device’s operating system and endpoint permissions are enforced automatically, and any app categories that are not included in the approved profile are blocked.
- [ ] Set up an automated control that checks for changes in permissions (“permission drift”) and stops a release from being deployed or used effectively until the required approval is completed.
- [ ] Set up an approval process for permission and access changes after installation, and make sure policy updates are only made after the approval is granted.
- [ ] Turn on audit logs for declared permissions, approved profiles, enforcement results, and approval decisions. Send alerts about permission changes (permission drift) and enforcement denials to security information and event management (SIEM).


---

#### AC-3.13 — Attribute-based Access Control (Enhancement)

This expectation is about ensuring people can access only the correct systems and files when their job role and access rights genuinely match what they are allowed to use, and only from the correct location and within the approved times. Without this, someone could view or change sensitive information they are not authorised to access, or access it from an unauthorised place or outside approved working hours. This increases the risk of data leaks, fraud, or disruption.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define which users and which resources are covered. It must create and maintain access rules that check: job function, identity confidence level, security clearance level (Secret or Confidential), system role, the resource’s classification, and the on-premises location and approved time window. Systems must then be configured so access is granted only when all these details match the rules, and denied when they do not.

The organisation must also document how access is enforced, record access decisions for later review, and assign responsibility to the right staff. It must keep evidence showing that the settings are in place and working as intended.

##### Policy-driven ABAC enforcement using IdP attributes and resource metadata

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define ABAC scope and attribute model (subjects/objects/actions), including required attribute lists and matching semantics (all-match allow, otherwise deny) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Produce resource metadata approach for object attributes (resource classification) including authoritative source mapping and determination logic | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Define authoritative attribute sources and claim/attribute contracts (HR job function, IdP assurance level, clearance, system role) and document redaction rules for audit logs | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement ABAC policy-as-code (policy DSL/engine) with environment attributes (on-prem/egress/ posture) and server-side time window enforcement | Software Lead | Enterprise | 56h | £12,000 |
| Integrate central enforcement point with application/API (UI/API/admin tiers) ensuring consistent allow/deny decisions for all defined object/action pairs | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £8,000 |
| Implement decision audit logging to SIEM (allow/deny for every request) including attribute identifiers/values used, correlation IDs, and sensitive-value redaction | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £3,000 |
| Create evidence pack and deployment controls: version-controlled repositories, CI/CD change management, test evidence (unit/integration), and system security documentation updates | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 28h | — |
| Run end-to-end validation and operational readiness (test cases for mismatched attributes, time window failures, and privileged/admin paths) with SOC/SecOps monitoring sign-off | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| **Total Estimated Effort** |  |  | **236h** |  |
| **Total Estimated Cost** |  |  |  | **£23,000** |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an attribute-based access control (ABAC) scope inventory that maps defined users or accounts to defined resources and actions, including each resource’s resource classification attribute.
- [ ] Set up the identity provider (IdP) and upstream systems so they send the job role, identity assurance level, and security clearance as official, trusted information to the point where access decisions are enforced.
- [ ] Set up server-side checks that determine the on-premises location and whether requests fall within approved time windows (for example, confirming an approved egress/zero trust network access posture and enforcing the time limits on the server).
- [ ] Develop access control rules in code that check the person’s job function, assurance level, security clearance, system role, the classification of the resource, and the operating environment. The rules must then produce a clear “allow” or “deny” decision.
- [ ] Set up a central authorisation control point (an application programming interface (API) gateway or authorisation service) so that every request to the defined objects and actions is checked against the attribute-based access control (ABAC) policy.
- [ ] Enable audit logging for every attribute-based access control (ABAC) decision to allow or deny access. Record the user (subject), the resource (object), the operation (action), and the reason for the decision (decision basis). Send these logs to the security information and event management (SIEM) system and keep them for the required retention period.


---

#### AC-3.14 — Individual Access (Enhancement)

This requirement is about helping people safely check what personal information an organisation holds about them and why it is used. Without this, someone may not realise their records are inaccurate, their information could be seen by the wrong person, or their information could be used and shared without clear transparency.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must provide:
- a secure online (web-based) way to request access, and  
- a signed-in area where individuals can view their own records held in the organisation’s official systems.

This viewing area must show the specific items of information held, the reasons the organisation processes it, and any history of sharing or transfers where this applies.

The organisation must also:
- set clear rules and written procedures for how access decisions are checked and approved,
- involve the correct staff who are responsible for enforcing access, and
- get legal advice where there may be limits.

Finally, the organisation must keep the necessary documentation and records of access activity, so that each request and viewing session can be traced to the correct person.

- [ ] Set up the web-based subject access request (SAR) portal process—submission, identity checks, approval decision, fulfilment, and completion—using a request reference.
- [ ] Connect the portal and viewing interface to the organisation’s identity provider and require users to be signed in for every request to view or export information.
- [ ] Set up server-side access checks and data retrieval so that system-of-record queries only return information for the authenticated user’s identifier.
- [ ] Implement a privacy view model that puts records into a consistent format, so data fields, the reasons for processing, and the history of data transfers or disclosures can be displayed clearly.
- [ ] Enable audit logs for suspicious activity report (SAR) submissions, identity checks, authorisation decisions, record lookups, and any actions to view, export, or download information.
- [ ] Document and put in place access limits and any approved exceptions, using a policy-based process with privacy and legal approval decision points.


---

#### AC-3.15 — Discretionary and Mandatory Access Control (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure every person and every system resource can only be accessed in the right way, for the right reasons, every time. It helps prevent a serious breach where someone with lower clearance, or a user account that has been misused, could read or change more sensitive information than they are allowed to. It also helps prevent one compromised account being used to spread access across the whole system.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must apply two layers of access checks to the specific in-scope users and resources it has identified. First, it must use fixed security levels (such as Confidential and Secret) so that a user can only access information at their clearance level or below. Second, it must apply permission rules based on job roles, and on file, service, and network permissions, using the principle of least privilege.

The organisation must ensure these rules are applied consistently and that all access decisions are recorded so they can be reviewed.

##### Enforce MAC + DAC together via PDP/PEP with labelled data and RBAC/ACL

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define MAC model (security labels, clearance levels, attribute mapping rules, label inheritance/override rules) and publish as policy-as-code schema | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define DAC model (RBAC roles/groups, action taxonomy, object/endpoint ACL structure, least-privilege baseline and separation of duties rules) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 28h | — |
| Implement PDP/PEP authorisation pattern at the mediation point(s) (API gateway/authorisation service/middleware) with explicit combined semantics (deny if MAC denies OR DAC denies) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £18,000 |
| Integrate PDP with identity provider for subject clearance claims and with data/object metadata for object labels (including service accounts/workload identities) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £6,000 |
| Implement object labelling and binding at creation/update time (including backfill for existing objects, validation, and enforcement to prevent unlabelled objects) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement auditable decision records (MAC result, DAC result, final decision, policy version, correlation IDs) and integrate with SIEM/logging retention requirements | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £4,000 |
| Build test suite and evidence pack (unit/integration tests for MAC-first + DAC-second evaluation, regression tests for bypass-path removal, and audit-ready documentation) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 36h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 264h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £28,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the mandatory access control (MAC) label set and the subject clearance levels, including how identity attributes are mapped to clearance levels.
- [ ] Define role-based access control (RBAC) roles and groups, and set action-specific access control lists (ACLs) for each in-scope object type and endpoint.
- [ ] Set up object classification so that every in-scope object is created or updated with a security label.
- [ ] Set up a single authorisation process that checks both mandatory access control (MAC) and discretionary access control (DAC), and applies “deny takes priority” rules.
- [ ] Remove or disable any ways to bypass authorisation, such as direct access to data or internal calls that do not pass on the identity of the user or system making the request.
- [ ] Set up structured audit records for every access attempt, including the mandatory access control (MAC) result, the discretionary access control (DAC) result, the final access decision, and the version of the access policy.
- [ ] Store mandatory access control (MAC) and discretionary access control (DAC) rules as code in version control, and deploy them through a reviewed, controlled release process.


---

### AC-4 — Information Flow Enforcement (Control)

This requirement is about making sure information only goes to the places it is supposed to, both within your systems and between connected systems, following the organisation’s approved rules. Without this, sensitive or restricted information could be sent to the wrong place, appear to come from inside the organisation when it does not, or be leaked to the public internet without protection, including export-controlled data. It could also break the rules of another business area or partner system, or allow unauthorised changes to how information is handled.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must enforce its approved cross-domain information-flow rules. This includes checking that the sender is allowed to send, directing traffic based on the information’s assigned handling labels, and applying extra controls for export-controlled material. The organisation must apply these rules to both normal information and system “control” traffic, such as routing and name lookups. It must block traffic that tries to pretend it is internal, require web requests to go through the organisation’s internal web proxy, limit transfers between organisations to agreed structures and content, and only allow such transfers when an agreement specifies that enforcement is required.

The organisation must also use trusted enforcement controls at boundary points, check permissions before accepting incoming information, support one-way flows and any label changes that are required, and keep audit records showing what was allowed or blocked.

##### Label-aware flow enforcement at cross-domain boundaries

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the authoritative information-flow policy model (policy-as-code) for ac-04_odp: allowed source→destination pairs, protocol/port rules, required handling labels, permit/deny/route actions, export-controlled handling, and web-proxy-only egress rules | Security Architecture Lead | Enterprise | 80h | — |
| Implement label-aware boundary enforcement design for all cross-domain boundary types (firewall/proxy/API gateway/service-mesh ingress/egress/ZTNA broker/DNS enforcement resolvers), including anti-bypass controls and boundary traversal guarantees | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Build/configure enforcement components to perform label-based routing and write-permission checks for inbound inter-domain flows (including session handling label validation and destination acceptance rules) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 120h | £25,000 |
| Implement export-controlled and web-proxy restrictions in the enforcement path (block cleartext Internet egress for export-controlled labels; restrict HTTP(S) to internal web proxy; align proxy routing to the same label model) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 96h | £10,000 |
| Extend enforcement to control-plane traffic (DNS and routing-adjacent/management-adjacent services as applicable): enforce approved resolvers, domain→resolver flows, and ensure control-plane cannot bypass data-plane policy | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 64h | £6,000 |
| Implement trusted regrading/label reassignment at designated enforcement points only, with before/after label decision recording and auditability | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £8,000 |
| Generate audit evidence and SIEM integration: log policy decision outcomes (permit/deny/route), matched rule identifiers, source/destination, labels, and write-permission verification results; create test evidence pack for representative cases (spoofed-internal blocking, disallowed transfers) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Execute end-to-end testing and go-live readiness: boundary traversal verification, bypass attempts, regression tests across environments (prod/test/DR), and operational runbook updates (monitoring, alerting, incident handling) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 64h | £3,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 624h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £52,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and get approval for the policy-as-code information flow model—covering where data comes from and goes to, what communication methods are used, how items are labelled, and what actions are taken (permit, deny, or route)—in line with **ac-04_odp**.
- [ ] Identify all connections between different security domains, and ensure that all traffic between them (including Domain Name System (DNS) and control-plane traffic) passes through the designated enforcement points.
- [ ] Set up boundary enforcement to check write permissions and use label-based routing for incoming and outgoing network traffic.
- [ ] Apply export-controlled handling when data leaves the system: by default, block unencrypted transmission to the public internet, and allow only pre-approved encrypted routes and destinations.
- [ ] Limit web traffic so that outgoing web requests using Hypertext Transfer Protocol Secure (HTTPS) or Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP) are only allowed through the internal web proxy, and ensure the proxy rules are applied based on the label model.
- [ ] Only apply trusted regrading or label reassignment at the agreed enforcement points, and record the label decision before and after the change.
- [ ] Set up security information and event management (SIEM) logging to record the results of policy decisions, including the rule identifier, labels, source and destination details, and whether access was permitted or denied. Confirm it works correctly using test cases.


---

#### AC-4.1 — Object Security and Privacy Attributes (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure sensitive information is only sent to the right places, and that personal data is shared only in line with the rules that apply. Without it, confidential information could be sent by mistake or on purpose to the wrong team, system, or country. Personal information could also be combined or released in ways that break privacy obligations, leading to financial loss, legal risk, and harm to people.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must define the labels it will use for both sensitivity and privacy. This includes whether data is **Secret** or **Top Secret**, whether it is limited to certain countries, and what type of personal data it contains, how it is used, and how sharing is restricted.

The organisation must then ensure that every piece of information, every sending device or service, and every receiving device or service is marked with these labels. It must keep an up-to-date record of the labels and where they apply, and apply a clear rule: transfers are allowed only when both the sensitivity and privacy sharing rules permit them. If not, the transfer must be blocked and an alert raised. The organisation must also record the decision in audit records and document the approach in its system security and privacy plans.

##### Enforce security+privacy attributes for allow/deny flow decisions

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define organisation security+privacy attribute model (schemas, allowed values, authoritative sources) and map to AC-4(1) / ac-04.01_odp.09 decision basis | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define allow/deny decision rule engine logic (security pass AND privacy pass; explicit deny precedence; default-deny for unknown/missing labels) and produce policy specification document | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement attribute tagging and label propagation for information/source/destination objects (including ingestion/transform pipelines and derived-message/record labelling) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Build/extend attribute-aware Policy Decision Point (PDP) service/API to evaluate source+destination+information attributes and return allow/deny + reason category (security vs privacy) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Integrate PDP with the flow enforcement point (gateway/secure proxy/segmentation/ZTNA/API mediation) and ensure enforcement is authoritative (deny-by-default, allow only on dual pass) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £25,000 |
| Implement deny-and-alert audit evidence generation (event schema, correlation IDs, SIEM integration, retention alignment, dashboards/alerts for denied flows) | SOC / SIEM engineer | Enterprise | 32h | £10,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 248h

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set the official security and privacy data standards (schemas) and the rule for deciding access: access is allowed only when both security permits access and privacy sharing permits access.
- [ ] Add labels (tagging) to information objects, source objects, and destination objects so each one includes the required security and privacy attributes.
- [ ] Set up or configure a policy decision point (PDP) that checks the source, destination, and information details against the organisation’s defined rules for controlling how information is allowed to flow.
- [ ] Connect the policy decision point (PDP) to the system’s traffic control point so that each attempted data flow is allowed or blocked based on the PDP’s allow/deny decision.
- [ ] Set up handling for denied traffic so that the traffic is blocked and alerts and audit records are generated, including the relevant attribute values and the category of the denial reason.
- [ ] Set up automated tests that cover key permitted and blocked scenarios (for example, Secret to Secret is allowed, Top Secret to Secret is blocked, and restricted personal data (PII) sharing is blocked) and run these tests automatically as part of continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD).

#### AC-4.2 — Processing Domains (Enhancement)

This requirement is about keeping information in the right “separate areas” within your systems, and only allowing it to move where the rules permit. Without this, sensitive data could be copied, leaked, or used in the wrong place, or one part of a system could quietly send information to another part that should not receive it. This could lead to fraud, privacy breaches, or regulatory problems.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set up protected, controlled processing areas and define clear rules for which types of information are allowed to move between those areas, and to or from specific data items. This includes rules on which areas can communicate with each other and which processes may switch from one area to another. The system must then use these rules to decide what is allowed and what is blocked, with processes placed in the correct areas and information clearly labelled by type.

The organisation must document how this works, configure the system to enforce it, keep evidence through audit records, and assign responsibility to the relevant administrators and security staff.

- [ ] Set up workload or process-to-domain mapping so the enforcement point can identify the source domain during runtime.
- [ ] Require information-type labelling when data objects are created or received, and ensure those labels carry through any processing or transformations.
- [ ] Create a “policy as code” ruleset that allows or blocks data flows based on (source domain, destination domain or object, information type, and action) from ac-04.02_odp.
- [ ] Route all messages between different domains (events and callbacks) and all process or workflow changes through the policy decision point, and block any actions that are not permitted.
- [ ] Create structured audit records for every decision to allow or deny access, including the rule that was used and the correlation identifiers, and send them to the security information and event management (SIEM) and logging system.
- [ ] Create automated test cases for example “allowed” and “denied” situations, and require peer review and a controlled, change-managed release process for updates to the policy.

#### AC-4.3 — Dynamic Information Flow Control (Enhancement)

This requirement is about allowing information to be shared only in special, time-critical situations, and stopping it immediately when circumstances change. Without this, staff could accidentally or automatically share sensitive information at the wrong time, or while the organisation is facing an increased threat level. That would raise the risk of data leaks, fraud, or disruption to essential services.

The organisation must set clear rules for when “dynamic” information sharing is allowed, based on two live checks:
- First, the specific mission-critical conditions must be met.
- Second, the latest threat and risk assessment must confirm that sharing is permitted.

If either check fails, the system must block dynamic sharing and immediately alert the Security Operations Centre so they can respond.

The organisation must also:
- document how these decisions are made,
- configure the system to enforce the rules,
- keep records of every decision to allow or block sharing, including the reason,
- and include how this is implemented in system plans and design documentation.

##### Dynamic info-flow gate with mission and threat permit checks

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define machine-enforceable dynamic flow decision rule (permit/deny), including reason categories (`MISSION_CRITICAL_NOT_MET`, `RISK_NOT_PERMITTED`, `ADVERSE_EVENT_DETECTED`) and deny-by-default semantics | Security Architect | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design PDP/PEP runtime architecture and interfaces (flow request schema, mission state token format, threat/risk assessment version/ID contract, adverse-event input contract, policy versioning) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement PDP service (policy evaluation engine) with audit-ready decision output (allow/deny, reason category, mission state identifier, risk assessment version/ID, timestamps, policy version) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 80h | — |
| Implement PEP enforcement integration at connection/session establishment (gateway/micro-segmentation/API gateway hook) with revalidation strategy where supported | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Integrate “changing conditions” signals: mission state ingestion (signed/authenticated), latest threat/risk assessment retrieval/validation, and adverse-event detection feed from SIEM/SOAR | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £15,000 |

| Produce security architecture/design documentation and system security plan updates (policy logic, enforcement points, integration sources, change-control evidence) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 360h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £29,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the mission-critical condition states and assign each one an official, machine-readable mission state token.
- [ ] Set the rules for dynamic traffic to allow or block connections, using the latest threat and risk assessment results and clear, specific reason categories.
- [ ] Set up a policy enforcement point (PEP) and policy decision point (PDP) integration so that dynamic traffic requests are checked while they are happening, and are blocked by default if the checks do not pass.
- [ ] Add the latest mission status and threat or risk assessment information to the programme decision process (PDP), and track the assessment version or identification number so you can prove that the most up-to-date information was used.
- [ ] Set up security operations centre (SOC) alerts for blocked dynamic network flows, using a consistent message format that includes the reason category, relevant identifiers, the policy version, and the time and date stamps.
- [ ] Set up tamper-resistant, append-only audit logs for every allow or deny decision, including the information used to make the decision and the decision result.
- [ ] Update the system security plan and the architecture and design documents to explain where security controls are applied, how decisions are made, and what evidence is used to prove compliance.


---

#### AC-4.4 — Flow Control of Encrypted Information (Enhancement)

This requirement is about preventing secret-looking messages from getting through your checks. If encrypted or encoded information can pass around your inspection process, harmful or sensitive material could be sent without being identified, categorised, or blocked according to your rules, creating real risk to the organisation.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must ensure that encrypted (and encoded) data is still inspected and checked against the correct data-type rules, rather than being able to bypass them. It must achieve this by using approved encrypted-traffic inspection gateways, configured so they only allow traffic to explicitly approved destinations. It must also block any encrypted traffic that would otherwise get around the checks, and it must end any communication attempts that try to do so.

The organisation must also alert the Security Operations Centre when blocks or session terminations occur, keep clear procedures and system design records, document the configuration settings, record events for later review, and include this approach in its security plan.

##### TLS inspection gateway to block encrypted bypass and terminate sessions

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Install approved Transport Layer Security (TLS) inspection gateways at agreed network choke points to inspect encrypted traffic.
- [ ] Set up gateway inspection rules to apply content inspection security filters and data type identifiers to decrypted Transport Layer Security (TLS) traffic.
- [ ] Create clear approved (allow-listed) destinations for the inspection gateway, and block all other destinations by default (default-deny).
- [ ] Put controls in place to stop attempts to bypass security using encrypted or encoded data, and end the affected communication sessions.
- [ ] Adjust handling for data that is encoded but not recognised, so it cannot get past the filters (use a conservative approach: deny and stop the process if the mapping cannot be determined).
- [ ] Link gateway start/stop events to the security information and event management (SIEM) and security operations centre (SOC) using clear reason codes and policy identifiers.
- [ ] Manage inspection gateway settings using version-controlled change control, with testing in non-production environments and approval before changes go live in production.


---

#### AC-4.5 — Embedded Data Types (Enhancement)

This requirement is about preventing files from hiding other files inside them too deeply, or in ways your organisation cannot properly examine. If someone sends a document or message that contains nested content (for example, a file inside a file, or compressed material that contains further hidden items), it can be harder to see what is actually inside. This increases the risk that harmful or unauthorised content passes through checks unnoticed.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set out and record clear rules that limit embedded content to a maximum of two levels of nesting. It must also reject any embedded content that its inspection tools cannot analyse. Staff must follow procedures that enforce these limits, system settings must be configured so the rules are applied to incoming and outgoing content, and the organisation must keep records showing enforcement decisions—including when items are blocked because they are too deeply nested or cannot be analysed.

##### Enforce max-2 embedded depth and block uninspectable types

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define version-controlled rule set (policy-as-code) for max embedded depth (=2) and inspection capability/limitations list (container/object types) including rationale and update workflow | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design content inspection gate logic: recursive unpack/analysis, embedding depth tracking, hard-stop at level 2, and “uninspectable embedded type” decision path | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement inspection gate integration across inbound and outbound file handling paths (upload/download/API ingestion/egress), ensuring enforcement occurs before persistence and before delivery | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Implement audit evidence generation for every allow/block decision (rule version, embedding depth, embedded type(s), decision, explicit reason) and integrate with existing logging/SIEM pipeline | Security Engineer | Department | 24h | — |
| Add operational controls: quarantine/blocked-item workflow, operator runbook for capability list updates (change control), and alerting for repeated bypass attempts | Operations Lead | Department | 24h | — |
| Develop and execute validation test suite with representative samples (nested archives/file-in-file) proving blocks at depth>2 and blocks uninspectable embedded types; include negative tests for bypass via alternate paths | Quality Assurance Lead | Business Unit | 40h | — |
| Provision/extend inspection tooling configuration (e.g., unpackers/handlers for supported container types) and ensure capability list aligns with actual tool behaviour in all environments | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 16h | £8,000 |

| Total Estimated Effort | Total Estimated Cost |
|---:|---:|
| 216h | £8,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a version-controlled set of automated policy rules that limits embedded content to a maximum depth of 2 levels and blocks embedded content types that cannot be inspected.
- [ ] Maintain an organisation-owned list of the embedded container or object types that the inspection tools can unpack and analyse, including any limitations.
- [ ] Add a recursive content-check step to every way files enter or leave the system, including uploads, application programming interface (API) transfers, attachments, and download (egress) operations.
- [ ] Set the gate to stop immediately at embedding level 2, and to block if embedding level 3 or higher is detected.
- [ ] Set up the gate to block embedded objects that have types that cannot be analysed, based on the limitations list.
- [ ] Set up audit logs for every decision to allow or block access. Each log must include the rule version used, the depth of what was detected, the embedded types involved, and the explicit reason for the block.
- [ ] Run test cases using nested archive files and embedded “file-in-file” samples to confirm the blocking works correctly and to produce evidence for audit purposes.


---

#### AC-4.6 — Metadata (Enhancement)

This expectation is about ensuring that the labels and descriptions attached to each piece of information are reliable, move with the information, and are used to decide where that information is allowed to go. Without this, someone could change the labels so sensitive information is shared by mistake, or information could be sent using incorrect details—leading to unauthorised access, data leaks, or breaches of legal and regulatory requirements.

To meet this, the organisation must set clear rules for which information transfers are allowed or blocked based on specific metadata tags, and document what types of tags are used. The system must securely link those tags to the actual information item, so any unauthorised change is detected, and it must check that the tags have not been altered before allowing or blocking sharing. The tags must be stored in a metadata store that only authorised people and systems can access or update.

Finally, the organisation must keep audit records showing who made the decisions, which tags were used, what happened, and must handle any integrity failures safely.

##### Cryptographically bound metadata tags for flow decisions

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define authoritative metadata tag taxonomy and governance (incl. structural vs descriptive tags, schema identifiers, and which tags are permitted for flow decisions) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design cryptographic metadata envelope format (versioning, tag schema ID, payload digest/hash, integrity protection approach, keying assumptions, failure semantics) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement envelope generation in the data path (authoritative tag extraction, payload digest calculation, integrity protection/MAC or signature, and envelope serialisation) | Software Lead | Department | 56h | — |
| Implement envelope verification at enforcement points (deny/restrict on integrity failure; no fallback to untrusted metadata; integrate with existing routing/authorisation decision flow) | Security Engineer | Department | 64h | — |
| Build access-controlled metadata/policy store for tag-to-decision mappings (least-privilege write access, separation of duties, environment segregation, and policy versioning) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Implement audit logging and SIEM integration (tag-level traceability fields, integrity verification result/failure reason categories, correlation IDs, and retention-aligned forwarding) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £3,000 |
| Develop and execute tampering and regression test suite (tag swap/tamper tests, replay/alteration detection, negative-path verification, performance impact checks, evidence pack for AC-4(6)) | Quality Assurance Lead | Team | 48h | — |
| Produce implementation evidence and runbook (architecture notes, threat model summary, key management assumptions, operational runbook, and audit-ready control mapping) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| **Total Estimated Effort** |  |  | **368h** |  |
| **Total Estimated Cost** |  |  |  | **£9,000** |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and document the official metadata tag categories used to decide whether information flows are allowed or blocked, including whether the tags describe the structure of data and/or provide descriptive details.
- [ ] Design and implement a “metadata envelope” format that uses cryptography to protect both the payload’s fingerprint (digest) and the official tag values.
- [ ] Create the envelope at the moment the data is created or labelled, and make sure the tags come from the organisation’s official metadata store.
- [ ] Carry out envelope verification at every point where enforcement decisions are made, before any decision about routing, exporting, saving data, or releasing information.
- [ ] Set up the policy and tag mapping store with least-privilege access controls, and allow write access only for authorised roles and services.
- [ ] Put in place rules to block or restrict access when integrity checks fail, and make sure there is no fallback to metadata that has not been verified.
- [ ] Record an audit log for every enforcement decision, including the data identifier or payload hash, the tag values, the destination, the result, and the integrity check result. Then send the log to the security information and event management (SIEM) system.


---

#### AC-4.8 — Security and Privacy Policy Filters (Enhancement)

This expectation is about preventing sensitive or private information from leaving the correct systems without being checked first. It matters because, without these checks, staff could accidentally send the wrong kind of file or a file that is too large, include hidden or not-allowed content, or share personal details that should not be disclosed—particularly when data moves from internal systems to external services or between different on-premises security areas.

To meet this, the organisation must set up approved security and privacy checking rules, including:
- file type and size limits,
- field value limits for structured data,
- detection of prohibited words and personal data patterns.

These rules must be used as the deciding step to allow or block data transfers.

For the specific routes covered, transfers are allowed only if **both** the security and privacy checks pass, including checks of the content, metadata, and file type.

If the checking process fails, or if the data does not meet the rules, the data must be quarantined by blocking the transfer or preventing release as appropriate. The system owner and security operations must be notified within 1 hour. If the issue is privacy-related, the privacy officer must also be notified within 1 hour.

##### Inline security+privacy policy filters at egress and cross-domain gateways

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define policy-as-code filter sets (security + privacy) including versioning, schemas, prohibited patterns, PII detection/minimisation rules, and quarantine/block actions | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Define covered information flows and routing requirements (egress + Secret↔Confidential cross-domain), including identification of all bypass paths and enforcement points | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design “both pass” enforcement logic and fail-closed behaviour (deny/quarantine/block release) with 1-hour notification triggers and escalation paths | Architect | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement gateway/inspection integration (inline decision point) to evaluate both filters per transfer, enforce allow/quarantine/block release, and ensure no bypass for covered flows | Platform Engineer | Department | 56h | — |
| Implement audit evidence generation (per-transfer logging: flow ID, filter set versions, security/privacy outcomes, action taken, timestamps) and integrate with SIEM | Security Engineer | Department | 32h | — |
| Build notification workflow for security operations and privacy officer (time-bound within 1 hour), including message templates, correlation IDs, and incident handoff hooks | Operations Lead | Department | 24h | — |
| Testing & assurance: unit/integration tests for filter evaluation, failure modes (cannot evaluate), performance/throughput validation, and end-to-end audit verification for all covered flows | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 40h | £6,000 |
| Deployment & change management: configuration rollout across environments (prod/test), release documentation, runbooks, and operational readiness sign-off | Project Manager | Business Unit | 24h | £2,500 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 284h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £8,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and document the exact information routes for data leaving the system (egress) and for transfers between Secret and Confidential, including every network and application path, to prevent any bypass.
- [ ] Create security policy filter rules approved by the Chief Information Security Officer (CISO) to enforce limits on file type and file size, check that structured fields fall within the required ranges, and block or hide prohibited or hidden content patterns.
- [ ] Create privacy policy filter rules approved by the Chief Information Security Officer (CISO) to detect and minimise personal information, including Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) and General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) identifiers and patterns for sensitive personal data.
- [ ] Set up the inline inspection and gateway checks so they review both filter sets, and allow data transfers only when **security = pass** and **privacy = pass**.
- [ ] Set filter processing to a “fail-closed” approach: if a security check fails, deny the transfer; if a privacy check fails, block release. Also send alerts to the security operations centre (SOC), the system owner, and the privacy officer.
- [ ] Enable audit logging that records the version of each filter set, the security and privacy results, any enforcement actions taken, and the date and time (timestamps) needed to prove that the 1-hour notification requirement is met.

#### AC-4.9 — Human Reviews (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that important information is never shared or accessed automatically when the system is not confident. It matters because, without a human check, confidential or highly sensitive data could be sent to the wrong place or people, or moved between different environments, simply because automated rules cannot reliably judge whether the request is allowed. It also matters because specific legal and contractual obligations—such as export controls, certain compliance frameworks, and health and privacy laws—require extra oversight.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly identify which data transfers and access to confidential or secret datasets involve cross-domain transfers, sharing outside the organisation, or other highly sensitive access. It must document the exact situations that trigger a human review, including when automated decisions are unreliable and when regulations require it. For those situations, it must route or pause the action for review, record what was decided and why for each case, keep those records for later checks, assign named staff to carry out the reviews, and ensure the system, its procedures, its plans, and its audit logs show that the review happens as required.

| Define machine-checkable enforcement conditions (ac-04.09_odp.02) and explicit regulatory trigger mappings (ITAR/EAR/CMMC-L2/L3 and HIPAA/GDPR) with testable criteria and confidence/uncertainty rules | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Design PDP/PEP integration pattern for the application data path (API gateway/service mesh/application middleware) including decision schema, pause/block semantics, and “no bypass” enforcement requirements | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 40h | — |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a catalogue and labels for in-scope information flows, including cross-domain transfers, sharing with external parties, and access to Confidential and Secret datasets.
- [ ] Turn the enforcement conditions (automation uncertainty and the mapping between ITAR, Export Administration Regulations (EAR), Cybersecurity Maturity Model Certification Level 2 (CMMC Level 2) or Level 3 (CMMC Level 3), or Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) / General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR)) into policy triggers that can be checked automatically by a computer.
- [ ] Add a policy decision step and an enforcement step into the application’s data flow so that requests that match the rules can be paused or blocked.
- [ ] Set up a human approval process that logs the flow ID, the trigger condition, who reviewed it, the decision made, and the reason for that decision.
- [ ] Set up enforcement so that only an approved workflow outcome can authorise the transfer or access, with no ways to bypass this requirement.
- [ ] Export and keep unchangeable audit records that link each request to the pause or block action, the reviewer’s decision, and the final release or denial in security information and event management (SIEM).

#### AC-4.10 — Enable and Disable Security or Privacy Policy Filters (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that only trusted, highly authorised people can switch key privacy and security checks on or off for specific transfers of sensitive information. Without this control, someone could accidentally or intentionally disable protections such as blocking harmful software or suspicious indicators, limiting which websites can be accessed, or applying rules that stop sensitive data from leaving approved boundaries. This could allow personal data to be sent without the right consent or without required redaction safeguards.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define which checks can be switched on or off, limit this ability to privileged administrators, and only allow changes when the transfer has been approved for Confidential or Secret information within the authorised security areas, and the change is within the system’s permitted scope.

For privacy consent or redaction, the destination must require privacy controls, and the administrator must have an approved privacy impact assessment. The organisation must also keep auditable records showing what was changed, for which data transfer, and maintain clear procedures and plans that explain how these decisions are governed.

##### Privileged, approved enable/disable of security & privacy filters per data flow

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define authoritative toggle catalogue for security & privacy filters, including allowed enable/disable contexts and required metadata (data-flow identifiers, domains, classifications, PIA requirements) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define and publish security-domain matrix and data-classification gating rules (Confidential/Secret only) with mapping to data-flow contexts and enforcement points | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Design approval-gated enable/disable workflow (admin UI/API contract, request schema, validation logic, system authorisation scope checks, privacy PIA validation rules) | Architect | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement privileged-only enable/disable service (API/UI endpoints, policy evaluation engine, least-privilege service accounts, and enforcement-point configuration for selected data flows only) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 120h | — |
| Implement data-flow scoping and configuration application (before/after state capture, idempotency, rollback strategy, and ensuring changes apply only to the specified data flow) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement tamper-evident audit logging and SIEM integration (audit event schema, evidence fields, retention hooks, and end-to-end verification) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 48h | £3,000 |
| Create operational procedures and auditor-ready evidence pack (runbooks, test evidence, reproducible decision logic, and change-management guidance) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 344h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £3,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep up to date a set of on/off options (a “toggle catalogue”) for the organisation’s security and privacy controls, including data loss prevention (DLP), website content filtering, blocking malware and indicators of compromise (IOCs), and privacy consent and redaction.
- [ ] Create an authoritative security-domain matrix that lists which source and destination domains are allowed to exchange data, what data sensitivity levels are permitted (Confidential or Secret), and which data movements (data flows) are approved.
- [ ] Set up an administrator “enable/disable” process that only users with a privileged role can perform, and record the data-flow identifier, the filters requested, and a reference to the system authorisation scope.
- [ ] Set up automated checks to confirm that both security and privacy requirements are met:

- **Security requirements:** the data flow is approved in the matrix, the data is **Confidential** or **Secret**, the domains are authorised, and the activity is allowed under the system’s authorisation.
- **Privacy requirements:** if the destination involves personal data, it must have the required privacy controls, and there must be an approved privacy impact assessment.
- [ ] Set up enforcement points so the filter settings apply only to the chosen data flow (not across the whole system), and ensure they are based on the validated request context.
- [ ] Set up tamper-evident audit records and send them to a security information and event management (SIEM) system for every action that turns a feature on or off. Each record must include who made the change (admin identity), what changed (before and after state), the relevant data-flow context, and the related approval and privacy impact assessment (PIA) references.
