#### AC-4.11 — Configuration of Security or Privacy Policy Filters (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that only trusted, senior administrators can set up and adjust the rules that scan information for harmful or sensitive content. These rules must be set separately for each system and each type of data. Without this control, the organisation could fail to detect dangerous material such as malware, attempts to exploit systems, or other prohibited content. It could also accidentally expose personal or health information if the organisation does not block the right terms, even while still allowing approved exceptions.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must provide a way for privileged administrators to configure security and privacy filter sets using:
- word lists,
- pattern-matching rules, and
- allow and deny lists.

Security filters must cover malware, exploit, and prohibited-content terms, aligned to the organisation’s Department of Defense (DoD) and Cybersecurity Maturity Model Certification (CMMC) expectations. Privacy filters must block personally identifiable information (PII) and protected health information (PHI) terms, aligned to the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) and the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA), including clearly defined exceptions.

The organisation must also:
- keep clear configuration documentation,
- maintain an up-to-date list of the configured filters,
- restrict editing to privileged roles, and
- record in audit records who changed what and when.

##### Privileged configuration of versioned security/privacy filter sets

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Design filter-set catalogue data model and configuration schema (security/privacy categories, system identifier + data classification keys, wordlists/regex/allow-deny with exceptions, metadata, versioning, effective dates) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement privileged admin configuration workflow (role-restricted create/edit, peer review + security/privacy approval states, promotion to “approved”, controlled activation triggers) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Build automated validation engine for filter sets (regex syntax + safety checks incl. catastrophic backtracking prevention, size/complexity limits, curated test-vector runner for match/non-match expectations) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Develop deployment mechanism with auditable, versioned change control (signed configuration bundle/artifact generation, promotion to enforcement points per system/classification, deployment success/failure recording) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 64h | — |
| Implement audit evidence and inventory reporting (immutable audit logs capturing who/what/when/where, filter-set diff/summary, inventory of configured security/privacy filter sets with versions and scope) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Create admin documentation and operational runbooks (how to structure wordlists/regex, exception/allow rule conventions, validation expectations, rollback approach, evidence mapping for audits) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Security testing and acceptance validation (end-to-end tests for privileged workflow, enforcement correctness across classifications, negative tests for invalid regex/oversized sets, regression testing in non-prod) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 48h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 344h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a filter-set structure that supports: word lists, regular-expression rules, and allow/deny lists, organised by system and data classification.
- [ ] Set up an administrator user interface and application programming interface (API) that only allows privileged users to create and edit security and privacy filter sets, using role-based access control (RBAC) to restrict who can access these functions.
- [ ] Before activation, add automated checks to confirm the regular expression is safe, and run a set of approved test cases that verify both matching and non-matching outcomes.
- [ ] Create a deployment process that uses version numbers and digital signatures, and applies the chosen filter set to the correct enforcement points.
- [ ] Set up audit logs that record: the user identity, the filter set version and a brief summary of what changed, the date and time, the target system and its classification, and the outcome of the deployment.
- [ ] Publish and keep an up-to-date list (inventory) of the configured security and privacy filter sets, and store the configuration documentation, including examples.

#### AC-4.12 — Data Type Identifiers (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that when information is sent between different parts of the organisation, the receiving system can confirm what the data actually is. It should do this by checking the data’s identifying markers and then verifying that the content matches an approved format. Without these checks, a file could be made to look legitimate (for example by using the right name or file type) while containing the wrong structure or meaning. This could lead to incorrect decisions, fraud, or sensitive information being shared when it should not be.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must maintain a list of approved data formats and the matching allowed identifiers (such as file signatures and any required tokens). Systems must use these identifiers rather than relying only on filenames or file counts. The system must then check both the structure and the meaning of the data against the approved specification, allow only transfers that meet the requirements, block transfers that do not, and record the result in audit records so it is clear what was checked and why a transfer was accepted or rejected.

##### Cross-domain data type gateway using signature/token + semantic validation

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define approved cross-domain data format specification library (per allowed data type): required fields, allowed values, syntactic structure rules, semantic/business constraints, and specification versioning model | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Create identifier-to-spec registry design and implementation approach: mapping rules for file signature patterns and/or transfer tokens (including support for multiple internal signatures/tokens per data type) and ambiguity handling (fail if ambiguous) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement gateway enforcement logic (policy enforcement point) at each cross-domain transfer path: signature/token extraction, cryptographic token verification (issuer/signature), identifier validation, mapping to exactly one spec, and fail-closed syntactic + semantic validation | Security Engineer | Department | 120h | — |
| Develop/extend validation engine and rule execution framework: schema/structure validation, semantic validation hooks, and deterministic reason-code outputs for each failure stage | Software Lead | Department | 72h | — |
| Implement audit evidence generation and integration: per-attempt logging of source/destination domains, identifier match result, mapped specification + version, syntactic/semantic pass/fail, and validation reason codes; ensure logs are SIEM-friendly | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Build governance and change-controlled deployment pipeline for the specification library + identifier registry (versioned config/policy-as-code, review gates, promotion across environments, rollback strategy) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort |  |  | **478h** |  |
| Total Estimated Cost |  |  |  | **£18,000** |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and get approval for the approved data format specifications for each cross-domain data type, including the rules for checking that the data is correctly structured (syntax) and meaningfully correct (semantics).
- [ ] Set up an approved registry that links file signature patterns and/or token identifiers to the correct specification versions.
- [ ] Set up a data type gateway at every point where data moves between different domains to extract and check the identifiers from the actual message content and access tokens (not from file names or extensions).
- [ ] Set up the gateway to check that incoming data matches the mapped specification, both in structure and meaning, and to block (fail closed) if anything does not match.
- [ ] Turn on audit logging for every transfer attempt, recording the identifier match result, the mapped specification version, and the reason codes for any syntactic or semantic pass/fail outcome.
- [ ] Include updates to the specification and identifier registry in the change management process, using version control and review before deployment.


---

#### AC-4.13 — Decomposition into Policy-relevant Subcomponents (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure that, before any information is moved from one protected area of your organisation to another, it is first broken down into clear, decision-ready details. These details should cover where the information is coming from, where it is going, how sensitive it is, what type of information it is, any special handling it needs, what attachments it includes, and what security label or certificate it carries.

Without this, the wrong rules may be applied. That can allow sensitive information to be sent to the wrong place, handled incorrectly, or released without the right checks—leading to data leaks, breaches of regulatory requirements, and reputational damage.

To meet this expectation, your organisation must identify and record the source and destination areas, the classification (Secret or Confidential), the data type, handling requirements, attachment information (metadata), and certificate or label information. These must be packaged as a single set of transfer details and submitted to your organisation’s information-movement decision process before the transfer is allowed to complete.

You must also document how this is done, configure the decision process to use these details for filtering, checks, and any possible sanitisation, assign named responsibilities, and keep records showing the decisions made for each transfer.

##### Cross-domain transfer context decomposition via policy decision API

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define enforceable security-domain identifiers and mapping rules (e.g., `sourceDomain`/`destinationDomain` to network/tenant/recipient groups/portal targets), including ownership and change control | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Produce canonical `TransferContext` schema (including required fields: `sourceDomain`, `destinationDomain`, `classification`, `dataType`, `handlingRequirements`, `attachmentsMetadata`, `certificateOrLabelInfo`) with field-level validation rules and versioning strategy | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement TransferContext construction in the application/gateway for all supported cross-domain transfer channels (API/email/file/portal), including extraction of classification/handling requirements and attachment metadata | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Integrate PDP/policy engine API to submit TransferContext and receive enforcement decision/actions (ALLOW/BLOCK/INSPECT/SANITISE_THEN_ALLOW), including robust error handling and timeouts | Security Engineer | Business Unit | 48h | — |
| Implement pre-transfer gating workflow: pause transfer until PDP decision is received; enforce decision outcomes (route to inspection/sanitisation workflow or block); ensure idempotency and safe retries | DevOps Lead | Department | 40h | — |
| Implement audit logging and evidence package: persist submitted TransferContext + decision + timestamp + transfer identifiers; integrate with SIEM and define retention/immutability requirements | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Prevent bypass paths: inventory all cross-domain transfer routes, disable/limit direct send paths where feasible, enforce gateway-only routing for supported channels, and document residual bypass risks | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £15,000 |
| Build test plan and execute validation (unit/integration/e2e) covering required-field completeness, decision enforcement, sanitisation/inspection routing, and audit evidence for each outcome | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 48h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort | 360h | Total Estimated Cost | £15,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish security-domain identifiers that can be enforced, and map each one to the real source and destination environments.
- [ ] Create a standard (canonical) **TransferContext** data structure that includes: **source domain**, **destination domain**, **classification**, **data type**, **handling requirements**, **attachment metadata**, and **certificate or label information**.
- [ ] Connect the transfer gateway/service to a policy decision system (policy decision application programming interface (API) or rules engine). This system should take the transfer context information (TransferContext) and respond with a decision to either allow, block, inspect, or sanitise the transfer.
- [ ] Block the release of the payload until the policy decision has been received and recorded, by enforcing a pre-transfer check (gating) before sending it.
- [ ] Set up inspection and sanitisation steps so they run when the policy engine asks for them, before the content is released to the destination domain.
- [ ] Enable audit logging for each transfer event, recording both the submitted transfer details (TransferContext) and the final enforcement decision outcome.
- [ ] Close or limit any bypass routes so that all supported ways of transferring data across different domains use the same “break down and decide” process.


---

#### AC-4.14 — Security or Privacy Policy Filter Constraints (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that any information shared between different parts of your organisation uses a strict, pre-approved message format, rather than an open-ended one. If messages are allowed to be flexible or loosely structured, attackers or careless systems could send unexpected data, hidden instructions, or badly formed content that avoids safeguards. This could result in unauthorised actions, privacy breaches, or corrupted records.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must:
- Define and document the approved cross-domain message rules.
- Ensure receiving systems only accept messages that exactly match the fixed structure (with no extra or unknown fields).
- Require messages to be written using UTF-8.
- Limit each message to no more than 10KB.
- Allow only letters and numbers, with no special characters.

Any message that fails any of these checks must be rejected. The organisation must also:
- Keep a documented list of the checks (filters) used.
- Record whether each message was accepted or rejected in audit logs.
- Include these constraints in both the system security plan and the privacy plan.

##### Enforce enumerated UTF-8/10KB/alpha-numeric filters at cross-domain boundary

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the approved enumerated filter specification (ac-4.4.14_prm_1): fixed schema rules, UTF-8 requirement, 10KB payload limit, alpha-numeric constraints, and precise “special characters” definition | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Produce two version-controlled enumerated schema policies in the policy repository: (1) Security policy filter (XML/JSON fixed tags, no free-form fields) and (2) Privacy policy filter (JSON fixed field set, no free-form fields) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement boundary enforcement in the cross-domain transfer component (API gateway and/or message broker): deterministic deny-by-default validation for UTF-8 decoding, canonical payload size ≤10KB, exact schema match (reject unknown/missing), and alpha-numeric/special-character rejection | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Configure routing to apply the correct enumerated filter per transfer type (security vs privacy), including schema version selection and fail-closed behaviour across all environments (prod/test/DR) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement audit evidence generation for each message decision: accept/reject logging with filter ID + schema version + failure reason (without echoing sensitive payload content) and correlation identifiers for source/destination domains | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Integrate audit events with SIEM (event format, routing, retention alignment, and access controls) and validate end-to-end ingestion | SOC/SIEM engineer | Enterprise | 16h | £6,000 |
| Update governance artefacts: reference the boundary enforcement component and the specific filter policy versions in the system security plan and privacy plan, including traceability to AC-4(14) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 176h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £6,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and route all cross-domain data transfer paths through a single boundary control component (an application programming interface (API) gateway and/or a message broker).
- [ ] Set up the listed security and privacy filter rules using the agreed fixed format and field set, using UTF-8 encoding, with a maximum size of 10 kilobytes, allowing only letters and numbers, and with no restrictions on special characters.
- [ ] Set up input checks that reject any requests that include unexpected fields or leave required fields out, and that prevent users from sending free-form data. Apply this both to security data (XML and JavaScript Object Notation (JSON) must use fixed tags) and to privacy data (JSON must use a fixed set of fields).
- [ ] Check incoming request data at the entry point to ensure it is valid UTF-8 text and that its size is 10 kilobytes (KB) or less, using the standard (canonical) form of the payload bytes.
- [ ] Apply character checks to all limited input fields so they accept only letters and numbers, and block any special characters according to the policy.
- [ ] Set up consistent “reject” replies and detailed audit records for every accept or reject decision. Each record must include the filter identifier, the schema version, and the reason for any failure, but must not record any sensitive payload content.
- [ ] Update the system security plan and the privacy plan to point to the boundary enforcement component and to the exact versions of the schema and filter policies.


---

#### AC-4.15 — Detection of Unsanctioned Information (Enhancement)

This expectation is about preventing dangerous or private information from being sent from one part of the organisation to another. When information is shared between different security areas, the organisation must check what is being sent for three risks: malicious software, information that is not allowed to leave the original area, and files that could be run and disrupt or damage the systems in the receiving area. If any of these organisation-defined unauthorised items are found, the transfer must be blocked so the receiving area never receives the item.

This matters because, without these checks, harmful software could be introduced, confidential or restricted information could be exposed to the wrong place, or the destination systems could be damaged or disrupted by files that can be executed.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must follow its Cross-Domain Security Transfer Policy and Data Transfer Privacy Policy, using the defined rules and procedures to detect these risks during cross-area transfers and stop the transfer when they are found.

##### Policy-driven inspection gateway for cross-domain transfer blocking

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define AC-4(15) unsanctioned information policy mapping (malicious code / unauthorised release data / harmful executable content) into machine-actionable rule categories, including policy references and block reason taxonomy | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Perform cross-domain transfer path discovery and gap analysis; produce a complete inventory of all transfer mechanisms (web/API/file/messaging/connectors) and design routing so no bypass paths exist | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Design and implement inspection gateway/proxy integration pattern (routing, request/response interception, payload extraction, streaming/size limits, and fail-closed/quarantine behaviour) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement policy-as-code engine and rule evaluation workflow (versioned rules, entitlement/classification checks, executable-content indicators, rule match precedence, and explicit block reasons) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Integrate multi-layer inspection capabilities (malware scanning incl. archive recursion; executable-content/run-capable detection; optional sandbox detonation for high-risk signals) and wire results into policy decisions | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 80h | £45,000 |
| Build audit evidence and SIEM integration (transfer ID, source/destination domains, payload hash, detected category, action taken, policy rule reference; log schema, retention alignment, and searchable dashboards) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Operational hardening and change control (gateway self-protection, rate limiting, resilience, tested policy rollout pipeline, monitoring/alerting, and runbooks for inspection failures) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £12,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 400h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £57,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Make a complete list of every method the application and its integrations use to move data between different systems, and document how each one works.
- [ ] Set up routing so that all cross-domain data requests pass through the inspection gateway or proxy, with no bypass.
- [ ] Set up “policy-as-code” rules that translate **AC-04.15 ODP.01** unsanctioned categories into specific, concrete detection controls.
- [ ] Add malware scanning, data classification and access-right checks, and detection of executable content to the inspection process.
- [ ] Apply a “deny-by-policy” approach to block any transfers when unauthorised information is detected, and return controlled error messages to the people or systems making the request.
- [ ] Set up audit logs to record the transfer reference, a fingerprint of the data (payload hash), the categories detected, what actions were taken, and which policy rules were applied.
- [ ] Test with realistic harmful files and unauthorised release attempts, and confirm that file transfers are blocked.

#### AC-4.17 — Domain Authentication (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that, for every piece of information your systems send and receive, the organisation can clearly and reliably identify who sent it and who received it. Without this, wrongdoing, mistakes, or breaches of policy can be hidden behind missing or unclear identities, making investigations harder and preventing personal information journeys from being checked or corrected.

To meet this expectation, your organisation must put in place a clear method to label and verify the sending and receiving points for information transfers. This includes using separate, distinct identifiers for the organisation, a system, an application, a service, and an individual, and making sure these identifiers are different and not open to interpretation.

The system must carry out this verification as part of the transfer, and it must record the verified sender and receiver details in audit records so they can be traced later. Your organisation must also keep the required procedures and documentation up to date, including what staff should do if identification cannot be confirmed.

##### Domain authentication for source/destination with audit-ready labels

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define AC-4(17) domain label taxonomy and registry (formats, allowed values per domain type, ownership, review cadence) and publish as an engineering standard | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design authenticated source/destination binding model at transfer boundaries (individual vs system/application/service), including cryptographic validation approach (mTLS/cert pinning, signed assertions, short-lived tokens) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement domain label validation and fail-closed enforcement in the application/API/messaging gateway (presence, schema validation, cryptographic verification, identity-to-label consistency checks) | Security Engineer | Department | 56h | — |
| Implement destination label derivation from authenticated target endpoint identity (receiving API/service identity, consumer identity, resource owner identity) and remove reliance on client-supplied metadata | Software Lead | Department | 40h | — |
| Extend audit logging schema to record authenticated source and destination domain labels (all required domain types), plus correlation identifier for end-to-end reconstruction; ensure integrity protections and SIEM forwarding | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Build and run test suite: unit/integration tests for valid/invalid label scenarios, replay/forgery resistance checks, and end-to-end correlation verification across tiers | Quality Assurance Lead | Team | 40h | — |
| Produce operational runbook and evidence pack (registry, enforcement/config review records, sample audit log entries, failure handling guidance) for audit readiness | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 248h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and get approval for a domain label taxonomy and registry that covers the domain types listed in **ac-04.17_odp**, using unique and unambiguous label formats.
- [ ] Set up source authentication checks at the point where data is transferred, for both: (1) individual users (using the identity provider session principal) and (2) systems, applications, or services (using workload or service identity, such as mutual Transport Layer Security (mTLS) or signed assertions).
- [ ] Set up destination authentication binding by using the domain name from the authenticated receiving endpoint identity (not information provided by the client).
- [ ] Add fail-closed enforcement in the application, application programming interface (API), and messaging gateway to reject transfers when the authenticated source and destination domain labels are missing, invalid, or cannot be verified.
- [ ] Extend audit logging to record the authenticated source and destination domain labels (all required domain types) and include a correlation identifier so the full end-to-end activity can be reconstructed.
- [ ] Set up security information and event management (SIEM) and monitoring to collect the new audit fields, and add protections to ensure the data cannot be altered. Then test the data transfers across all environments (production, testing, and disaster recovery).

#### AC-4.19 — Validation of Metadata (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure that when information is shared between different parts of the organisation that follow different rules, any extra details that come with it are checked and corrected before it is delivered. Without this, sensitive information could be labelled wrongly, sent to the wrong place, or include personal information that should have been restricted or removed—creating legal and reputational risk.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must define and apply checks to the extra information (metadata) during every cross-domain transfer, so that it follows the required Department of Defense handling rules. This includes the correct security classification, what can be shared, the system of record, and the required security markings. The organisation must also ensure the metadata matches the classification of the main information it describes.

The organisation must apply privacy protections to the metadata by limiting personal data to only what is strictly necessary, ensuring the required legal basis information is included, and removing (redacting) personal-data fields.

The organisation must document how this is done, configure its systems to enforce it, and keep audit records showing what was checked, filtered, corrected, or blocked for each transfer.

##### Metadata validation and filtering on cross-domain transfers

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define metadata validation rule set (policy-as-code) for ac-04.19_odp.01 and ac-04.19_odp.02, including domain transfer mappings, metadata schema/field semantics, and correction vs block criteria | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Specify effective payload classification derivation approach (metadata vs bound payload), including deterministic rules, edge cases, and how to handle missing/contradictory labels | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design and implement cross-domain transfer enforcement point (API gateway / transfer middleware / secure egress component) with a single metadata-aware validation step for all approved flows | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement metadata validation engine: validate consistency (classification/releasability/system of record/security markings), apply HIPAA minimum-necessary metadata rules, enforce GDPR lawful-basis tags, and perform safe redaction/masking for personal-data fields in metadata | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Implement correction-and-forward logic with deterministic transformation rules and ambiguity detection; ensure “no silent pass-through” behaviour and correct handling of correction failures | Software Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Build audit evidence generation and integration (structured logs/events, rule set versioning, validated fields, allowed/corrected/blocked outcomes, redaction/correction actions) and wire to SIEM/monitoring | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Create test harness and acceptance test suite covering source→destination domain permutations, metadata inconsistency cases, redaction outcomes, and performance/throughput baselines; include regression tests for rule set updates | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 48h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 336h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £6,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the official metadata structure and the field-by-field rules for: classification, whether information can be released, the system of record, the required security labels, and how personal data is identified.
- [ ] Encode Department of Defence (DoD) domain-transfer rules and privacy filters as enforceable “policy-as-code” for every source-to-destination domain pair.
- [ ] Set up a metadata-aware cross-domain transfer control point (a gateway or middleware) so that every cross-domain data flow must pass through validation.
- [ ] Add checks during data transfer to work out the effective payload classification, and confirm that the metadata matches the rules for the destination.
- [ ] Put privacy protections in place for metadata, including: allowing only the minimum necessary items for health data (HIPAA), checking that data processing has a valid legal basis for data protection (General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR)), and hiding or removing personal information where it appears.
- [ ] Set up predictable results (either correct and continue, or block) and make sure any metadata that does not meet requirements cannot be released unless it first passes validation.
- [ ] Enable audit logging that records the rule set version, the fields that were checked and validated, any redaction or correction actions taken, and the final outcome (allowed, corrected, or blocked) for every transfer attempt.

#### AC-4.20 — Approved Solutions (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that very sensitive information can only be moved between different security areas using approved methods. If this is not done, confidential or secret information could be sent through the wrong systems, blocked incorrectly, or routed using unapproved tools or settings. This increases the risk of unauthorised access, data leaks, or information being handled improperly.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must use only National Security Agency (NSA)-approved cross-domain solutions and settings to control how Confidential and Secret information moves between security domains. It must also clearly document, in its cross-domain information flow rules, the step-by-step procedures staff must follow, the system design, and the actual configuration settings.

The organisation must keep an up-to-date list and baseline of the approved configurations, maintain audit records that show the approved controls are being applied, and include the approach and named responsibilities in the system security plan so that it can be independently checked.

##### Enforce NSA-approved cross-domain solutions for Confidential/Secret flows

| Draft and update cross-domain information flow enforcement policy with appendix listing exact approved solution/configuration identifiers and Confidential/Secret information-flow rules (allow/deny, protocol/application constraints, handling constraints) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Define configuration baseline approach (single source of truth), including version control structure, template/profile naming conventions, and drift-prevention checks requirements | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

| Create evidence generation package: configuration compliance exports/snapshots per enforcement point and audit-log correlation fields (enforcement component ID + approved profile ID) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |

| Update System Security Plan (SSP) with enforcement approach and named responsibilities (inventory owner, change approver, compliance validator, audit evidence reviewer) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 12h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 154h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £12,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an authoritative inventory that lists every security-domain boundary for Confidential and Secret information flows, and links each one to the specific National Security Agency (NSA)-approved solution and configuration profile that is used.
- [ ] Update the cross-domain information flow enforcement policy to:

- list the approved solutions and configurations, and  
- set clear allow and deny rules for how **Confidential** and **Secret** information may flow between domains.
- [ ] Create an approved, version-controlled set of configuration templates and profiles (templates/profiles) for each enforcement point, and deploy it using automated configuration management.
- [ ] Put controls in place to check that live (running) configurations are continuously or periodically compared against the approved baseline, so any changes are detected.
- [ ] Export and keep configuration evidence for each enforcement point, showing the approved settings that were applied.
- [ ] Enable and keep audit logs that record enforcement decisions (allowed or denied). Include identifiers for the enforcement component and the approved profile.
- [ ] Update the System Security Plan to describe how enforcement will work and who is responsible for each part, and publish operational guides for how to verify compliance and handle exceptions.

#### AC-4.21 — Physical or Logical Separation of Information Flows (Enhancement)

This requirement is about keeping different types of information traffic on separate routes through your network, so they cannot be mixed up while they are moving. Without this, a mistake or misuse could allow sensitive information to end up in the wrong environment, enable unauthorised access between systems, or allow operational technology (the systems that run equipment) to be reached from the wrong place—raising the risk of disruption or data exposure.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must first decide and record which traffic must be separated. This includes, for example: incoming versus outgoing communications; requests versus replies; Secret versus Confidential information; and information technology (IT) versus operational technology (OT) control traffic. It must then set up and record the logical and physical measures used to enforce the separation, such as dedicated network sections and firewall areas; separate encrypted connection routes for each type of traffic and each sensitivity level; and separate routing routes for each category. It must also use dedicated physical network and switching routes for Secret and OT control traffic.

The organisation must keep the separation rules, designs, configuration details, and proof that the controls are working up to date. It must assign named responsibilities and keep records so the separation can be checked and verified.

##### Implement VRFs/VLANs + firewall zones + per-classification VPN tunnels

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Produce traffic taxonomy + traffic-to-construct mapping (inbound/outbound, request/response per service/API, Secret/Confidential, IT/OT control) including VRF/zone/tunnel bindings | Network Security Architect | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design segmentation architecture: VLAN/VRF/routing instances per classification + routing domain rules (no route leaking; document any required interconnections and restrictions) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement VLAN/VRF/routing instance configuration and baseline connectivity (lab + production parity), including validation of non-commingling at L3 | Platform Engineer | Department | 56h | — |
| Configure firewall security zones with stateful inspection and default-deny between non-approved zones; implement directionality (inbound entry vs outbound return) and rule sets per traffic category | Security Engineer | Department | 64h | — |
| Configure per-classification/per-traffic VPN tunnels (separate tunnels for Secret vs Confidential; separate IT vs OT where applicable), bind tunnels to dedicated address pools and restrict to corresponding VRF/zone destinations | Infrastructure Lead | Department | 48h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 312h

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Document how network traffic is classified and mapped, including inbound versus outbound traffic, requests versus responses, Secret versus Confidential data, and IT versus operational technology (OT) controls. Record how these map to virtual local area networks (VLANs) and virtual routing and forwarding instances (VRFs), firewall zones, routing domains, and virtual private network (VPN) tunnels.
- [ ] Set up virtual routing and forwarding (VRF) instances, and routing instances, for the Secret and Confidential environments. Then assign each application tier and endpoint to the correct VRF.
- [ ] Set up separate firewall security zones for each type of network traffic, and configure rules that remember active connections (stateful) and block everything by default (default-deny) between zones that are not approved.
- [ ] Set up separate virtual private network (VPN) tunnels for each type and category of traffic. Link each tunnel to its own dedicated set of IP addresses, and restrict those addresses to the matching virtual routing and forwarding (VRF) instance or network zone.
- [ ] Update the service or application programming interface (API) network routes so that requests enter through the designated inbound (request) zone and responses leave through the designated outbound (return) zone.
- [ ] Collect and keep evidence (network diagrams, exported firewall, virtual private network (VPN) and virtual routing and forwarding (VRF) settings, and copies of relevant logs) showing that separation is enforced and that attempts to mix traffic were blocked.

#### AC-4.22 — Access Only (Enhancement)

This requirement is about allowing people to use one single computer to view information from different security areas, while ensuring that information from one area cannot be used in another. Without this, a user could accidentally or intentionally copy sensitive information from a higher-protection area into a lower-protection area, leading to unauthorised disclosure, fraud, or breaches of legal and regulatory requirements.

To meet this, the organisation must configure the single device so it only allows viewing within each area. Users must be able to open and read content in each area, but the system must actively stop any way of moving information between areas, including copying and pasting, saving or exporting, printing, using shared storage, or moving data using removable media.

The organisation must document:
- the rules for how this separation is enforced,
- the procedures for running and maintaining it, and
- the system design and configuration settings that make it work.

It must also keep audit records showing that access occurred and that attempts to transfer information were blocked. Named responsibilities must be clearly assigned to the right staff, so that administrators and security personnel oversee the separation properly.

##### Access-only multi-domain terminal with enforced no-transfer controls

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define reference architecture for access-only multi-domain terminal (context isolation model, domain-to-session mapping, threat model, and “no-transfer” control objectives) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Build and harden the access-only gold image (minimal OS/apps, disable local persistence, restrict admin access, enforce secure baseline, session lockdown) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement per-domain isolated execution contexts on the same device (e.g., separate VDI sessions/containers with no shared clipboard, no shared filesystem, no cross-context session communication) | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Configure and enforce “no-transfer” primitives across all domain contexts (block clipboard, disable drag-and-drop, block downloads/export/save-as, restrict printing to domain-scoped queues, disable removable media, restrict network/share access to domain-appropriate locations only) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Centralise configuration management and policy-as-code for the access-only build and transfer-block settings (ensuring persistence after updates; automated drift detection) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Integrate audit logging for domain access and denied transfer attempts (SIEM event schema, correlation rules, alerting thresholds, retention alignment, and evidence export) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £12,000 |
| Develop operating procedures and exception handling playbook (controlled printing workflow, time-bounded exceptions, approval evidence, periodic access review, and runbook for incident response) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 280h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £12,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set up domain-to-context mapping for the access-only terminal, so you can specify which user roles are allowed to view each domain context.
- [ ] Create and deploy a secure “access-only” endpoint or virtual desktop infrastructure (VDI) session host “gold” image that includes only essential software and prevents software from being saved permanently on the local device.
- [ ] Set up separate, isolated execution environments for each security domain, with clipboard sharing turned off and no access to files across those environments.
- [ ] Disable or block transfer methods, including copy-and-paste between different contexts, downloading or exporting files, drag-and-drop, using removable storage devices, and general printing.
- [ ] Centralise and keep version records of the endpoint and virtual desktop infrastructure (VDI) policy settings, so the no-transfer controls stay enabled even after changes.
- [ ] Turn on security information and event management (SIEM) logging for access to the domain and for denied transfer attempts; check that the logs are complete using test cases.
- [ ] Publish clear operating procedures for maintenance and for time-limited exceptions (for example, controlled printing for specific business needs), and assign named responsible owners.

#### AC-4.23 — Modify Non-releasable Information (Enhancement)

This requirement is about protecting information when it is sent between different parts of the business that do not have the same level of trust. Any information that is not authorised to be shared must be deliberately hidden or changed before it leaves. Without this, sensitive information—such as secret identifiers, confidential customer information, or internal-only data—could be accidentally exposed during transfers, previews, or record-keeping. This could lead to data leaks, misuse, or attacks that are specifically targeted.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- Clearly define which cross-area information transfers require this protection.
- Document that any information that is not approved for sharing will be handled using redaction and masking.
- Build these rules into its official guidance, day-to-day procedures, system design, and security plans.
- Configure systems so masking happens automatically for the relevant transfer routes.
- Ensure the right named staff are responsible, including system and network administrators and information security staff.
- Keep audit records showing that masking was applied.

##### Cross-domain transfer redaction/masking via secure exchange service

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---|---:|---:|

| Design secure exchange service enforcement architecture (content-aware vs tag-based strategy, transformation pipeline, bypass prevention, and error-handling rules to avoid sensitive leakage) | Architect | Enterprise | 40h | — |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and record all ways data can move between different security areas for the application, including preview or secondary screens, and document the security areas that send and receive the data.
- [ ] For each receiving domain, define which data elements must not be released, and set out the redaction or masking format for each type of data element.
- [ ] Set up a secure exchange or gateway enforcement point so that all cross-domain data transfers must pass through the transformation service.
- [ ] Set up content-aware or label-based transformation to apply the organisation’s approved modification action (redaction and masking) before the content is released.
- [ ] Link transformation events to audit logging and security information and event management (SIEM) using non-sensitive evidence (rule identifiers, transformation types, and hashes), and check that the records are kept for the required retention period.
- [ ] Run end-to-end tests for each way data is transferred to confirm that any fields that must not be released are always hidden or masked, and that the original values never appear in the data sent or in any logs.


---

#### AC-4.24 — Internal Normalized Format (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure information is understood correctly when it moves between different parts of the organisation. It does this by first converting the information into a standard internal format, and then recreating it in the exact format that the receiving area expects. Without this, attackers or careless systems could send data with unexpected formatting, which could be misread and lead to incorrect decisions, damaged or corrupted records, or harmful data leaving the organisation in the wrong form.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- clearly identify which information transfers move between different security areas
- ensure the system turns incoming data into a consistent internal representation
- then regenerate it so it matches the destination’s requirements for fields, data types, structure, and formats

The organisation must also reject invalid or unprocessable data (or handle it safely). It must keep clear records showing what happened, who is responsible, and how this approach is documented in design, procedures, configuration, and the organisation’s security planning.

##### Canonical parse-and-regenerate at cross-domain data boundaries

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Cross-domain transfer inventory and boundary mapping (per integration path: API gateway, message consumer, ETL step) including data types and destination contracts | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define canonical internal models per transferred data type (strict typing, canonicalisation rules, versioning strategy, explicit null/optional handling, enumerations) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement strict parse → validate → canonicalise library/module (reject unknown fields, enforce encoding/length/type/value constraints; deterministic canonicalisation) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 72h | — |
| Implement regenerate layer to emit destination-specific contracts exactly (field ordering/structure/encoding, required vs optional, template-driven regeneration) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Safe failure and quarantine workflow (block forwarding on errors; restricted-access quarantine store; alert/event emission; retry policy for transient vs permanent failures) | Operations Lead | Department | 40h | — |
| Audit-ready evidence and observability (correlation/transaction IDs linking parse → normalise → regenerate → delivery; log schema; canonical model version + destination contract version; retention alignment) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Security testing and validation (unit/integration tests for invalid encodings, schema violations, type mismatches, boundary bypass attempts; negative tests; deterministic output checks) | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 48h | — |
| Deployment pipeline updates (config/version artefact management for canonical models/templates; rollout/rollback; environment parity checks) | DevOps Lead | Business Unit | 24h | £3,000 |

| Total Estimated Effort | Total Estimated Cost |
|---:|---:|
| 336h | £3,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a list of all information moved between different systems, and clearly define the point where each integration starts and ends (for example, an application programming interface (API) gateway, a message receiver, or an extract, transform, and load (ETL) step).
- [ ] For each type of transferred data, define a standard internal model with strict data typing and clear rules for how the data is converted into that standard format.
- [ ] Apply strict checks at every point where data enters or leaves the system: validate the format, encoding, and data types, and convert incoming information into the agreed internal “canonical” format. If anything is wrong, stop immediately (fail fast) rather than continuing.
- [ ] Set up regeneration templates that produce destination-compliant outputs using only the approved “canonical” model, with no direct copying or passing through of fields from the original input.
- [ ] Add safe failure handling to move invalid data into quarantine and stop it from being delivered to the destination domain.
- [ ] Set up audit logging to include a reference ID that links related events, the canonical model version, the destination contract version, and the results of parsing and regenerating.
- [ ] Create and run automated tests to check for invalid character encodings, data that breaks the required structure (schema), incorrect data types, and that regenerated outputs are correct.


---

#### AC-4.25 — Data Sanitization (Enhancement)

This expectation is about ensuring that when information is moved between different security areas, any data that should not be allowed to move is permanently wiped or destroyed, so it cannot be recovered. Without this, sensitive information could end up in the wrong place, where it could be read, misused, or used to support harmful activity, such as delivering malicious content, taking control of malicious code, adding malicious capabilities, or hiding information in plain sight.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must first identify every instance where information is transferred between security areas, and then apply its own data sanitisation policy to each transfer. The organisation must have clear written procedures, make sure the right staff can access and follow them, and assign named responsibilities to accountable roles, including system and network administrators.

The organisation must also build sanitisation into system design and settings, keep records showing that sanitisation has taken place, retain those records for verification, include the approach in the system security plan, and maintain any supporting documentation needed to demonstrate compliance.

##### Policy-driven sanitise-on-transfer for cross-domain data flows

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Build and maintain the cross-domain transfer catalogue (“transfer map”) covering all integration pathways (APIs, message buses/streams, storage replication/backup, gateway/broker, email/SaaS connectors, removable media workflows, DMZ components) with source/destination domains, data classification, and transfer mechanism | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Define sanitisation policy-as-code rules by translating the organisation’s data sanitisation policy into enforceable logic (data type + storage medium + transfer mechanism) including explicit objective to minimise sensitive information spillage | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Design enforcement architecture for sanitise-on-transfer (eg egress layer, messaging egress, storage replication/backup jobs, gateway/broker forwarding) including block/transform decisioning and handling of “not applicable” justifications | Architect | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Implement sanitisation enforcement integrations across selected pathways (API/microservice egress, messaging/streaming egress, storage replication/backup hooks, gateway/broker forwarding) with idempotency, failure handling, and policy-driven gating so transfers cannot complete without required sanitisation | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 120h | — |
| Implement cryptographic erasure / secure erase / destruction workflow adapters for supported target platforms (eg key lifecycle events for encrypted storage; secure erase completion status for supported media; destruction workflow triggers where required) | Security Engineer | Department | 72h | £25,000 |
| Generate audit evidence for every sanitisation event (timestamp, source/destination domain identifiers, data classification, sanitisation method, target identifiers, workflow identity/operator identity, verification outcome) and ensure audit schema is consistent across pathways | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Configure SIEM/log ingestion, retention, and operational runbooks; update system security plan entry and provide test/assurance evidence for assessment (including negative tests where sanitisation is not applicable and positive tests where transfers are blocked until completion) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 64h | £6,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 440h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £31,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and get approval for a cross-domain transfer map that covers every way data can leave and enter applications, including all integration points.
- [ ] Turn the organisation’s data sanitisation policy into enforceable “policy-as-code” rules, linked to the type of data, the storage or transmission medium, and the method used to transfer it.
- [ ] Implement “sanitise-on-transfer” enforcement in the outgoing (egress), gateway, and transfer process, so transfers are blocked until sanitisation is complete.
- [ ] Integrate checks that confirm sanitisation has been completed and signals that confirm key erasure has finished, so the system can record an auditable result.
- [ ] Set up audit logging for every sanitisation event, recording the domain, method, target, user identity, and verification result, and send the records to the security information and event management (SIEM) system.
- [ ] Update the system security plan and day-to-day operating guides to document the data sanitisation approach, who is responsible, and where the supporting evidence is stored.


---

#### AC-4.26 — Audit Filtering Actions (Enhancement)

This requirement is about keeping a clear record of what happens to each message as it moves between different parts of the organisation’s systems that have different rules. It matters because, without detailed records, you cannot prove that the correct filtering rules were applied. You also may not be able to explain why a message was changed, blocked, or put in quarantine, which increases the risk of inappropriate information crossing boundaries and makes mistakes harder to fix.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- define which message movements across boundaries count
- ensure that for every message that is checked, the specific filtering action taken is recorded and linked to that message
- record the final result of the filtering decision

These records must be kept for the required period, be searchable for later review, and include enough detail to support troubleshooting—for example, the reason a message was modified or blocked.

##### Per-message content filtering audit records at cross-domain boundaries

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Map cross-domain content filtering enforcement points and define boundary taxonomy (e.g., Internal→DMZ, Corporate→Internet, Partner→Internal) with owners and applicable policy sets | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define per-message audit schema for filtering action/outcome (message identifier, action, outcome, rule name/reason code, policy version, timestamps) and align to AU-2/AU-12 evidence requirements | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement/enable filtering audit event generation at each boundary technology (gateway/component configuration) to emit action+outcome per individual message with stable correlation key | Security Engineer | Department | 40h | — |
| Build SIEM/log normalisation and correlation logic to query action and outcome together by message identifier; implement dashboards/queries and ensure field-level mapping is consistent across boundaries | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Configure immutable/write-once capable log routing, retention, and access controls for audit events; verify integrity protections and least-privilege access | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £12,000 |
| Execute end-to-end validation: controlled test messages across each boundary path; produce an evidence pack showing 100% audit coverage and correct action/outcome pairs | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Operationalise: monitoring alerts for missing/failed audit events, runbooks, and change-management checklist for future boundary/policy updates | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 176h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £12,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] For each cross-domain security boundary, identify the specific content-filtering enforcement point(s) used in the environment.
- [ ] Set up the filtering components to record an audit event for each message, including a consistent message identifier, what filtering action was taken, and the result of the filtering.
- [ ] Add troubleshooting details to audit records (rule name, reason code, policy version, and timestamps) and make sure these details are filled in for every outcome.
- [ ] In the security information and event management (SIEM) and log processing pipeline, combine and match audit events using the message identifier so that the action and the outcome can be searched together.
- [ ] Set up rules to keep audit records for the required period and protect their accuracy when filtering audit events in the organisation’s central log system, and limit who can access audit data.
- [ ] Run boundary-path test cases to confirm that each test message results in the correct action and outcome audit record, and that end-to-end correlation works correctly.

#### AC-4.27 — Redundant/Independent Filtering Mechanisms (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that when information is moved between different protected areas of the business, it is checked against the agreed rules more than once, using more than one type of checking approach. If this is not done, a failure, outage, or software defect in one checking tool could allow unsafe or unwanted content to pass through, or could stop enforcement altogether—creating real risk such as malware, sensitive data leaks, or breaches of policy.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- define which types of information (each data type) must be checked during transfers between areas
- set out clear procedures for how the checks are carried out and how the results are applied
- document how the filtering is built, configured, and monitored
- keep records showing that the checks were performed and what decision was made
- include this approach in the security plan
- assign clear responsibility to the relevant staff

For each data type, the system must use duplicate and independent filtering methods—for example, different implementations and separate running components—so that if one method fails, the other still enforces the rules.

##### Active-active dual content filters per data type at cross-domain transfer

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define cross-domain transfer points, data types, and per-data-type decision rules (allow/quarantine/block) including final decision logic (block/quarantine if either engine flags) | Security Architect | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Select/confirm two independent filtering engines per data type (different code base/libraries and separate processes/services) and document independence evidence (architecture, dependencies, update pipelines) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | £0 |
| Design fail-closed enforcement model and unavailability handling (engine down/crash/timeout) including “most restrictive policy if both down” | Security Architect | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement gateway/enforcement deployment for Engine A and Engine B at each cross-domain transfer point (separate services/processes, service accounts, network boundaries) | Infrastructure Lead | Business Unit | 56h | £18,000 |
| Implement per-data-type routing and orchestration so both engines are evaluated for every transfer, with final decision aggregation and deterministic outcomes | Software Lead | Department | 48h | £6,000 |
| Configure audit logging and evidence fields (timestamp, source/destination domains, data type, engine decision, final decision, reason codes, error/unavailability indicators) and integrate with SIEM | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | £4,000 |
| Build operational readiness: health checks, alerting, runbooks, configuration/version control, and controlled update procedures for both engines (separate change paths) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £0 |
| Execute validation and assurance testing (independence verification, failover/fail-closed tests, representative transfer test cases, and audit log review) and produce compliance evidence pack | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £0 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 336h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £28,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify all points where information moves between different domains, and list the types of data that need content filtering.
- [ ] Set policy actions for each type of data and define the enforcement decision rule (for example, block or quarantine if either system flags it).
- [ ] For each type of data, choose and run two separate filtering engines. They must use different code and libraries, and they must run in separate processes or services.
- [ ] Set the system to fail closed, so that if the engine is unavailable it does not allow access by default for any type of data.
- [ ] Turn on and check audit logging that records: the engine’s decisions, the final decision, and any error or unavailability indicators.
- [ ] Set up separate health checks, alerts, and step-by-step recovery instructions (runbooks) for each engine, and test failover by deliberately simulating an engine failure.


---

#### AC-4.28 — Linear Filter Pipelines (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that whenever information is sent between different parts of the organisation that have different protection levels, it is checked in the same clear, step-by-step way every time, with no way to skip the check. Without this, sensitive or unsuitable information could get through by taking an alternative route, exploiting a misconfiguration, or being handled in a way that avoids the check—leading to unauthorised access, breaches of policy, or data leaks.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- Clearly define which information transfers are covered.
- Publish a rule that all covered transfers must pass through a single, sequential filtering process.
- Design the system so that this filtering process cannot be bypassed and is always used.

It must also enforce the filtering result using:
- Permission rules (who is allowed to send or receive information), and
- Policy rules (what types of content are allowed).

Finally, it must keep clear documentation and audit records showing that the filtering process ran, what decision was made, and whether the transfer was allowed or blocked.

##### Non-bypassable linear content filtering for cross-domain transfers

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define and publish cross-domain transfer scope (protocols/interfaces/data paths) and map each to a single inspection path; produce an architecture diagram and routing matrix | Security Architect | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design the non-bypassable choke point: select/confirm inspection gateway/proxy pattern (active/standby if required) and define network routing/firewall/SD-WAN rules so the gateway is the only permitted ingress/egress path | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement strictly linear gateway pipeline (single ordered chain) with normalise → decode → classify → scan → policy-evaluate → enforce; configure fail-closed behaviour and remove/disable any parallel/bypassable branches | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £18,000 |
| Implement discretionary enforcement (sender/receiver authorisation) by integrating enterprise IdP claims and RBAC/ABAC context into gateway policy evaluation | IAM Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement mandatory enforcement (allow/deny/quarantine) and ensure mandatory deny/quarantine cannot be overridden by discretionary allow; add explicit policy precedence and test cases | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Guarantee non-invocation: validate all configured transfer flows traverse the same linear pipeline; implement reachability controls to prevent alternate routes (including egress bypass checks) and document results | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Configure audit-ready evidence: per-transfer logging (discretionary outcome, mandatory decision, final action, invocation metadata/correlation IDs), SIEM forwarding, and retention alignment; produce sample audit log pack | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £6,000 |
| Execute end-to-end testing and acceptance evidence: representative traffic types, fail-closed verification, regression tests for bypass attempts, and sign-off pack for AC-4(28) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 264h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £24,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and document which systems the application can transfer data to across different domains, including the specific communication methods, interfaces, and data routes. For each one, assign one inspection route.
- [ ] Set up a dedicated inspection gateway (or proxy) as the only allowed entry and exit point between security zones, using firewall, routing, and software-defined wide area network (SD-WAN) rules.
- [ ] Set the gateway inspection to run in a strict, step-by-step order, and make it fail closed if any inspection error occurs.
- [ ] Integrate information about the user’s identity into the gateway, so that discretionary permission decisions are assessed together with the required content and classification rules.
- [ ] Apply required policy results (block or quarantine) so they cannot be overridden by optional “allow” decisions.
- [ ] Disable or remove any parallel or alternate inspection routes that check the same type of data, and confirm that all traffic goes through the single, linear processing pipeline.
- [ ] Enable and keep audit logs that record, for every transfer attempt: the gateway request, the discretionary decision, the mandatory content decision, and the final enforcement action.
