#### AC-4.29 — Filter Orchestration Engines (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that when information is shared between different parts of the organisation that have different protection rules, it is checked in a coordinated, step-by-step way, and that the checking process finishes properly. Without this, checks could fail without anyone noticing, stop part-way through, or run in the wrong order—allowing unsafe or incorrect information to pass, or leaving the organisation unable to show what happened.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must use a coordinating “orchestration” system for these cross-domain transfers. This system must ensure that content checks run to completion without errors (including unexpected stopping or unusual behaviour), that each check is carried out in the approved order, and that the actions follow the organisation’s approved cross-domain data handling policy. The system must also produce clear completion reports showing that the checks succeeded in the required sequence, so that anyone reviewing the records can confirm the process worked as intended.

##### Orchestrate cross-domain content filtering with ordered completion reports

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Design deterministic workflow definitions per transfer type (intake → classify → filter/scan → transform/quarantine → deliver → finalise), including workflow versioning model and stage identifiers | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement single cross-domain transfer entrypoint and routing enforcement (remove/disable bypass paths; ensure all transfers invoke orchestration engine) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Build orchestration engine core: ordered stage execution, dependency/state management, idempotency controls, and stage transition persistence | Software Lead | Enterprise | 80h | — |
| Implement orchestration error semantics: detect anomalous actions/unexpected termination/timeouts; mark run as failed; suppress successful completion reports; emit failure evidence | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement audit-ready completion evidence generation: stage reports + final completion report with transfer ID, workflow version, ordered stage statuses, timestamps, and execution-path consistency checks | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Integrate logs and completion reports into central logging/SIEM with tamper-evident/immutable retention (including event schema, correlation IDs, and access controls) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £25,000 |
| Establish controlled change and governance for workflow/policy updates: version control integration, approval gates, automated checks to prevent unapproved step-sequence changes, and release pipeline enforcement | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort**: 272h  
**Total Estimated Cost**: £25,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the order of steps for each workflow, for every cross-domain transfer type, mapped to the approved cross-domain data handling policy.
- [ ] Set up one single transfer entry point across all domains, so that every transfer is routed through the content filtering orchestration engine.
- [ ] Set up orchestration controls to ensure stages run in the correct order and to stop tasks from running out of sequence.
- [ ] Set up failure handling so that any unusual actions or unexpected stopping or timeouts cause the run to be marked as failed, and prevent sending reports that indicate successful completion.
- [ ] For each transfer, produce a stage-by-stage report and a final completion report. Each report must include the transfer ID, the workflow version, the status of each stage in the order they occurred, and the relevant timestamps.
- [ ] Add orchestration run logs and completion reports to a central logging system and security information and event management (SIEM), and store them with immutable or tamper-evident retention.
- [ ] Store workflow and policy definitions in version control and require formal change-management approval before updating the step sequence.


---

#### AC-4.30 — Filter Mechanisms Using Multiple Processes (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that when information is moved between separate security areas, it is checked for unsafe or unwanted content using more than one independent checking step. This way, if one check fails, it does not automatically allow harmful material to pass through.

Without this, a single broken or bypassed check could create a weak point, allowing harmful files, messages, or data to reach the wrong area. This could lead to fraud, disruption, or the exposure of sensitive information.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly state in its information-sharing rules that transfers between security areas use multiple independent content checks. It must also create and follow step-by-step procedures that explain how the checks are carried out and what happens if one check fails. In addition, it must configure its systems so the multiple checks are actually applied, keep records showing that the checks were completed during transfers, and include this approach and the responsible roles in the organisation’s security plan.

##### Dual-engine content filtering for cross-domain transfers

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define cross-domain transfer paths and domain boundary rules (scope list, enforcement points, and “different security domains” mapping) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design multi-process filtering architecture (Engine A + Engine B), including independent configuration objects, health checks, log identifiers, and verdict logic (AND/quorum) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement enforcement pipeline changes at each scoped transfer path (service/process separation, correlation ID propagation, per-engine invocation and timeouts) | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 72h | — |
| Configure non-bypass decision rule and failure handling (block/quarantine on timeout/unavailability; no silent fallback; deterministic outcomes) | Security Engineer | Business Unit | 32h | — |
| Implement audit evidence model and logging (per-transfer correlation ID with per-engine verdicts, reason codes, timestamps, engine versions/config IDs, failure indicators) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Integrate with SIEM/SOC workflows (log ingestion validation, dashboards/alerts for blocked/quarantined transfers and engine failures, sample queries for audit evidence) | Operations Lead | Department | 24h | £6,000 |
| Update system security plan and operating procedures (workflow, escalation/incident handling, engine down runbook, testing/verification approach) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 240h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £6,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify every route where data can move between different security domains, and clearly define the security-domain boundaries each route passes through.
- [ ] Set up a filtering pipeline with multiple processes at the point where enforcement happens, using at least two separate engines or stages that work independently.
- [ ] Set the final decision rule to **AND/quorum** and to **block/quarantine** if any engine fails or times out.
- [ ] Set up logging for each transfer that records, for every engine used, the engine’s decision (verdict), the reason for that decision, the time it happened, and which engine produced it.
- [ ] Update the system security plan and create procedures for the multi-step filtering process and what to do when it fails.
- [ ] Use test cases to confirm that the bypass cannot happen if one engine is unavailable, and that audit evidence is produced.


---

#### AC-4.31 — Failed Content Transfer Prevention (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that when information is shared between different parts of your organisation, anything that does not meet the required checks is stopped at the boundary and never reaches the other side. Without this, a corrupted or unsafe item could pass through and then be stored, processed, or used in the receiving area, which could lead to damage, errors, or further security problems.

To meet this expectation, your organisation must:
- clearly identify which information transfers move between separate security areas;
- make sure the system completes the required checks before any transfer is allowed to finish; and
- block any item that does not pass the checks so it is not delivered in any form.

You also need to document the rule and how it is enforced, explain how the system is designed to stop failed items, configure the relevant settings, keep evidence of those settings, and retain records showing that failed transfers were blocked. Named staff must be responsible for overseeing and maintaining this enforcement.

##### Reject-and-quarantine at cross-domain transfer boundaries

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Produce cross-domain transfer inventory and boundary/interface map (in-scope transfers, approved paths, send/receive semantics, and enforcement point placement) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define validation rule sets per interface (malware/content/type/size, schema validation, allow/deny lists, integrity/signature checks, classification/DLP checks) and document pass/fail outcomes | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Design and implement enforcement point per interface (gateway/proxy/relay/service) with pre-transfer validation and hard reject behaviour (no delivery to receiving domain) | Security Engineer | Department | 80h | — |
| Implement reject-and-quarantine workflow (isolated quarantine storage, access controls, retention, and secure retrieval for authorised security operations) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £18,000 |
| Ensure atomic delivery semantics and remove/avoid “queue then scan” patterns (transaction boundaries, idempotency, and commit-after-validation logic) | DevOps Lead | Business Unit | 40h | — |
| Implement audit evidence generation and SIEM integration (transfer ID, sender identity, destination domain, interface, validation rule(s), outcome; dashboards and alerting for bypass attempts) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £6,000 |
| Prevent bypass and enforce routing controls (network/service allowlisting, disable direct routes, configuration hardening, and automated detection/alerting on misrouting) | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort | 320h | Total Estimated Cost | £24,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Take an inventory of all cross-domain transfer interfaces used by the application, map how data moves between them, and define the approved routes for those transfers.
- [ ] Set up a boundary control point (gateway, proxy, relay, or service) for each interface, and make sure every data transfer goes through it.
- [ ] Set up checks before data is transferred for each transfer type, such as malware/content/type checks, verifying the data matches the expected format, using allow-lists and deny-lists, and confirming the data’s integrity and any digital signatures.
- [ ] Set up a “reject and quarantine” process so any failed content is rejected and never sent to the receiving organisation, with the quarantine kept isolated from the receiver.
- [ ] Ensure delivery is all-or-nothing, so the receiver only accepts and saves the content after it has passed validation successfully.
- [ ] Turn on audit logging for every attempted transfer, recording the transfer ID, sender, destination domain, the validation rule(s) applied, and whether the transfer was blocked or rejected.
- [ ] Block or detect any bypass routes that get around the enforcement point, and raise an alert when a bypass attempt is made.


---

#### AC-4.32 — Process Requirements for Information Transfer (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure information moves between different parts of your organisation only after it has been properly checked, and that it is sent on unchanged. Without this, sensitive or restricted information could be sent to the wrong place, or be handled incorrectly because the instructions for how it should be treated were wrong or incomplete.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must use a transfer process that does not change or filter the message content during handover. It must, however, check that the “filtering instructions” or labels that describe what should happen are valid. The organisation should only forward the content after the associated filtering step has completed successfully, and then send the approved content to the next stage.

The transfer method should be kept as simple and limited as possible, with built-in checks to show it is working correctly. This should be supported by clear procedures, design and configuration records, and audit logs.

##### Immutable payload transfer with metadata validation and success gating

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the immutable information-flow contract (payload + metadata/envelope) including required fields, versioning, and byte-for-byte pass-through rules | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Establish metadata trust model and validation approach (e.g., signed metadata or trusted policy registry lookup), including allowed values, length limits, and schema constraints | Security Architect | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement transfer component core logic: immutable forwarding (no content transformation), strict schema validation, correlation binding enforcement, and destination mapping restrictions | Software Lead | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Integrate explicit success gating with filter pipeline completion signals (same correlation identifier), including fail/timeout/non-success handling and “never forward on failure” enforcement | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 40h | — |
| Add assurance evidence: auditable event records per transfer attempt (validation result, correlation match result, filter success/failure, destination hand-off timestamp) and retention alignment | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Build and run byte-for-byte verification harness (pre/post payload hash comparison), plus negative tests for metadata validation failures and gating failures | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 32h | — |
| Produce deployment/configuration package and operational runbook (minimal code/config, monitoring hooks, alerting guidance, and change-management artefacts) | Operations Lead | Department | 24h | — |
| Implement security review artefacts (threat model update, code/config review checklist, and evidence pack mapping to AC-4(32) assurance expectations) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 276h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define an unchangeable message body, and a separate agreement for how the supporting information (envelope) is sent, including a correlation identifier, a filter policy identifier and version, and the destination pipeline identifier.
- [ ] Implement strict checks that the metadata follows the required format and is trustworthy (for example, by using signed metadata or by looking up the policy in a trusted policy registry) in the transfer component.
- [ ] Add correlation binding checks so the metadata correlation identifier must match the payload processing context before any forwarding decision is made.
- [ ] Connect to the filtering stage so it reports a clear success or failure result using the same correlation identifier, and forward the block unless success is received.
- [ ] Set up the transfer component to forward data exactly as received, with no changes to the content (use a byte-by-byte comparison in tests).
- [ ] For each transfer attempt, record the audit evidence (the result of the metadata check, whether it matched the expected correlation, the result of any filtering, and the time the transfer was handed off to the destination).
- [ ] Set up automated tests and monitoring alerts to detect these failure types: forward-without-success, metadata validation failure, and correlation mismatch.


---

### AC-5 — Separation of Duties (Control)

This expectation ensures that the same people do not both (1) have control of powerful systems and (2) approve or check the evidence that those controls were used correctly. Without this separation, one person could quietly change who has access, alter the rules that control access, and then review the records in a way that conceals wrongdoing—whether accidental or deliberate—across all systems covered by the organisation’s policy.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must clearly identify and document who is responsible for three separate duties:  
- administering privileged access  
- making security policy or role changes  
- reviewing and approving audit log information  

The organisation must then set up access permissions so these duties are separated in practice. This includes ensuring that no single person is authorised to both administer privileged access and review or approve audit logs. Where required, the same separation rules must also apply to security policy or role changes, across all relevant systems and components.

##### Enforce separation of duties for privileged admin, policy change, audit approval

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the organisation-defined SoD matrix for the application scope (prod/test/DR as applicable), including the three duty types and mapped role/team ownership | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Document explicit “no-overlap” rules (Privileged Admin vs Audit Reviewer/Approver; Privileged Admin vs Policy/Role Change where required), including exception criteria, risk acceptance, compensating controls, and time limits | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 12h | — |
| Perform in-scope role/person mapping assessment and gap analysis (current access, policy change permissions, audit review permissions) and produce a remediation plan | Project Manager | Business Unit | 20h | — |
| Configure identity/authorisation controls to enforce duty separation (role/group assignments and least-privilege) across all in-scope environments; include evidence-ready configuration exports | Security Engineer | Department | 24h | — |
| Implement distinct workflows for privileged actions and policy/role changes (ticketing/GRC routing) ensuring approver/reviewer identity differs from executor; ensure workflow records capture approver identity, timestamps, and evidence links | Platform Engineer | Department | 28h | — |
| Implement audit log review/approval workflow and restrict access to “Audit Reviewer/Approver” only (read/approval permissions limited to audit evidence and workflow actions) | Operations Lead | Department | 16h | — |
| Establish periodic SoD verification and evidence generation (monthly/quarterly cadence), including exception register maintenance and auditable reporting stored in the GRC repository | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort | 156h | Total Estimated Cost | £0 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a separation-of-duties matrix that lists the application’s in-scope environments and shows how the three types of responsibilities are assigned to specific named roles or teams.
- [ ] Define and get approval for clear “no overlap” rules between privileged access administration and audit log review or approval (and any required policy or role changes). Include the criteria for exceptions and the compensating controls to use when an exception is granted.
- [ ] Set up identity permissions so that **Privileged Administrator** roles cannot access audit log review or approval functions, and so that **Audit Reviewer/Approver** roles cannot manage privileged access.
- [ ] Route requests for privileged actions and changes to security policy or roles through separate ticket and workflow approvals, with the people approving different from the people carrying out the work.
- [ ] Carry out an initial and ongoing segregation of duties (SoD) conflict check across all in-scope systems and components, and record the results (including any approved exceptions) in the governance, risk and compliance (GRC) repository.
- [ ] Store audit-ready evidence: segregation of duties (SoD) matrix, exports of access authorisation settings, workflow approval records, and records of approved exceptions.


---

### AC-6 — Least Privilege (Control)

This requirement is about making sure people and automated tasks only have the access they genuinely need to do their jobs, and no more. Without this, a mistake or misuse could allow someone to view, change, or damage information or systems they were never meant to use. It could also cause wider harm if an automated task is compromised.  

To meet this expectation, the organisation must have a clear, written least-privilege rule and keep it up to date. It must also have step-by-step procedures for requesting, approving, changing, and removing access. The organisation must keep a current, documented record of what each person is allowed to do, and configure systems so they match that record.  

The organisation must also document and keep up to date the system settings, keep relevant records of access activity for review, and maintain a plan that shows how least-privilege is applied—including ensuring background processes run with no higher permissions than they need.

##### Least-privilege RBAC with JIT elevation and access matrix evidence

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Produce authoritative role/permission catalogue for the application (fine-grained permissions, task-to-permission mapping, minimum-data/functionality definitions) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define and publish access authorisation list (access matrix) template and governance workflow (justification, approver, environment scope, expiry rules for privileged roles) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement IdP role/group claims and conditional access rules to enforce access to application UI endpoints and APIs per access matrix (incl. environment separation) | IAM Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £8,000 |
| Implement server-side authorisation checks in the application (authorisation middleware/guards; deny-by-default; ensure APIs and admin consoles validate claims/roles) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Implement JIT time-bound privileged elevation workflow for admin functions (approval-based, logged, automatic revocation at expiry; least-privilege elevation scopes) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £12,000 |
| Implement least-privilege for user-context actions and background jobs (no privilege escalation; OAuth scope/claim inheritance rules; dedicated service identities with narrowly scoped permissions per job) | Platform Engineer | Department | 32h | — |
| Centralise and harden audit-ready evidence generation (authorisation decision logging where feasible, role/group changes, JIT elevation events with expiry, admin actions; SIEM integration and retention controls) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 28h | £6,000 |
| Run end-to-end validation and evidence pack for AC-6 (test cases, access matrix reconciliation, privileged access scenarios, audit review readiness) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| **Total Estimated Effort** |  |  | **272h** |  |
| **Total Estimated Cost** |  |  |  | **£26,000** |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and approve an application role and permission list, including the reasons for each permission and the minimum data and functions each role can access.
- [ ] Create and keep an up-to-date access authorisation list (access matrix) for each environment, and link it to identity provider (IdP) groups and roles.
- [ ] Set up the organisation’s identity provider to include users’ roles and permissions in its access information, and apply conditional access rules for the application.
- [ ] Carry out authorisation checks on the server for every user interface action and every application programming interface (API) endpoint, based on the mapped roles and permissions.
- [ ] Set up just-in-time (JIT) privileged access for administrative tasks, where access is approved in advance, lasts only for a limited time, is automatically removed afterwards, and all activity is recorded in logs.
- [ ] Provide dedicated service accounts for background jobs, and ensure actions that run in a user’s context only have the same access rights as the user who started them.
- [ ] Set up centralised audit logs for sign-ins, changes to roles or groups, requests to gain elevated (privileged) access, and administrative actions. Limit access to these logs to authorised reviewers only.


---

#### AC-6.1 — Authorize Access to Security Functions (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that only a small, named group of trusted roles can access and change the security tools that protect your systems and decide who is allowed in. Without this, the wrong people could quietly weaken key defences, change the rules that block unwanted network traffic, alter how suspicious activity is detected, switch off or tamper with what is recorded for investigations, or change the information used to manage encryption keys—leaving the organisation exposed to fraud, data theft, and attacks that go undetected.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must explicitly authorise only the following roles to manage the security functions used for access decisions: System Security Officer, Security Administrator, System Administrator, System Programmer, and Privileged Access Manager. This includes managing hardware and software protections and the related firmware settings, as well as security-relevant configuration information such as firewall and router access rules, detection settings, audit recording settings, and encryption key management details.

The organisation must document who is allowed to do this, keep clear procedures that follow the principle of giving only the minimum access needed, set up system accounts and permissions accordingly, and keep records showing the authorisations and the system audit trail for changes.

##### PAM-gated RBAC for security functions and security-relevant configs

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define scope of “security functions” and “security-relevant information” categories for the target estate (firewall/router ACLs, IDS/IPS parameters, SIEM audit-event settings, cryptographic key management metadata; plus hardware/software/firmware access points) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Produce authorisation matrix mapping the five privileged roles to allowed actions (view vs change) per security-function category and security-relevant information category | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| PAM broker policy design and implementation plan: enforce PAM-mediated access for all administrative sessions to the identified security-function interfaces (including hardware/software/firmware where technically accessible) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Configure PAM broker enforcement and session recording/command logging for the relevant admin entry points; integrate recorded logs with SIEM forwarding | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £25,000 |
| Implement target-side RBAC for each security function so only PAM-managed identities can perform configuration changes (firewall/router, IDS/IPS, SIEM admin settings, OS security configuration services) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £10,000 |
| Implement cryptographic key metadata change restrictions so only Privileged Access Manager and System Security Officer (or equivalent mapping) can modify key-management metadata and related HSM configuration | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Denial handling and auditability: ensure non-authorised attempts are denied and logged end-to-end; validate SIEM audit-event setting changes are restricted to authorised roles | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Evidence and change control: store authorisation matrix and PAM policy configuration in version control with approval workflow; define evidence retention and produce an audit-ready pack template | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 244h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £35,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a role-to-action authorisation matrix showing what each of the five privileged roles is allowed to do for every security function and for each category of security-relevant information.
- [ ] Connect all security administration systems—hardware security modules (HSM), firewalls and routers, intrusion detection and prevention systems (IDS/IPS), security information and event management (SIEM), endpoint security, and operating system security configuration services—to a privileged access management (PAM) broker.
- [ ] Set up privileged access management (PAM) rules so that only authorised roles can make configuration changes. Deny configuration-change access by default for all other roles.
- [ ] Set up role-based access control (RBAC) on the target systems so that only identities managed by privileged access management (PAM) can change firewall and router access control lists (ACLs), intrusion detection system/intrusion prevention system (IDS/IPS) settings, security information and event management (SIEM) audit-event settings, and information about cryptographic keys.
- [ ] Turn on session recording and command logging for all privileged access management (PAM)-mediated security administration, and send the logs to the security information and event management (SIEM) system.
- [ ] Limit changes to cryptographic key details to the Privileged Access Manager and the System Security Officer, and document how responsibilities are separated between them.
- [ ] Store the privileged access management (PAM) policy and the authorisation matrix in version control, using an approval workflow, and keep audit records showing who approved access and any changes made.


---

#### AC-6.2 — Non-privileged Access for Nonsecurity Functions (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making sure that people who can see sensitive security information or use security tools do not use their highest level of access when they are doing routine, non-security work. The real-world risk is that if someone uses a highly privileged account for everyday tasks, a mistake, misuse, or compromise could expose security records or settings. This could make it easier for an attacker to hide their actions or change protections.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly document:
- which security-related information and security tools are covered (including audit logs, security monitoring screens, and security configuration settings), and
- which user accounts or roles can access them.

It must also define what counts as non-privileged access and what counts as non-security tasks. The system must then be configured so that access to non-security functions is only allowed when the person is using a non-privileged account, or—where roles are used—an equivalent non-privileged role.

The organisation must document the approach, assign responsibilities to the right staff, configure the system to enforce it, and keep records showing that the rule is being followed.

##### Enforce non-privileged role for nonsecurity functions

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Create covered-scope mapping: classify application endpoints/workflows into (a) security functions/security-relevant information and (b) nonsecurity functions; define privileged vs non-privileged role taxonomy for the covered scope | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design RBAC/authorisation separation: specify required authorisation checks for every nonsecurity endpoint/workflow when user holds any covered privileged security role | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement application/API enforcement: add endpoint-level authorisation rules and deny-by-default behaviour for nonsecurity functions under covered privileged roles | Software Lead | Department | 56h | — |
| Implement role switching with equivalent assurance: configure IdP/app session controls so nonsecurity access requires the equivalent non-privileged role (including MFA/device/session posture parity) and only authorisation scope changes | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Prevent privileged session reuse: ensure privileged-role tokens/sessions cannot access nonsecurity endpoints (separate entitlements/authorisation checks; no “privileged session is sufficient” paths) | Security Engineer | Department | 32h | — |
| Configure audit evidence pipeline: emit IdP + application logs for each nonsecurity access attempt (identity, role/entitlement used, target category, allowed/denied) and route to SIEM with required retention and query fields | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £3,000 |
| Test, validate, and produce audit-ready evidence pack: create test cases, run regression/security tests across environments, and document control effectiveness and evidence queries for auditors | Quality Assurance Lead | Business Unit | 32h | — |
| Operationalise governance: implement policy-as-code/config management for role mapping and endpoint category assignments; establish change-control workflow and periodic review checklist | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | £2,500 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 280h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £5,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an official inventory tool that maps each application endpoint and workflow to either the security functions and information that are covered, or to non-security functions.
- [ ] Define which users have privileged access and which users have non-privileged access in the identity provider (IdP) for the security functions and information covered.
- [ ] Set up application and application programming interface (API) gateway authorisation so that, when users have covered security roles, any non-security functions can only be accessed using non-privileged roles.
- [ ] Set up role switching rules so that non-security access is allowed only when it runs under the same non-privileged role, with the same session assurance controls.
- [ ] For non-security endpoints, do not reuse privileged roles or sessions. Instead, check that the user is authorised for the specific role on every request.
- [ ] Set up and centralise audit records that capture each user’s identity, the role they used, the function category, and whether access was allowed or denied, so the information can be used as evidence for generated reports.
- [ ] Add policy-as-code and change-management controls for updates to role mappings and endpoint category assignments.


---

#### AC-6.3 — Network Access to Privileged Commands (Enhancement)

This requirement is about letting trusted staff make important system changes remotely, but only when there is a real and urgent need. If the rules are not strict, someone could use remote access to run powerful commands when they should not, which could lead to service outages, data loss, or unauthorised changes that are difficult to trace.

The organisation must decide which remote methods are allowed for running system administration commands (for example, approved tools such as `sudo`, PowerShell remoting, or approved vendor administration tools). It must also allow network-based access to those commands only for 24 hours a day, 7 days a week on-call support for time-critical incident response and maintenance when it is not practical to attend the device locally.

The organisation must record the reason for granting this remote access in the system’s security plan, including the specific operational need that justifies it.

##### Policy-gated PAM/remote admin for approved privileged commands

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| PAM/ZTNA architecture design for tool-anchored privileged command execution (command profile model, session flow, and policy gate points) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Build approved privileged command inventory per target system (sudoers/PowerShell remoting/vendor CLI profiles) and define “approved command profiles” mapping to workflows | Security Engineer | Department | 32h | — |
| Configure PAM/ZTNA to restrict remote privileged access to approved command profiles only (no ad-hoc shells; enforce workflow binding) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement policy gate logic for authorisation (24x7 on-call roster check, time-critical incident/maintenance attestation, local access impracticality evidence, ticket/incident reference capture) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 28h | — |
| Enable command-level audit logging and evidence capture (justification fields, executed command profile, requester identity, system, timestamps, ticket reference; retention and export to SIEM) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Integrate with SIEM/log export and validate audit record completeness (test cases for allowed/denied sessions; evidence review workflow) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Update system security plan for each affected system (document operational need definition, local access impracticality basis, tooling/workflow mapping, and how rationale is retained) | Data Protection Officer | Department | 20h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 204h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] For each system, list and confirm the approved “privileged command” profiles and the approved remote tools that run them.
- [ ] Set up privileged access management (PAM) and zero trust network access (ZTNA) to route all network-based privileged command sessions, and allow execution only for the approved command profiles.
- [ ] Set up a check at the start of a session to confirm the user is on the on-call roster, that the request is linked to a time-critical incident or planned maintenance, and that there is a documented reason why local access is not practical, including a ticket or incident reference.
- [ ] Enable and keep detailed audit records at the command level, showing the user’s identity, the target system, the command that was run, and the reason for running it.
- [ ] Update each affected system’s security plan to record the approved operational reasons for the approach (24 hours a day, 7 days a week on-call support; responses and maintenance that must happen quickly; and that local access is not practical). Also, point to the workflow that has been put in place and the sources of supporting evidence.
- [ ] Test and confirm that direct remote administrator access routes (for example, unrestricted remote shells or administrator network ports) are blocked, or cannot be used to run privileged commands outside the approved privileged access management (PAM) and zero trust network access (ZTNA) process.


---

#### AC-6.4 — Separate Processing Domains (Enhancement)

This requirement is about keeping different parts of a system clearly separated, so people only have the permissions they genuinely need for the specific area they are working on. Without this separation, a user who has extra rights in one area could potentially use them to access other areas, or even the underlying platform that runs the system. This increases the risk of unauthorised changes, data exposure, or wider impact if something goes wrong.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must design and set up the system using separate, isolated processing areas (for example, separate virtual machines, separate physical environments, or other built-in isolation methods). It must also ensure that permissions do not carry over between these areas, or to the underlying platform.

The organisation must document the access rules and the principle of least privilege, keep clear records of the system design and configuration that show the separation is in place, and maintain audit records of domain access and any changes to privileges. It must also include the approach and responsibilities in the system security plan, naming the people responsible for defining least-privilege access, supported by information security and system developers.

##### Isolated VM domains with enforced privilege boundaries

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define processing domain model (e.g., App/Data/Admin domains) and produce boundary documentation, including admin-task mapping and explicit “no shared admin” rules | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design and implement VM/cluster layout per domain (separate resource groups/projects, dedicated VM templates, placement rules) and establish secure baseline configuration for each domain | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 56h | £6,000 |
| Harden management plane access: restrict hypervisor console/API/host login to dedicated privileged identities; remove/deny normal user paths to host credentials and management sockets | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £2,500 |
| Implement network segmentation with default-deny between domains: create virtual network topology, security groups/ACLs, and allow-list only required application/data flows; block cross-domain administrative protocols | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £3,000 |
| Implement domain-scoped least-privilege RBAC/OS groups: create per-domain admin roles, service account separation, and enforce that Domain A admins cannot administer Domain B (including credential/group checks) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Build infrastructure-as-code and policy-as-code automation to prevent drift: codify VM hardening baselines, network rules, and RBAC assignments; add CI/CD validation gates | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 64h | £8,000 |
| Enable audit evidence collection and central logging: configure hypervisor management-plane logs, domain access attempts, and privilege/role change events; set retention and produce an audit-ready evidence pack | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | £5,000 |
| Run validation and acceptance testing: perform cross-domain access tests, lateral movement attempts, and management-plane access verification; document results against acceptance criteria | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 336h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £23,500

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a domain map that assigns business functions and administrative tasks to separate virtual machines (VMs) (or VM clusters), with clearly documented boundaries.
- [ ] Limit access to the hypervisor management controls to a dedicated group of privileged users, and block any host access routes for users who are not authorised for management.
- [ ] Set up virtual network segmentation so that traffic between different network areas is blocked by default, and then allow only the specific application and data connections that are explicitly required.
- [ ] Set up domain-local role-based access control (RBAC) and operating system (OS) groups so that administrative roles are limited to each domain and cannot administer other domains.
- [ ] Use infrastructure-as-code and policy-as-code to enforce virtual machine hardening, network access control lists (ACLs), and domain-limited administrator role assignments, and to enable detection of configuration changes (drift).
- [ ] Turn on and centralise audit logs for attempts to access domains, changes to privileges or roles, and actions in the hypervisor management interface; check that these logs are reviewed in a security information and event management (SIEM) system.


---

#### AC-6.5 — Privileged Accounts (Enhancement)

This expectation is about keeping control of the system’s keys tightly restricted to the right people. If ordinary staff were able to use powerful administrator or super-user accounts, they could accidentally or intentionally change security settings, access sensitive information, or leave the system in an unsafe condition.  

To prevent this, the organisation must ensure that every privileged account on the system—including any built-in super-user accounts—can be used only by the authorised system administrator role and the authorised information system security officer (ISSO) role.  

The organisation must also be able to show this in practice by keeping clear written rules for who is allowed privileged access, step-by-step procedures for granting and removing only the minimum access needed, an up-to-date list of all system-generated privileged accounts, a current list of authorised administrators, documentation of the system settings that enforce these limits, and retained records that show privileged activity.  

Finally, the organisation must include this approach in the system’s security plan and keep the supporting records, so it can demonstrate that privileged access is ongoing and limited.

##### Restrict privileged accounts to System Admin and ISSO roles

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define authoritative privileged roles (System Administrator and ISSO) in the enterprise IdP and document the mapping to privileged capabilities | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement/adjust authorisation enforcement for privileged actions so only identities in the authorised roles can exercise privileged capabilities (including application admin endpoints and admin APIs) | Software Lead | Department | 24h | — |
| Inventory privileged accounts across environments (built-in/super-user, local admin, OS/app admin, service accounts) and classify as identity-backed vs system-generated; produce an auditable inventory register | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Disable/lock down built-in/super-user accounts where feasible; where not feasible, implement compensating controls (strong authentication, controlled credential management, break-glass governed by authorised roles) | Infrastructure Lead | Business Unit | 24h | — |
| Implement JIT/JEA elevation for privileged actions where supported (time-bound access, approval/justification, attribution to authorised role holder) | DevOps Lead | Department | 24h | — |
| Configure audit evidence generation: ensure privileged session logs and administrative action logs are forwarded to SIEM and retained; validate log fields include role/identity attribution | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 20h | £3,000 |
| Execute technical validation and access testing (attempt privileged actions with non-authorised identities; verify denial, attribution, and audit trail completeness across prod/test environments) | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 16h | — |
| Update governance artefacts (system security plan/access control procedures) to reflect the privileged-account restriction rule and the operational process for granting/revoking privileged access | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 12h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 168h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £3,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create or confirm the official identity provider (IdP) roles for “System Administrator” and “information system security officer (ISSO)”, and make sure all high-privilege permissions are assigned only to these two roles.
- [ ] Identify and list every privileged account on the system, including built-in super-user accounts, and record its current status (enabled, disabled, or locked) and the specific way it can be used to access the system.
- [ ] Where possible, disable or restrict built-in “super-user” accounts. If this is not feasible, use controlled sign-in rules and ensure these accounts are used only for the authorised roles.
- [ ] Remove standing privileged access from all users who are not authorised, and require role-based, time-limited permission increases for privileged actions where this is supported.
- [ ] Set up administrative endpoints and functions so they allow only users in the authorised roles, and block everyone else.
- [ ] Set up and confirm logging of privileged sessions and administrative actions in the security information and event management (SIEM) system, so that every log entry can be traced back to the authorised person performing the role.
- [ ] Publish and keep up to date an auditable list of privileged accounts and the authorised privileged administrators or staff, aligned to the two roles.


---

#### AC-6.6 — Privileged Access by Non-organizational Users (Enhancement)

This expectation is about ensuring that only trusted people can carry out high-level, sensitive system tasks, and that no one outside the organisation is ever given those powers. Without this, a contractor, visitor, or other person who is not an employee could accidentally or deliberately change security settings, view confidential information, or take control of the system, causing serious financial, legal, and reputational harm.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must clearly define:
- what counts as privileged access, and
- what a non-organisational user is.

It must then create and follow rules that explicitly prevent non-organisational users from being given any privileged role or account.

The organisation must also:
- keep up-to-date lists of non-organisational users and any system-created privileged accounts,
- configure the system so these privileges cannot be assigned to non-organisational users,
- include this restriction in its system plans, and
- keep audit records showing that attempts are blocked.

Finally, it should regularly check that privileged access assignments match the lists, and review the audit records to confirm that no successful privileged access occurred.

##### Block non-organisational users from privileged roles via IdP + PAM

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Confirm privileged role definition and mapping to application admin/security actions (including APIs, admin consoles, and security configuration endpoints) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Define authoritative “organisational vs non-organisational” identity attribute model (e.g., employee-equivalent flag) and data sourcing/ownership for the attribute | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement IdP conditional access/authorisation rules to deny privileged role assignment to non-organisational users (default deny; no manual exceptions) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Configure IdP-to-application authorisation integration so privileged groups/roles are only issued when the organisational attribute is present and valid | IAM Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement PAM enforcement for privileged actions: step-up authentication, privileged token/session issuance only via PAM, and hard block for non-organisational users | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Integrate IdP and PAM so elevation requests are evaluated against the same organisational attribute (including deny logic and consistent error handling) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Enable audit logging and evidence package: privileged role assignment attempts, PAM elevation requests, privileged session lifecycle, and denied attempts; configure SIEM alerts and retention | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | £12,000 |
| Execute test and acceptance validation (test window, negative/positive cases, evidence review, and sign-off that no successful privileged access occurs for non-organisational users) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 220h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £12,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and document which application roles and permissions count as privileged access for enforcing AC-6(6)
- [ ] Create or confirm an official identity provider (IdP) attribute that shows “employee-equivalent” status. This information must come from human resources (HR) or the workforce system and be controlled through approved processes.
- [ ] Set up identity provider (IdP) access rules so that, by default, non-organisational users are blocked from being assigned privileged roles or groups.
- [ ] Connect the application’s administrative functions to privileged access management (PAM) so that privileged user sessions are handled through PAM and users must complete an additional verification step (step-up authentication) before gaining access.
- [ ] Set up privileged access management (PAM) eligibility so that permission to elevate access requests is granted only when the identity provider (IdP) employee-equivalent attribute shows the user is an organisational user.
- [ ] Enable and keep audit logs for attempts to assign privileged roles, requests to elevate to privileged access, activity during privileged sessions, and any denials.
- [ ] Run a controlled test to prove that a user who is not part of the organisation cannot gain privileged access, and that any access denials are recorded in logs.


---

#### AC-6.7 — Review of User Privileges (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that only the right people and automated services have the highest level of access, and that this access is still justified. Over time, roles change, systems are updated or retired, and business needs shift. If higher access is left in place without regular checks, it increases the risk that someone could do more than they should—either by mistake or misuse—potentially resulting in unauthorised changes or damage.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must review, at least every 90 days, the access privileges held by privileged users, system administrators, and service accounts with elevated access. For each one, it must confirm whether the access is still needed for the organisation’s mission and business needs, and promptly remove or reassign privileges that are no longer required.

The organisation must also keep clear records of what was reviewed, the reasons for each decision, and any privilege removals or reassignments. These records must be supported by the organisation’s documented access rules and its least-privilege approach.

##### 90-day privileged access recertification with automated entitlement changes

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define in-scope privilege sources and entitlement mapping (privileged user roles/groups, system administrator roles, elevated service accounts, and system-generated identity-to-entitlement mappings) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design the 90-day recertification campaign model (scope rules, environment segmentation prod/test/DR, reviewer assignment logic, attestation data requirements, decision options) | Architect | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement automated entitlement enumeration and campaign roster generation (per environment/app; include direct privileges, roles, groups; ensure no blind spots) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £25,000 |
| Configure reviewer attestation workflow with mandatory rationale validation and decision capture (“still required” vs “remove/reduce”) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Build corrective action workflow (automated entitlement change where safe/approved; otherwise change request with approval gate; record deltas, timestamps, reviewer identity) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £10,000 |
| Generate audit-ready evidence packs per cycle (campaign roster, rationales/decisions, exceptions, proof of entitlement removals/reassignments; export format aligned to audit needs) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Operationalise ownership, escalation, and overdue handling (SLA timers, escalation paths, dashboards/alerts for pending corrective actions and overdue recertifications) | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort | 208h |  |
|---|---:|---:|
| Total Estimated Cost |  | £35,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and label all in-scope privileged users, system administrators, and elevated service accounts (including system-generated roles and classes) in identity and access management (IAM).
- [ ] Set up an identity and access management (IAM) access review programme to re-check permissions every 90 days for all in-scope access rights.
- [ ] Set mandatory reviewer sign-off fields for: the system or application, the privilege or role, an evidence-based reason for the decision, and the outcome (whether the access is still required or should be removed or reduced).
- [ ] Automate the removal or reduction of access rights for “remove” or “reduce” outcomes, or send the request through an approved change process with set deadlines that must be followed.
- [ ] Turn on audit logging and export evidence packs for each cycle (roster, decisions and reasons, changes to access rights, dates and times, and corrective actions).
- [ ] Assign clear responsible owners and set escalation rules for overdue reviews and outstanding corrective actions.

#### AC-6.8 — Privilege Levels for Code Execution (Enhancement)

This expectation is about preventing risky or unknown code from quietly gaining more access than the person who started it. If an unapproved or unsigned script, programme, or installer (including PowerShell, batch files, and Microsoft Installer (MSI) installers) is started using an elevated prompt, it must not end up running with higher privileges than the user who clicked to start it. Otherwise, a normal user could indirectly get access they are not authorised to have, which could lead to unauthorised changes, data theft, or a takeover of the system.

To meet this, the organisation must keep a documented list of software that is not allowed to run with higher privileges. This list must include anything unsigned or not approved. The organisation must also set clear rules that enforce this “no privilege gain” behaviour even when elevated prompts are used.

Named roles must be responsible for keeping the list and rules accurate. Information security must review and approve them. The system designs and settings must be documented and configured to enforce the restriction. Audit records must be kept to show that attempts are blocked and to record the outcomes.

##### Block unsigned/unapproved elevated execution via endpoint allowlisting

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define the “Approved/Prohibited Execution Catalogue” schema (publisher/signing certificate, hash, version, allowed execution context, file type mapping for PowerShell/batch/binary/MSI) and governance workflow for approvals/rejections | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Build initial catalogue population for the prohibited scope (identify candidate unsigned/unapproved items, define baseline prohibited categories, and register known-good approved admin tools/workflows) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Select and design the endpoint enforcement approach (e.g., Microsoft Defender Application Control / App Control for Business, or equivalent) including deny-by-default rules and “no privilege gain” evaluation model for elevated prompts | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement endpoint application control policies (deny-by-default for unsigned/unapproved PowerShell scripts, batch files, binaries, and MSI installers; allow only catalogue-approved identities; ensure evaluation applies under elevated tokens) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Integrate policy distribution and change control (policy-as-code/config management, staged rollout across environments, catalogue update pipeline with security review gates) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Configure telemetry and SIEM forwarding (blocked execution events, reason codes for signature/hash mismatch, process lineage, user/session context) and create alerting for repeated elevated execution attempts | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Execute validation and evidence pack (test matrix for standard vs elevated prompts across all prohibited categories; capture configuration baselines, approval records, and SIEM logs; produce audit-ready report) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 296h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish the prohibited scope for **ac-06.08_odp**, covering unsigned or unapproved **PowerShell scripts**, **batch files**, **binaries**, and **Microsoft Installer (MSI)** packages when they are run using elevated prompts.
- [ ] Create an approved list of approved execution items (including the publisher or signing certificate, a hash value, and the version), and set up a security review and approval process for any changes to that list.
- [ ] Set up endpoint application control to block the prohibited categories by default, and make sure the system checks these rules every time, even when users have elevated prompt permissions.
- [ ] Set up controlled processes for administrator actions so that legitimate privileged tasks are carried out using approved management tools and packages, rather than using ad-hoc elevated scripts or installers.
- [ ] Centralise and version the application control policy distribution (policy-as-code), with change control evidence.
- [ ] Send application control enforcement activity data to security information and event management (SIEM), and set up alerts for repeated blocked attempts to run elevated (higher-privilege) commands.
- [ ] For each prohibited category, run validation tests using both normal and higher-privilege prompts, and record the results as audit evidence.


---

#### AC-6.9 — Log Use of Privileged Functions (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure the organisation keeps a clear record of every time a high-privilege action is carried out on its systems. If high-privilege access is misused—whether by someone who should not have done it, by an insider making a mistake, or by an attacker who has taken over an account—the damage can be difficult to detect and even harder to investigate later.  

To meet this expectation, the organisation must first decide and document exactly which high-privilege actions must be tracked, and which types of events count as the official records to capture. The system then must automatically record an entry in its audit records every time one of those approved actions is carried out, and keep those records available for later review.  

Finally, the organisation must assign responsibility for reviewing these logs to the right people, and document in its security plan how logging and review will work.

- [ ] Enable built-in auditing on the operating system (OS) or host, the application, and the database components, so that every mapped privileged function produces audit records.
- [ ] Strengthen audit logging by limiting who can change audit settings and by preventing unauthorised attempts to clear or turn off logs
- [ ] Set up authenticated forwarding of privileged-function audit events to the central security information and event management (SIEM) or log system, using the minimum necessary permissions (least-privilege access).
- [ ] Document and keep up to date a mapping between privileged functions and event types, then check it using controlled test runs.
- [ ] Update the system security plan to include the audit sources, how events are mapped, the approach to keeping records, and who is responsible for reviewing logs.

#### AC-6.10 — Prohibit Non-privileged Users from Executing Privileged Functions (Enhancement)

This expectation is about preventing everyday users from carrying out powerful, high-risk actions that could weaken the protections around your systems. Without it, someone without the right permission could disable or get around key safeguards, create hidden user accounts, run checks that reveal whether someone has tampered with the system, or take control of the secret keys used to protect sensitive data—making it easier for fraud, theft, or unnoticed misuse to occur.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly document which actions are “privileged” (high-risk) and exactly which authorised people are allowed to carry out each one. It must also define who is considered “non-privileged” (not authorised for those actions). The system then must be configured so that non-privileged users are blocked from trying any privileged actions, including attempts to bypass security controls or protections against malicious code.

The organisation must also keep evidence that these protections are in place, record any attempts in system logs, include this in its security planning, and test that non-privileged attempts are consistently denied while authorised privileged users can perform only the permitted actions.

##### Enforce privileged-function allowlisting with JIT elevation

- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---|---:|---:|

| Define privileged role model in IdP (authorised privileged roles) and ensure non-privileged users cannot be assigned privileged roles (RBAC/ABAC policies, group/attribute rules) | IAM Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |

| Implement enforcement in application/admin interfaces and automation endpoints (deny-by-default authorisation checks; ensure privileged functions only callable via controlled admin workflows/broker sessions; remove/deny direct standard-user execution paths) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 56h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 240h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £3,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and get approval for a list of privileged functions, mapped to the specific administrative actions they perform across the application and supporting infrastructure.
- [ ] Assign each privileged function to its own dedicated privileged role in the enterprise identity provider (IdP), and make sure non-privileged users cannot be given those roles.
- [ ] Set up “step-up” authentication and just-in-time (JIT) permission increases for privileged roles, using a privileged access management (PAM)-style process.
- [ ] Set up “deny by default” access checks for all privileged administrative endpoints, application programming interfaces (APIs), and automated workflows.
- [ ] Limit privileged actions to approved administrator interfaces or brokers, and where possible remove direct access for standard users.
- [ ] Enable and centralise audit logs for both successful and denied attempts to use privileged functions, and send them to security information and event management (SIEM).
- [ ] Run test cases using non-privileged accounts to confirm that every privileged function is consistently blocked, and collect evidence for the audit.

### AC-7 — Unsuccessful Logon Attempts (Control)

This requirement is about stopping repeated attempts to guess login details. It limits how many times a person can enter the wrong sign-in information within a short time. Without this, an attacker could keep trying different usernames and passwords until they eventually find the correct combination, which could lead to unauthorised access to accounts or systems.

The organisation must configure the system so that each user is allowed no more than **5 consecutive invalid login attempts** within any **rolling 15-minute period**. This must include both:
- sign-ins made locally, and  
- sign-ins made over the network.

Once the maximum is exceeded, the system must automatically **lock the user account or the affected system component**. It must remain locked until an administrator explicitly releases it, and it must not be usable again until that release happens.

The organisation must also:
- document the policy and the administrator release procedures,
- keep evidence in audit logs showing when accounts are locked and when administrators release them,
- include this in the system security plan, and
- ensure the appropriate teams are responsible for implementing and maintaining the settings and enforcement.

##### Enforce 5 invalid logons/15 mins with admin-controlled unlock

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Confirm current authentication flow (OIDC/SAML/SSO) and identify all interactive sign-in paths that must be covered (web, API gateway interactive login, portal/VPN if applicable) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 8h | — |
| Configure IdP sign-in policy for rolling lockout: 5 consecutive invalid attempts within 15 minutes | IAM engineer | Enterprise | 12h | — |
| Configure exceeded-attempt action to lock account until administrator release (no automatic/self-unlock) and ensure policy applies to both local and network sign-in paths routed via IdP | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 10h | — |
| Validate that the application does not bypass IdP lockout (no alternate auth path, no cached sessions that allow access after lock, correct handling of locked-state responses) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement/enable audit evidence: ensure IdP events for threshold reached, lock initiation, and admin unlock are forwarded to SIEM with required fields and retention alignment | SIEM/monitoring engineer | Enterprise | 14h | — |
| Create administrator release workflow: role-restricted unlock/release process with auditable approval trail and separation of duties (IdP console or privileged access workflow) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 18h | — |
| Perform end-to-end testing and evidence pack: test accounts, verify rolling-window behaviour, confirm generic failure messaging, and produce audit-ready test results and screenshots/log excerpts | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 98h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set the identity provider (IdP) lockout threshold defined by the organisation so that it allows 5 consecutive invalid login attempts within a rolling 15-minute period.
- [ ] Configure the system so that, after too many failed login attempts, the account is locked until an administrator unlocks it (no automatic self-unlock).
- [ ] Check that the application signs in only through the identity provider (single sign-on (SSO) using OpenID Connect (OIDC) or Security Assertion Markup Language (SAML)), so network sign-in attempts are recorded consistently.
- [ ] Set up and send identity provider (IdP) sign-in, account lock, and account unlock audit records to the security information and event management (SIEM) system, and keep them long enough to support investigations.
- [ ] Set up an auditable process for unlocking administrator access, limited to restricted roles, with an explicit approval and a written reason for each unlock.
- [ ] Test and record that locked users cannot sign in to the application until an administrator unlocks their account.


---

#### AC-7.2 — Purge or Wipe Mobile Device (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that if a staff phone or tablet is lost or accessed by the wrong person, it will not keep organisation information on the device after repeated failed attempts to unlock it. Without this, someone could keep trying codes until they eventually guess, or the device could be left in a state where sensitive information is still accessible even after it should have been cleared.

The organisation must:
- define which mobile devices used by staff are covered; and
- configure them so that after **10 consecutive unsuccessful attempts to unlock the device** (not failed logins to a specific app or user account), the organisation information on the device is automatically deleted or wiped.

If the device uses strong full-device encryption, the organisation must use **cryptographic erase**. Otherwise, it must use an **approved wipe method**.

A successful unlock must reset the failure count back to zero.

The organisation must also keep:
- documented procedures,
- lists of covered devices, and
- rules for which wipe technique to use,

configure the devices accordingly, and keep audit records showing that the wipe happened and which method was used.

##### MDM-enforced wipe after 10 failed device unlocks (AC-7(2))

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Confirm MDM platform capabilities and supported wipe/sanitisation methods (cryptographic erase vs purge/wipe) and identify required configuration knobs for “device unlock attempt” counting | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Define in-scope device population and enforce enrolment scope/conditional access so only approved, MDM-enrolled devices can access organisation information | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Configure MDM policy to trigger automatic sanitisation after **10 consecutive unsuccessful device unlock attempts** (device logon), ensuring the counter is device-level and consecutive | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement encryption-strength decision logic using available MDM/OS signals (e.g., encryption status/attestation) and map outcomes to **cryptographic erase** (strong encryption) vs **NIST SP 800-88 Rev. 1 purge/wipe** (otherwise) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Integrate and validate audit/event logging for wipe initiation/completion in SIEM, including device identifier, timestamp, wipe method chosen, and result/status | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Execute test plan and evidence capture: (1) fail unlock up to threshold-1, (2) successful unlock resets counter to zero, (3) fail to threshold triggers correct sanitisation method based on encryption posture, (4) verify SIEM events | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Produce configuration documentation and compliance sign-off pack (decision logic, in-scope criteria, wipe trigger details, encryption-signal approach, evidence references) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 152h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a mobile device management (MDM) enrolment scope for mobile devices that are in scope and used to access organisation information.
- [ ] Set up the operating system (OS) / mobile device management (MDM) device lock policy and turn on tracking of unlock failures at the device level.
- [ ] Set an automatic wipe to start after 10 consecutive unsuccessful attempts to unlock the device.
- [ ] Implement encryption-strength detection in mobile device management (MDM) and link strong full-disk encryption to cryptographic erase.
- [ ] Set up devices that do not use strong encryption to use an approved data purge or wipe method from the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) Special Publication 800-88, Revision 1.
- [ ] Integrate mobile device management (MDM) wipe events into security information and event management (SIEM), keep the records for the required retention period, and make sure the device identifier, the time of the wipe, and the wipe method are recorded.
- [ ] Run and record test cases to prove that the counter resets after a successful unlock, and that the correct wipe method is selected.


---

#### AC-7.3 — Biometric Attempt Limiting (Enhancement)

This requirement is about stopping repeated failed biometric sign-ins from being tried again and again. It sets a firm limit of **5 unsuccessful biometric attempts**. Without this limit, someone could keep trying different fingers, faces, or other biometric samples until they eventually succeed, or they could overload the system and make genuine access harder to manage.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must configure its biometric sign-in process so that **after 5 failed attempts, no further biometric sign-in attempts are allowed**. The organisation must follow its documented approach for what happens next (for example, blocking biometric sign-in or requiring an alternative way to sign in).

The organisation must also:
- keep clear written procedures
- make sure the system is actually configured to **5** attempts
- record the results in audit records, including when the limit is reached
- include this approach in its security planning and system design documentation, so it can be demonstrated and maintained over time

##### Enforce 5 biometric failure attempts with audit and post-limit fallback

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Confirm biometric authentication entry points and map end-to-end flows to the central IdP (including Windows Hello/mobile/biometric-capable clients) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Configure central IdP/authentication policy to enforce **max 5 unsuccessful biometric attempts** using parameter **ac-07.03_odp = 5** across all relevant auth journeys | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement and validate post-limit behaviour (block further biometric attempts and route to documented alternative) with consistent UX and fallback logic in prod/test | Architect | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Enable and tune audit logging for each failed biometric attempt and for the **threshold-reached/blocked** event (ensure required fields and distinct indicator) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| SIEM integration: create correlation rules/dashboards and verify event retention/alerting meets audit requirements for AC-7(3) evidence | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 16h | £3,000 |
