| Design the shared output-rendering component contract (API/library interface) specifying required inputs (object attributes, output artefact type, subscriber/session context) and outputs (rendered labels + masked/full values) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement subscriber-aware masking logic at render time, including derivation of `unmasked_access` from the authorisation context (RBAC/ABAC decision from enterprise IdP/session claims) and deterministic redaction patterns | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Integrate the renderer across all output channels (web UI views, mobile screens, server-generated PDFs, report exports, print templates) ensuring every artefact includes the six labels and no channel bypasses rendering | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Add CI/CD enforcement: template/export linting and automated unit/integration tests that fail builds if any output path does not call the shared renderer and if required labels are missing | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement audit evidence emission per output object (output identifier, subscriber identity, attribute set version, `display_mode=full|masked`) and configure log retention/forwarding to SIEM/monitoring per organisational policy | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Perform end-to-end verification and assurance testing (authorised vs unauthorised sessions across all artefact types; shoulder-surfing leakage checks; regression suite; evidence pack for AC-16(5)) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 296h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a shared output display component that automatically adds the six required labels to every output document or file.
- [ ] Set up subscriber-specific permission checks so that `unmasked_access` is decided when the information is displayed (rendered).
- [ ] Use deterministic masking so full attribute values are shown only when `unmasked_access=true`; otherwise, show masked or redacted values.
- [ ] Make sure the correct renderer is used for every output path by using continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) template checks and automated tests.
- [ ] Add audit logging for each output that records the subscriber identity, the attribute set version, and the display mode (full or masked).
- [ ] Document the process for generating the output and hiding (masking) sensitive information, and get approval (sign-off) from the application owner and the security and compliance stakeholders.

#### AC-16.6 — Maintenance of Attribute Association (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring the right people have the right permissions, and that those permissions stay accurate over time. In everyday terms, the organisation must correctly record:

- which staff accounts and job roles are allowed to do what  
- which information and systems need which level of protection  
- what personal information is involved  
- what it may be used for  
- how long it must be kept  

Without this, sensitive information could be accessed or handled incorrectly, and personal data could be used or kept in ways that do not follow organisational policy or the law.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:

- set clear rules for linking security and privacy labels to the correct people and data  
- assign responsibility to the appropriate information security and privacy staff (and system developers where needed)  
- document the steps for doing this  
- give staff practical ways to set up and maintain these links in line with the organisation’s attribute rules and privacy policies

#### AC-16.7 — Consistent Attribute Interpretation (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure every part of your systems understands the same meaning when it receives information about who is allowed to access something and how data is allowed to move. If different components interpret these “rules of the road” differently, automated decisions could accidentally allow access that should be blocked or permit information to move where it shouldn’t, leading to real privacy and security failures.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define, in writing, the exact meaning of every security and privacy attribute used across distributed components—both for access decisions and for decisions about moving data—and publish a single organisation-approved guide so everyone uses the same interpretation. It must ensure all relevant components are configured to apply these rules, document how they are used for access and data-movement enforcement, assign named responsibility to the appropriate staff and developers, keep evidence from configuration and audit records, include this approach in security planning and privacy policy, and verify through testing or review that components behave consistently.

##### Shared security/privacy attribute semantics with contract validation

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Publish one organisation-approved interpretation guide and a version-controlled, machine-readable contract document.
- [ ] Implement contract validation in every component that uses attribute data, with documented “fail closed” or “quarantine” actions when attributes do not meet the required standard.
- [ ] Update the access checks and traffic-control logic so they use the shared interpretation resource (shared library or policy module) instead of their own local rules.
- [ ] Add continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) contract tests and release checks to prevent changes in meaning over time, without updating the shared interpretation guide.
- [ ] Set up enforcement logging to record the attribute values received and the interpretation or policy version that was used.

#### AC-16.8 — Association Techniques and Technologies (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that the labels showing how sensitive data is, and how it may be used, are securely linked to the data itself so they cannot be changed without detection. Without this, someone could alter the labels to get access they should not have, or to send personal information through the wrong processing steps—damaging both privacy commitments and access rules.

To meet this, the organisation must use a defined method to cryptographically link (mathematically secure) the security and privacy labels to each item of information. It must do this by embedding signed label details in the data’s metadata, with the signing keys protected using hardware-based safeguards supported by a hardware root of trust.

The system must check the signed security label every time access is requested, and check the signed privacy label every time the data is processed. Only after these checks are successful may the system use the verified labels to make automated access and data-handling decisions.

The organisation must document the approach, set up and record the required system behaviour, keep evidence in audit records, include it in both security and privacy plans, and assign clear responsibilities to information security and privacy staff and to system developers.

##### JWS-bound security/privacy labels verified at access/processing

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define canonical security/privacy label schema and JWS claim set (incl. label IDs, versions, issuing authority, object identifier/hash binding, expiry/rotation semantics) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design JWS embedding approach (object metadata vs sidecar metadata linked by object hash) and data model changes across storage/access/processing components | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement HSM-backed signing service (non-exportable keys, key aliasing/rotation, JWS generation for both security and privacy labels) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £45,000 |
| Implement verification libraries and enforcement middleware for access-time security label checks (signature validation, claim validation, object binding mismatch handling, fail-closed) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 64h | — |
| Implement verification at processing-time for privacy labels (workflow/ETL/stream ingress and export/share entry points; routing/processing block on failure; fail-closed) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Add audit logging, evidence generation, and SIEM integration (per verification attempt: object ID/hash, label values on success, outcome, key identifier, decision allow/deny/block; retention alignment) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £12,000 |
| Build test harness and acceptance validation (unit/integration tests, negative tests for tampering/expired keys/mismatched hashes, performance benchmarks at access/processing decision points) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Deploy with change management and runbook (configuration, key trust chain distribution, operational runbooks, monitoring/alerting for verification failures, DR considerations) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 336h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £57,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define a standard security and privacy label system (schema) and an object link (object identifier or hash) for signing JSON Web Signatures (JWS).
- [ ] Set up a label-signing service that creates security-label JSON Web Signatures (JWS) and privacy-label JSON Web Signatures (JWS) using hardware security module (HSM)-backed keys that cannot be exported.
- [ ] At the time an object is created or updated, store the signed JSON Web Signature (JWS) tokens in the object’s metadata (or, if needed, store them in a separate linked metadata record that is connected to the object by its hash).
- [ ] Check access time at the point where data access is enforced, and block or deny access if the security label JSON Web Signature (JWS) verification fails.
- [ ] Set up a check that confirms the processing time at the point where workflows, extract-transform-load (ETL), and exports enter the system, and stop any routing or processing if the privacy label JSON Web Signature (JWS) verification fails.
- [ ] Set up audit records for every verification attempt, including the result, the key identifier, and the label values used, and send these records to security information and event management (SIEM).


---

#### AC-16.9 — Attribute Reassignment — Regrading Mechanisms (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that any change to the security and privacy labels attached to information is made only through a trusted, approved re-labelling process. Without this control, the organisation could accidentally or incorrectly treat sensitive information as less protected (or more protected than it should be), which could lead to unauthorised access, incorrect handling, or privacy breaches.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must use an approved data-labelling workflow that includes:
- a formal policy-exception request
- re-tagging that can be checked and verified
- complete records of what was changed and when

Before the process is used, it must be validated for security labels using automated checks against the approved exception and test examples. It must also be validated for privacy labels by confirming the labels follow the required format and by running tests that compare what different users can access before the process is released.

Only authorised staff and developers should make these reassignments, using documented procedures and keeping audit records.

##### Validated, ticketed label regrading service with signed retags

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define single-purpose Label Regrading Service scope, API contract, and “no bypass” enforcement requirements (including downstream trust model) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement exception-ticket integration (ticket reference, scope, expiry, reason) with validation gating and rejection paths | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement cryptographic re-tagging (signed label metadata) including exception ID, label version, and validation evidence hash; integrate signing key management | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £25,000 |
| Build security attribute validation pipeline per ac-16.09_odp.01 (automated rule checks vs approved exception + security test vectors) with deterministic evidence generation | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Build privacy attribute validation pipeline per ac-16.09_odp.02 (schema conformance + differential access-control tests) with deterministic evidence generation and block-on-failure | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Implement audit logging and immutable retention (who/what/when/why, exception linkage, input/output labels, validation run IDs, pass/fail) and SIEM forwarding | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £12,000 |
| Enforce authorisation/authentication and prevent alternative label-edit paths (API-only reassignment, least-privilege roles, database write protections, and runtime guardrails) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| End-to-end validation, test evidence pack, and operational governance (runbooks, technical design, release checklist, and audit readiness sign-off) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 320h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £37,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Design and implement a dedicated “label regrading” service that provides only label reassignment functions.
- [ ] Integrate the service with policy-exception ticketing so every request cites an approved exception, with the approved scope and expiry date enforced.
- [ ] Before each retag release, carry out automated security checks against the approved exception list and a set of agreed security test cases.
- [ ] Before releasing a retag, carry out privacy checks by confirming the data matches the required format (schema conformance checks) and by running tests that verify access permissions behave correctly (differential access-control tests).
- [ ] Add cryptographic re-tagging using signed, integrity-protected label tokens, including an exception identifier and a validation evidence hash.
- [ ] Set up tamper-proof audit records for every regrade attempt, and send the records to the organisation’s security information and event management (SIEM) system, linked to the relevant ticket and including the validation results.
- [ ] Update the enforcement points downstream so they accept only regraded labels that have been digitally signed, and block and alert on any direct label changes that happen outside the service.


---

#### AC-16.10 — Attribute Configuration by Authorized Individuals (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that only the right people can decide what labels and rules the system uses to describe who is allowed to access information and how that information should be handled. If unauthorised staff could create or change these labels and values, they could accidentally or deliberately give themselves or others access they should not have, or incorrectly classify sensitive information. This could lead to real compliance and privacy failures.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must give authorised individuals the ability to define or change the types and values of both access-related (security) and privacy-related attributes. These attributes must be able to be linked to both people and information. The organisation must also have clear written procedures and documented rules that state who is authorised, ensure the system settings enforce those permissions, and keep records of changes so any attempt to alter attributes can be traced back to the person who made the change.

##### Authorised-only security/privacy attribute schema configuration

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define security-attribute and privacy-attribute configuration authorisation roles; document least-privilege scope and map roles to IdP groups/claims | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Configure phishing-resistant MFA and session controls for the attribute schema configuration UI/API (e.g., FIDO2/passkeys where feasible; conditional access; step-up auth) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £8,000 |
| Implement application/API enforcement: deny-by-default for create/update/delete of attribute types and values; enforce role checks at request time for both UI and API endpoints | Software Lead | Department | 48h | — |
| Build versioned schema configuration mechanism: controlled repository, schema validation (policy-as-code/rule checks), and deployment pipeline gating (no direct production hot edits) | Platform Engineer | Department | 56h | — |
| Implement approval workflow for schema changes (ticket/approval integration + automated validation results + promotion to environments) and ensure production changes require approved artefacts | Project Manager | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Emit tamper-evident audit events for every schema change (allowed/denied), including initiating identity, timestamp, old/new type/value, approval/ticket reference; forward to SIEM and configure retention | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £12,000 |
| Constrain subject/object association to the currently deployed authorised schema set: reject unknown/unconfigured attribute types/values and add negative tests + runtime safeguards | Architect | Business Unit | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 256h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £26,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and implement separate authorised roles for configuring security attributes and privacy attributes, and map these roles in the organisation’s identity provider (IdP).
- [ ] Require phishing-resistant multi-factor authentication (MFA) and conditional access for all attribute configuration user interface (UI) and application programming interface (API) endpoints.
- [ ] Set up access checks for applications and application programming interfaces (APIs) so that only authorised roles can create, update, or delete attribute types and values.
- [ ] Store attribute schemas as version-controlled configuration, and automatically check they meet the required rules (for example, using policy-as-code or an equivalent method) before deployment.
- [ ] Set up an approval process for database schema changes and stop making direct emergency edits in the live production environment.
- [ ] Create audit records that show if data has been altered for every change to a data schema, including who made the change, when it was made, what changed, the old value, the new value, and the approval reference, and send these records to security information and event management (SIEM).
- [ ] Limit attribute links (between subjects and objects) to the currently deployed authorised schema set, and reject any unknown types or values.


---

### AC-17 — Remote Access (Control)

This requirement is about ensuring that only approved ways of connecting from outside the organisation can reach your systems, and that every such connection is set up and used in a controlled, documented way. Without clear rules and prior approval, staff or devices could connect using the wrong method, bypass safeguards, or gain access before anyone has checked that the connection is safe and appropriate. This increases the risk of unauthorised access and data loss.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must list every type of remote access it allows (for example, dial-up, broadband, or wireless). For each type, it must document in plain language:
- who may use it
- what is allowed and what is prohibited
- the exact connection and configuration requirements
- practical guidance on how to set it up correctly

The organisation must also ensure that each remote access type is formally approved before any connections are permitted, and that it can provide records of remote access activity for review.

##### Authorised remote access types registry with gateway enforcement

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define remote access type taxonomy and register schema (per system/environment) including mandatory fields, evidence requirements, and naming conventions | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Build Remote Access Types Register templates and initial population for all in-scope systems/environments (Prod/Test/DR) with restrictions, auth/encryption requirements, and runbook/verification checklist per type | Project Manager | Business Unit | 56h | — |
| Implement gateway enforcement configuration templates (VPN concentrator/ZTNA/jump host/bastion) to allow only register-approved profiles, auth methods, and prohibited features (e.g., split tunnelling) | Network/Platform Engineer | Department | 72h | £18,000 |
| Implement identity-layer enforcement (e.g., conditional access / device posture / session constraints) mapped to authorised remote access types and required authentication methods | Security Engineer | Department | 64h | £12,000 |
| Create authorisation workflow and data model linking: register entry ↔ system/environment ↔ approver(s) ↔ effective/expiry ↔ change request reference; include audit-friendly export | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 48h | £6,000 |
| Configure audit evidence capture and SIEM forwarding for remote access sessions (user identity, remote access type/profile, start time, source endpoint/network) and validate log completeness | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £10,000 |
| Implement automated drift detection and enforcement guardrails (scheduled checks comparing enabled gateway/identity policies vs register; alerting and blocking unauthorised changes) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 56h | £14,000 |
| Perform end-to-end validation and audit readiness testing (authorisation-before-enable, evidence sufficiency, drift alert scenarios, and remediation run-throughs) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 392h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £60,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a separate Remote Access Types Register for each system. It must list every remote access type that is allowed, including any restrictions, required configuration settings, and step-by-step implementation instructions (runbooks).
- [ ] Set up gateway controls (virtual private network (VPN), zero trust network access (ZTNA), jump host, or bastion) so that only approved connection profiles and approved authentication methods can be used, based on the register.
- [ ] Set up identity-based conditional access so that remote sessions are only allowed if they match the authorised remote access type and meet the required security posture.
- [ ] Set up an approval process for remote access. Each type of remote access must be approved and recorded with a date and time before the matching gateway and identity rules are turned on for each environment.
- [ ] Set up and test audit logging so it records remote access type or profile, the user’s identity, the time the connection started, and the source endpoint and network details. Then send this information to the security information and event management (SIEM) system.
- [ ] Automate checks for configuration changes by comparing the currently enabled gateway and identity settings against the approved register, and alert or block any unauthorised changes.


---

#### AC-17.1 — Monitoring and Control (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure that every time someone connects to your systems from a distance, the organisation automatically checks that the connection is allowed and records what happened. Without this, unauthorised people could try to break in, or staff could connect in ways that do not follow company rules, and you might only find out after damage has been done.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must use automated tools to continuously monitor remote connections from all supported device types, including servers, laptops, workstations, smartphones and tablets. It must also automatically enforce the organisation’s remote access rules by allowing or blocking connection sessions based on those rules. The organisation must automatically produce clear records of both the monitoring activity and the results of any allowed or blocked connections, using the agreed details, so that later reviews can demonstrate compliance.

The organisation should be able to show that these monitoring and blocking features are enabled in current settings, work in practice, and are reviewed by the responsible people.

##### Policy-enforced remote access with automated allow/deny logging

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

| Design the policy model and enforcement logic (allow/deny/restrict) using IdP claims/roles, MFA requirements, device posture/compliance signals, and contextual constraints (IP/geo/time/target sensitivity) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Implement IdP ↔ enforcement point integration (SSO, session establishment hooks, authorisation decision flow, and re-evaluation where supported) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Configure automated allow/deny enforcement on the gateway/secure access proxy for all in-scope methods, including fail-closed behaviour and consistent target/service identification | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Enable and validate enforcement-time audit logging for both allowed and denied sessions; ensure structured event payloads contain required remote access fields and source context where available | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |

Total Estimated Effort: **296h**  
Total Estimated Cost: **£25,000**

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] List all ways people can access systems remotely, and identify which ones fall within the scope of AC-17(1).
- [ ] Connect every remote access entry point to the organisation’s identity provider (IdP) so users are authenticated and authorised in one central place.
- [ ] Set up rules for conditional access and session authorisation to automatically allow or block remote access, based on the remote access policy.
- [ ] Integrate information about the security status of endpoints and devices so the enforcement point can identify whether a device is compliant and apply the required enforcement.
- [ ] Enable and confirm audit logging at the time of enforcement for both permitted and blocked or denied remote access attempts.
- [ ] Match the remote access audit event fields to the organisation’s AU-2 and AU-2(a) remote access audit event definitions, then check the results in the security information and event management (SIEM) system.
- [ ] Set up security information and event management (SIEM) alerts for denied access attempts and unusual remote access activity, using the same audit records.

#### AC-17.2 — Protection of Confidentiality and Integrity Using Encryption (Enhancement)

This requirement is about protecting information when people connect to your systems from elsewhere. It ensures that data sent and received during remote connections stays secret and cannot be altered while it travels over the internet. Without this protection, an attacker could intercept remote connections, read sensitive information, or change what is sent—leading to fraud, data leaks, or unauthorised changes.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must use approved, secure encryption for every remote access session. This should use a recognised secure remote method, such as a private network connection and/or a secure web connection, and it must be set up correctly. The organisation must record which encryption methods are used and how they are configured, keep the relevant records and audit information showing encryption was active, and ensure remote-access instructions and staff procedures follow the organisation’s access rules.

The organisation should also maintain design and security planning documents that clearly explain how encryption protects remote access.

##### Enforce VPN/TLS-only remote access with approved cryptography

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define approved remote access paths and cryptography requirements (VPN required for network/admin access; TLS-only for web/API; explicit minimum TLS/VPN parameters) and publish into the access control standard | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Perform network/app exposure assessment and produce a “bypass map” showing all current remote access routes to application and admin interfaces (including direct-to-internal paths) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement tunnel-first enforcement: block direct inbound access to application/admin subnets and allow only VPN gateway egress/approved ingress (firewall/security group rules + routing controls) | Infrastructure Lead | Business Unit | 32h | — |
| Configure TLS enforcement for all remote web/API endpoints: disable HTTP, enforce minimum TLS version and strong cipher suites, enable certificate validation and HSTS where applicable | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 40h | — |
| Configure approved VPN cryptography and authentication hardening (e.g., IPsec/IKEv2 or TLS-based VPN): minimum protocol/cipher/key exchange, certificate validation, and session controls aligned to identity policy | Security Engineer | Business Unit | 32h | £3,000 |
| Integrate identity and session controls at the VPN/TLS entry points (phishing-resistant MFA where available, conditional access/risk-based re-authentication, session termination on policy change) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Enable audit-ready logging and SIEM integration for VPN/TLS sessions (session start/stop, user identity, source IP, negotiated cryptographic parameters where available), and validate retention/alerting | SOC / SIEM Administrator | Department | 24h | £2,500 |
| Produce configuration baseline and system design/security plan evidence pack mapping each remote access mechanism to the approved cryptography settings, including test results and change records | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| Total Estimated Effort |  |  | **208h** |  |
| Total Estimated Cost |  |  |  | **£5,500** |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish the approved remote access routes in the access control standard—for example, using virtual private network (VPN) only for internal and administrative access, and using transport layer security (TLS) only for remote web and application programming interface (API) access.
- [ ] Set up network, firewall, and internet-entry (ingress) rules to block direct access from the public internet to internal network sections and administrative pages, except through the virtual private network (VPN) gateway or an approved Transport Layer Security (TLS) termination layer.
- [ ] Update the virtual private network (VPN) and transport layer security (TLS) settings to match the organisation’s approved encryption standards, including the minimum supported protocol versions, approved cipher suites, certificate checks, and the strength of the key exchange.
- [ ] Require users to prove their identity when accessing remotely (connect to the organisation’s identity provider and require multi-factor authentication and any policy-based access checks).
- [ ] Send and centralise virtual private network (VPN) and transport layer security (TLS) termination logs to the security information and event management (SIEM) system, including session start and end times, the user’s identity, the source internet protocol (IP) address, and any available details of the encryption settings that were agreed during the connection.
- [ ] Keep records of the configuration baseline and the system design and security plan evidence that show which encryption methods are used for remote access and how those methods are set up.

#### AC-17.3 — Managed Access Control Points (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that anyone connecting to your systems from outside the office does so only through approved access points that your organisation controls and monitors, rather than finding a direct route in. Without this, attackers could bypass your protections, reach your systems from the open internet, and potentially steal data, disrupt services, or take over accounts.  

To meet this expectation, your organisation must have clear written rules and step-by-step procedures for remote access that specify the approved access points, and it must keep up-to-date design and configuration records showing how remote access is routed through those points. You also need a current, complete list of every approved access point used for remote access, audit records showing that the routing is actually taking place, and a system security plan that describes and supports this approach.

##### Centralise remote access via managed gateways with enforced routing

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

| Perform target-side network access scoping and design (identify all administrative/management endpoints/ports, define required gateway-origin source restrictions per environment) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement network routing enforcement (firewall/security group rules to deny direct internet-to-target admin access; allow only from gateway networks/security groups; validate bypass resistance) | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Integrate gateways with enterprise IdP and enforce phishing-resistant MFA + conditional access (authorised identity/session context at entry point; test end-to-end session establishment) | IAM Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £12,000 |
| Standardise gateway hardening and configuration-as-code (secure baselines, policy templates, peer-reviewed change workflow, automated drift checks where feasible) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Centralise evidence and monitoring (configure log forwarding from gateways and network controls to SIEM; implement detections/alerts for attempted direct-to-target admin access; confirm retention settings) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £8,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 304h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £26,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep an up-to-date, official list of approved managed access control points, including their gateway identifiers, owners, environments, and the sources of their logs.
- [ ] Set up firewalls and security groups so that administrative access ports on the target systems can be reached only from the approved gateway networks or security groups.
- [ ] Connect the gateways to the organisation’s identity provider (IdP) and apply conditional access rules, requiring phishing-resistant multi-factor authentication (MFA) for remote administrative access.
- [ ] Apply secure gateway configuration standards and manage any changes using configuration-as-code, with peer review before changes are approved.
- [ ] Limit management access to the target system’s management endpoints to approved sources only, using an allowlist that matches the gateway’s registered entries.
- [ ] Send the gateway and firewall logs to the security information and event management (SIEM) system, and set up alerts to detect any direct attempts to access administrative functions on the target system.
- [ ] Update the system design diagrams and the system security plan to show that remote access is only possible through the managed gateways.

#### AC-17.4 — Privileged Commands and Access (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that when someone needs to sign in from a different location to carry out high-privilege work or view sensitive security information, it is done only for clearly approved reasons and in a way that can be checked later. Without this, remote access could be misused to make unauthorised changes, conceal wrongdoing, or steal information needed to protect the business—turning a helpful support route into a serious weakness.

The organisation must allow remote access to run privileged commands and to view security-relevant information only when there is explicit approval for specific purposes: incident response, fixing vulnerabilities, privileged maintenance, and security monitoring or audit evidence.

Privileged commands must be limited to emergency maintenance, applying patches, making configuration changes, or running security tools to produce audit evidence. Viewing security-relevant information must be limited to incident response support, fixing vulnerabilities, and security monitoring for Confidential and Secret data.

Every remote action must create clear records showing who did what, when, and why. The organisation’s security plan must also document the reasons for using remote access.

##### Purpose-bound remote privileged access with evidence-rich approvals

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define purpose-to-entitlement mappings and allowed remote access scope (ac-17.04_odp.01 / ac-17.04_odp.02), including emergency deviation categories and required approver roles | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design PAM/remote admin broker workflow: request → approval → time-bound access, including session metadata schema (purpose, approval/ticket ID, requester, target, time window) and enforcement points | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement/Configure PAM policies for purpose-bound privileged command execution: command allow-lists/role policies, session gating on approval presence, and time-window enforcement | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £25,000 |
| Implement/Configure entitlements and access controls for security-relevant information sessions: purpose-bound entitlements for IR/vulnerability remediation/security monitoring views and Confidential/Secret scoping | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £10,000 |
| Enable evidence generation: session recording + command-level auditing for privileged sessions; access logging for information sessions; centralisation to SIEM/logging with integrity protections and retention alignment | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £18,000 |
| Integrate approvals with ITSM/workflow tooling: ensure approval/ticket IDs are captured and validated at session start, including emergency justification capture and linkage to compensating controls | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | £6,000 |
| Update system security plan and produce audit-ready documentation: rationale, enforcement approach, evidence types, log locations/fields, and review procedures mapped to AC-17(4) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Execute end-to-end testing and governance readiness: test cases for each purpose, negative tests (no approval / wrong purpose / out-of-window), evidence completeness checks, and operational runbook handover | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 272h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £59,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] For each permitted remote use of privileged commands and each security-relevant information need, link it to the specific privileged access management (PAM) entitlements and purpose codes.
- [ ] Set up a workflow for remote privileged access management that requires: a request, an approval, and access limited to a specific time window. Record the reason for access and the approval or ticket reference in the session details.
- [ ] Set up an approved list of commands and apply role-based restrictions so that, during approved remote sessions, only the permitted categories of privileged commands can be run.
- [ ] Enable recording of privileged user sessions, audit actions taken during those sessions, and log access to security-relevant information views and queries.
- [ ] Add privileged access management (PAM) session and access logs to the central security information and event management (SIEM) and logging system, with protections to keep the records trustworthy and retention that supports audit requirements.
- [ ] Update the system security plan to explain why remote access is used, what each access purpose is for, and how supporting evidence is collected and linked to the relevant approvals.


---

#### AC-17.6 — Protection of Mechanism Information (Enhancement)

This requirement is about keeping the instructions for how remote access works securely controlled, so only the right people can use them and only for approved purposes. Without this, someone could obtain the information needed to connect from outside the organisation, then misuse it or share it further, which could lead to unauthorised access to systems and sensitive information.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly identify what remote-access information it holds and protect it from unauthorised use or sharing. It should ensure that the rules for who can access what, the step-by-step remote access procedures, the system security plan, and any relevant agreements or behaviour rules all explicitly include these protection requirements.

Access to this information must be limited to authorised staff responsible for setting up or monitoring remote access, and to authorised system users who genuinely need to know. The documentation must be kept up to date and easy to use.

##### Remote access mechanism info vault with role-based access controls

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define vault information handling model (classification, authorised roles, rules of behaviour/PL-4 mapping, access agreements/PS-6 mapping) and produce security requirements document | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Perform remote access mechanism information inventory and classify assets (documents, runbooks, diagrams, connection strings, screenshots, troubleshooting steps) and define content ownership | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Take an inventory of all information assets used for remote access (including documents, runbooks, diagrams, connection steps, and troubleshooting guidance) and mark each one as sensitive.
- [ ] Set up a dedicated secure storage area (vault) for information about the remote access method, and configure how that information is kept confidential.
- [ ] Set up role groups based on who needs access (people who implement and monitor systems, the security operations team, and authorised system users) and link each group to the organisation’s identity provider (IdP).
- [ ] Apply rules for who can access repositories, including multi-factor authentication (MFA) and conditional access, restrict viewing, downloading, and exporting, disable public sharing, and prevent uncontrolled creation of share links.
- [ ] Use an approved information technology service management (ITSM) process for delivering access within a set time or by using a vault link, and do not allow mechanism information to be sent as email or chat attachments.
- [ ] Keep audit logs enabled for all repository access and sharing attempts, and set a regular schedule for reviewing and formally attesting content changes, with clear records showing what changed and when.


---

#### AC-17.9 — Disconnect or Disable Access (Enhancement)

This requirement is about being able to quickly stop remote access to your systems when it is no longer safe. If remote access cannot be turned off fast enough, an attacker or an unauthorised person could keep using your systems, or access could continue after a staff member leaves or a device is compromised. This could cause real disruption to the business and financial loss.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must have a working way to disconnect or disable remote access within 15 minutes of starting the action. This must be supported by clear, written rules and step-by-step instructions. The instructions must:

- name who is responsible for making the change  
- explain exactly what to do for each type of remote access  
- require that the organisation records who made the change and when, so it can be checked later  

The organisation must also keep records of how the system is designed and configured to show it can support this fast shut-off, and keep audit records proving that the shut-off was actually completed within 15 minutes.

##### Emergency remote-access kill switch with 15-minute disablement

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Map remote access methods to exact enforcement points (VPN/remote gateway, firewall policy, ZTNA app policy, bastion/jump host, remote support tooling) and produce an auditable coverage matrix | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design emergency deny policies per enforcement point, including stable policy identifiers, scope (target systems/environments), and safe rollback approach | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 28h | — |
| Implement policy-as-code (where supported) and configure emergency deny rules at each enforcement point (including test/staging parity) | Platform Engineer | Department | 40h | — |
| Build operator-triggered kill-switch orchestration/runbook integration (authorised roles only, step-up authentication, single “activate/deactivate” actions, idempotency) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £6,000 |
| Define and document emergency workflow (ticket/reference capture, rationale, operator identity, approval requirements where governance permits) and align with change/config governance | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement verification procedure to measure disablement within 15 minutes (stopwatch start/end, controlled test account/session, evidence capture of timestamps and policy identifiers) | Security Operations Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Centralise and validate audit evidence forwarding to SIEM/log management (orchestration execution ID, operator identity, start/end timestamps, policy identifiers, enforcement-point logs) and confirm retention | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £2,500 |

| Total Estimated Effort | 200h |  |
| Total Estimated Cost |  | £8,500 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] List all ways people can access the application or system remotely, and match each one to where access is controlled (the enforcement point).
- [ ] Create emergency “deny” rules for each enforcement point, using stable identifiers so audit records can be matched reliably.
- [ ] Set up an operator-activated “kill switch” procedure (runbook/playbook) that uses role-based access control (RBAC) and requires step-up authentication.
- [ ] Define and document an emergency process that records who carried out the action, why it was done, and a reference to what was executed.
- [ ] Run a timed check to confirm remote access is turned off within 15 minutes, and record the start and end times.
- [ ] Set up security information and event management (SIEM) and log retention so that it keeps records of kill-switch execution IDs, the operator’s identity, policy identifiers, and enforcement-point logs.


---

#### AC-17.10 — Authenticate Remote Commands (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that remote “admin” instructions sent to your on-premises servers and operational technology gateways are genuine, not altered, and only carried out once. Without these checks, an attacker could try to send unauthorised commands, change a legitimate command while it is being sent, or resend an old command so the system repeats an action—potentially leading to serious disruption, damage, or compromise of sensitive information.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set up approved remote management routes so that both sides prove they are trusted using digital certificates. Each command must also include (1) a per-command integrity check to confirm it has not been tampered with and (2) a sequence number that increases steadily. The receiving systems must verify these checks before executing any command. They must reject any command with an incorrect or missing integrity check, and they must refuse any command that is out of sequence or a repeat.

The organisation must document how this works, define the procedures, configure the systems to enforce it, record the results in audit logs, include it in the security plan, and assign clear responsibility for implementation and oversight.

##### Authenticate remote admin commands with mTLS, HMAC, and sequence checks

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the authenticated remote admin command protocol (mTLS requirements, command envelope schema, HMAC input canonicalisation rules, sequence number scoping by sender/target, and explicit rejection reason codes) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design and document the approved management channel enforcement (allow-listed ingress paths, ZTNA/jump host routing or dedicated admin network segments, and mapping to command ingestion endpoints) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement receiving-side verification in on-prem server command handler/agent (mTLS client cert validation, HMAC verification, strict monotonic sequence acceptance, and “reject-not-execute” execution gating) | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 40h | — |
| Implement receiving-side verification in OT gateway command handler/agent (same envelope verification logic, plus OT-specific integration points and failure handling to ensure no command execution on verification failure) | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 40h | — |
| Implement key management and HMAC key handling (shared secret/derived key strategy bound to mTLS identity/session, secure storage, rotation procedure, and backward compatibility strategy during rotation windows) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £8,000 |
| Build and integrate audit/telemetry for compliance evidence (log fields for sender identity, target stream, sequence number, HMAC result, mTLS result, and explicit rejection reason; forward to SIEM with retention tagging) | SOC/SIEM Engineer | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Develop and run test plan (unit/integration tests for HMAC mismatch, replay/out-of-order sequence, invalid certs, and end-to-end acceptance/rejection; include both server and OT gateway paths) | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 32h | £3,000 |
| Produce audit-ready implementation evidence pack (design docs, configuration snapshots, test results, operational runbook for rotation/revocation, and change-management records) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 232h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £11,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set the approved management communication routes and limit network connections so that only those approved routes can access the command input points for on-premises servers and operational technology (OT) gateways.
- [ ] Set up mutual Transport Layer Security (mutual TLS) for the remote command intake endpoints, and configure which certificate authorities are trusted, how certificates are checked, and how certificates are revoked and rotated.
- [ ] Define and implement a standard “command envelope” format that includes: a standardised (canonical) version of the message content, a separate hash-based message authentication code (HMAC) for each command, and a sequence number that increases step-by-step (monotonically) for each sender/target communication stream.
- [ ] Set up checks on the receiving side to confirm mutual Transport Layer Security (mTLS), verify the hash-based message authentication code (HMAC), and reject any command that arrives out of order or that has already been received before.
- [ ] Record an audit log entry for every command that is accepted or rejected, including the specific reason for rejection (for example: failed HMAC, replayed or out-of-order sequence, or certificate failure).
- [ ] Carry out end-to-end tests that replay and attempt to tamper with data for both on-premises servers and operational technology (OT) gateways, and record the results as evidence for compliance.


---

### AC-18 — Wireless Access (Control)

This requirement is about making sure any wireless connection to your systems is set up correctly and is only used when it has been formally approved. If this is not done, someone could connect using an unapproved device or wireless method, bypass the intended controls, or gain access through a poorly set-up wireless link. This could lead to unauthorised entry, data exposure, or disruption.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must first list every type of wireless connection it will use (for example, Wi‑Fi, Bluetooth, and other wireless links). It must then document clear setup rules, clear connection rules (including what is allowed and what is not), and step-by-step guidance for each type. The organisation must also name specific people who are responsible for managing wireless connections and for oversight.

Finally, the system must only allow each type of wireless connection after the organisation has recorded and approved it for the specific purpose. It must also keep records of wireless connection activity so later checks can confirm that what happened matched the approvals.

##### Authorise-then-enable wireless access with mutual authentication

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Establish scope and data model for wireless authorise-then-enable (catalogue schema, identifiers for SSID/profile, Bluetooth pairing mode, radio link profile; mapping to site and validity window) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Build wireless access catalogue templates and authorisation requirements (purpose, allowed identities, required authentication with authenticator protection + mutual authentication, usage restrictions, approval workflow fields) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define per-technology enforceable configuration baselines (802.11x/EAP-TLS or equivalent mutual auth; disable legacy/unauthenticated modes; Bluetooth authenticated pairing/device identity controls; radio link authentication requirements) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement policy-as-code/profile generation from authorisation records (machine-readable policy output that is the sole source of truth for enabling profiles) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £8,000 |
| Integrate authorisation workflow with enforcement points (GRC/ticketing → policy generation → wireless controllers/NAC/Bluetooth management/radio gateways; ensure unauthorised profiles cannot be broadcast/accepted) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | £15,000 |
| Implement audit logging, retention, and SIEM forwarding with traceability to authorisation record (association/auth attempts/success/failure; linkage via profile/SSID identifier and validity scope) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £6,000 |
| Conduct validation and sample audit evidence pack (test cases for mutual authentication/authenticator protection; verify no enabled profile exists without current authorisation; produce audit-ready report) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 216h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £29,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a wireless access catalogue that covers every wireless technology used for access, including Wi‑Fi (IEEE 802.11), Bluetooth, and any microwave or packet radio connections used.
- [ ] Set out configuration requirements for each technology that clearly require protection of the authenticator and mutual authentication, and link these requirements to the controller and gateway settings.
- [ ] Set up an “authorise first, then enable” process that creates a machine-readable wireless policy from approved authorisation records, including the purpose, scope, and validity period.
- [ ] Set up the wireless enforcement points so that only authorised device profiles are enabled and broadcast, and unauthorised profiles are blocked.
- [ ] Enable and centralise logging of wireless connection and authentication attempts, including both successes and failures. Send these logs to security information and event management (SIEM), using identifiers that link each event to the relevant authorisation record.
- [ ] Carry out a test audit to confirm that a switched-on wireless profile has a current authorisation record, and that connection records can be traced back to it.

#### AC-18.1 — Authentication and Encryption (Enhancement)

This expectation is about ensuring that anyone trying to connect to your systems over wireless is properly checked, and that any information sent over that wireless connection is protected so it cannot be read or altered by others. Without strong checks, an unauthorised person could join your wireless network, pretend to be a legitimate user, or capture sensitive information while it is being sent through the air.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set up wireless access so that both the people using it and the devices they use are strongly verified. This means only authorised users and approved devices can connect. The organisation must also use strong encryption so wireless data cannot be read by outsiders while it is being transmitted.

The organisation should document how wireless access is implemented and what limits apply, keep the relevant design and configuration records, and retain audit records showing wireless access activity. It should also include these wireless verification and encryption requirements in its security planning, so the right teams maintain the protections and can show that they remain in place over time.

##### WPA3-Enterprise 802.1X with user+device auth and strong encryption

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Wireless security baseline: define standard SSID security profile (WPA3-Enterprise preferred, WPA2-Enterprise fallback), disable open/WEP/WPA/WPA2-Personal/legacy modes, and publish configuration requirements | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Controller/AP configuration rollout: implement WPA3-Enterprise (or WPA2-Enterprise fallback) and enforce 802.1X on all organisation-managed production SSIDs (with change-controlled deployment to prod/test) | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| RADIUS/AAA integration: configure RADIUS servers and 802.1X authentication policies for user+device flows (EAP method selection, session handling, fail-closed behaviour, and attribute release) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| User authentication integration: integrate 802.1X user auth with the enterprise IdP and enforce phishing-resistant MFA for interactive user logins (including mapping of IdP claims to RADIUS attributes) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Device certificate authentication: implement device certificate issuance/approval workflow, deploy trust anchors to RADIUS, and configure certificate-to-device identity mapping to an “approved device” record | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Authorisation & segmentation enforcement: implement AAA authorisation rules (user group + device certificate attributes) and map authenticated sessions to correct VLAN/VRF/ACLs; ensure non-approved devices are denied or restricted to non-production networks | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Evidence & audit pack: produce audit-ready evidence (controller/AP config exports, RADIUS/AAA policy configuration, certificate issuance/approval records, and retained RADIUS auth logs for success/failure) and validate logging/retention meets audit needs | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 256h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Enable Wi-Fi Protected Access 3 for Enterprise (or Wi-Fi Protected Access 2 for Enterprise where required) and turn off open or older wireless modes for all Wi-Fi network names (service set identifiers) used to access systems.
- [ ] Configure each service set identifier (SSID) so that devices must use IEEE 802.1X with remote authentication dial-in user service (RADIUS) / authentication, authorisation, and accounting (AAA). If authentication fails, block the device from connecting.
- [ ] Set up 802.1X user sign-in authentication with the organisation’s identity provider (IdP) and require phishing-resistant multi-factor authentication (MFA) for user logins.
- [ ] Set up device-certificate based sign-in and keep an approved-device list that is used when authorising access through authentication, authorisation, and accounting (AAA).
- [ ] Apply “authentication, authorisation, and accounting (AAA)” rules to assign authenticated users and devices to the correct virtual local area network (VLAN) and virtual routing and forwarding (VRF), and limit access to only the resources they need.
- [ ] Export and store the wireless controller/access point configuration and the RADIUS (Remote Authentication Dial-In User Service) and authentication, authorisation and accounting (AAA) policy configuration as evidence for audits.
- [ ] Send and keep RADIUS authentication logs (successful and failed logins) in the security information and event management (SIEM) system, with suitable retention periods and alerts.


---

#### AC-18.3 — Disable Wireless Networking (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that any built-in wireless features on new devices are switched off before the devices are issued and put into use, unless wireless is genuinely needed for an essential business purpose. If wireless is left switched on by default, it can give attackers an easier way to interfere with or access systems from nearby, which can result in data loss, service disruption, or unauthorised access.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must first identify which devices include built-in wireless capabilities. It must clearly record when wireless is allowed for essential business missions, and ensure that for all other cases the wireless features are disabled before deployment using the device’s built-in settings (not temporary workarounds).

The organisation must also keep written rules, design and configuration records showing how wireless is disabled. It must retain evidence and audit records proving the wireless was switched off before deployment, and assign named staff who are trained or authorised to follow the documented process.

##### Disable embedded Wi‑Fi/Bluetooth before device issuance (default-off)

- Priority: Critical

| Define exception criteria and approval workflow (essential mission/function definition, scope, expiry, approver requirements, and audit record fields) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement golden build/provisioning configurations (golden images + UEFI/BIOS provisioning templates where supported; OS/device-management profiles for Wi‑Fi/Bluetooth default-off) | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 56h | £6,000 |
| Configure endpoint management enforcement to prevent post-build drift (compliance policies, remediation actions, and exception tagging/time-bounding) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £4,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 208h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £12,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Maintain an inventory of managed device types, and record which built-in radios (Wi‑Fi and Bluetooth) are present and how they can be switched off (using the device firmware, the operating system, or management tools).
- [ ] Publish an exception policy that defines the criteria for what counts as an “essential mission or function”, who must approve exceptions, what systems are covered, and how long the approval lasts for enabling wireless.
- [ ] Update the “golden” build and provisioning process to turn off Wi‑Fi and Bluetooth by default, including any firmware settings where this is supported.
- [ ] Set up endpoint management to ensure all devices (except approved exceptions) have wireless turned off, and automatically fix any changes that drift away from this setting.
- [ ] Set up an approval step (“issuance gate”) that checks for configuration compliance evidence and deployment or release records before any devices are provided to users.
- [ ] Set up regular checks (automated where possible; where firmware evidence is limited, use documented spot checks) and keep records of the results for audit.

#### AC-18.4 — Restrict Configurations by Users (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that only the correct named people can make independent changes to your wireless settings, such as Wi‑Fi configuration. Without this, someone who is not meant to could quietly weaken security, disrupt services, or redirect connections, creating opportunities for unauthorised access or outages.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must keep a clear, up-to-date list of the specific users who are allowed to independently configure wireless networking, and it must explicitly approve each person on that list. It should define what “independently configure” means in practice, and then enforce it through its written rules for system access, its documented procedures for how wireless is set up and used (including any restrictions), and the way the wireless systems are configured.

The organisation must also keep supporting design and configuration records, maintain audit logs showing who made wireless changes, and include this restriction in its overall security plan so that changes can be checked and verified.

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and document which in-scope wireless features count as being able to be configured independently.
- [ ] Set up a controlled, authorised configurators register that lists named users, includes scope tags, records the approver, and sets review dates.
- [ ] Connect the Wi‑Fi controller and administration portals to the organisation’s identity provider (single sign-on), and link the Wi‑Fi register scope tags to role-based access control (RBAC) roles and groups.
- [ ] Set up the wireless management system so only authorised users with the correct role-based access control (RBAC) permissions can change configuration settings. All other users must either be limited to read-only access or be denied access.
- [ ] Turn on and keep audit logs for all changes to wireless settings, including the authenticated identity from the identity provider (IdP).
- [ ] Create a regular reconciliation report that compares the “changed-by” identities for wireless changes against the authorised configurators register.
- [ ] Update the system security plan and the wireless configuration and procedure documents to reference the register, scope, and enforcement.

#### AC-18.5 — Antennas and Transmission Power Levels (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure your building’s wireless internet signals stay within the areas you control. You do this by choosing the right antenna types and setting the correct transmission strength for each wireless access point. If you do not, signals could travel outside your organisation’s controlled areas, allowing unauthorised people to pick them up from outside and potentially gain access to your systems or data.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must select antennas for each access point with the specific goal of reducing signal reception outside the boundary, and record the reasons for each choice. It must also calibrate and document the transmission power settings so signals are unlikely to travel beyond the boundary. This should be based on results from regular wireless surveys that measure the local radio environment and take account of other nearby radio systems.

The organisation should apply the agreed antenna and power settings consistently, keep evidence of the survey results and decisions, and ensure any changes are approved and can be traced back to who authorised them and when.

##### RF survey-led antenna selection and calibrated Wi‑Fi power baselines

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Create authoritative WAP inventory (coordinates/floor plan mapping, mounting details, boundary segment served, current antenna model/orientation, current transmit power settings) | Network Engineering Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define evidence requirements and calibration methodology (survey acceptance criteria, minimum viable in-boundary coverage target, out-of-boundary reduction rationale, required artefacts for audit) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Plan and execute initial boundary-focused wireless survey (active site survey + spectrum analysis; capture time-of-day/shift variability where feasible; include nearby emitters and record measured results) | RF Survey Vendor or Internal RF Engineering Team | Enterprise | 32h | £18,000 |
| Select and document antenna configuration per boundary segment (directional/sector/beamforming-capable where supported; rationale linking antenna type/orientation to boundary reduction; update WAP inventory accordingly) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Calibrate transmission power per WAP to minimum viable levels (derive dBm/equivalent settings from survey measurements; produce per-WAP calibration worksheets and measured basis) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Produce auditable configuration baseline (controller/infrastructure exports and/or infrastructure-as-code artefacts; include antenna model/orientation and transmit power settings; versioned and access-controlled) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement change control and enforcement (workflow for approvals, restrict who can modify antenna/power settings, periodic review triggers, and drift detection approach) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 16h | £3,000 |
| Establish periodic survey cadence and re-validation process (cadence definition, triggers for re-survey, reporting templates, and evidence retention schedule) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 12h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 164h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £21,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep an accurate, official inventory of wireless access points (WAPs), including location tags for sites near boundaries and details of how each unit is mounted
- [ ] Carry out an initial wireless coverage survey focused on the boundaries of the area (active survey plus radio-frequency spectrum analysis), including nearby radio systems.
- [ ] Choose antennas that can point in a specific direction (directional, sector, or beamforming-capable) for each boundary segment, and record the reasons for your choice.
- [ ] Adjust the transmit power of each boundary-adjacent wireless access point (WAP) to the lowest level that still works, using the measured survey results, and record the power settings (in dBm) and the corresponding power profile.
- [ ] Create an auditable baseline for wireless local area network (WLAN) settings (for example, controller exports and/or infrastructure-as-code) that fixes the antenna and power settings.
- [ ] Put in place change-management controls so that any changes to the antenna or power settings must be approved, and so that the baseline and supporting evidence are updated.
- [ ] Arrange regular wireless coverage checks and re-check the antenna and power settings after major changes in the surrounding environment.

### AC-19 — Access Control for Mobile Devices (Control)

This expectation is about ensuring company phones and tablets are set up and used in a controlled, consistent way, including when staff are working away from the office. Without clear rules and enforced connection checks, an unapproved device could be able to access company systems, or a device could be left unprotected and become a way for data theft, fraud, or disruption.  

To meet this expectation, the organisation must define and keep up to date clear rules for organisation-owned mobile devices. These rules must cover the required settings and how devices must be protected when they are in controlled areas and when they are outside them. The organisation must also provide step-by-step guidance for both users and administrators, including what protective software is required, regular security updates, checks for suspicious or changed software, and how to switch off unnecessary device features.  

Finally, the organisation must only allow mobile devices to connect to its systems when it has explicitly approved that device’s connection, and it must be able to prove this using records and audit logs.

- [ ] Define and get approval for the organisation’s rules for mobile devices, including what users must do when working away from the office to stay protected, and what to do if a device is lost or stolen.
- [ ] Set up mobile device management (MDM) baseline settings for iPhone and Android devices to require device encryption, a screen lock with a passcode, and restrictions on apps that are not managed by the organisation.
- [ ] Set up and keep an up-to-date list of approved devices in mobile device management (MDM), including each device’s ID or serial number, and make sure only devices on that list can access systems.
- [ ] Set up and require mobile protection software using mobile device management (MDM). Where supported, scan for malware and block access if the protection software is turned off or out of date.
- [ ] Set up mobile device management (MDM) checks to confirm that each device’s operating system and security updates/patches meet the required security standard, and block access for any device that falls below that minimum baseline.
- [ ] Link mobile device management (MDM) compliance information with the identity provider, and use conditional access to allow only compliant, authorised devices to connect. Apply stricter rules for off-site access, such as requiring a virtual private network (VPN).
- [ ] Enable and keep audit logs for mobile device enrolment and authorisation, the results of compliance checks, and whether access attempts to mobile resources succeed or fail.
