#### AC-19.4 — Restrictions for Classified Information (Enhancement)

This requirement is about preventing people from bringing normal mobile phones and tablets into secure areas in a way that could accidentally reveal sensitive, classified information. Without these controls, an allowed device could connect to the wrong systems, copy or store sensitive material, or use wireless features in a way that bypasses safeguards—creating a real risk of unauthorised access or data leakage.

The organisation must only allow unclassified mobile devices in classified facilities when the Authorising Official has specifically approved this. Even then, the device must never be connected to any classified system. Any connection to unclassified systems must also be approved by the Authorising Official. The device must not use built-in or external phone or network connections, or wireless features such as Wi‑Fi, Bluetooth, or mobile data.

The Information System Security Officer and the Security Operations Centre incident response team must carry out random checks of permitted devices and the information stored on them. If any classified information is found, the organisation must follow its incident response plan.

For classified mobile devices, connections must be limited in line with the approved classified mobile device connection policy.

##### Allowlisted unclassified mobile devices with enforced no-wireless/no-classified

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define governance model for Authorising Official (AO) device/destination approvals, including approval reference format, facility scoping rules, and review/recertification cadence | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement device allowlist data model and workflow (device identifiers, AO approval reference, facility assignment, quarantine status) with integration-ready APIs/exports for MDM and access control | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Configure MDM/UEM enforcement profiles for permitted devices in classified facilities (disable/lock Wi‑Fi, Bluetooth, cellular/mobile data, hotspot/tethering; ensure device-level enforcement and compliance reporting) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £18,000 |
| Implement “no classified connectivity” technical controls (network segmentation, deny rules for classified IP ranges/FQDNs, block VPN/tunnel establishment, enforce ZTNA/SASE policy so no path exists to classified zones) | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 64h | £25,000 |
| Build conditional access for explicitly approved unclassified destinations (policy-as-code/approval token validation; default deny for all other unclassified destinations; support for audit trails) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £12,000 |
| Integrate facility entry/registration with allowlist (badge/QR/asset scan flow, registration gating, quarantine workflow for non-allowlisted devices, and operator/guard exception handling) | Operations Lead | Business Unit | 32h | — |
| Implement audit evidence and monitoring (SIEM log schema, event correlation for allowlist status, facility registration, MDM compliance, and denied classified connectivity attempts; dashboards and alerting for incident triggers) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £6,000 |
| Execute end-to-end validation and acceptance testing (device onboarding/offboarding, classified connectivity test attempts, wireless/modem lockdown verification, conditional access tests, and evidence review for random inspections) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 320h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £61,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an Authorising Official–approved list of allowed unclassified mobile devices for each classified facility, based on their International Mobile Equipment Identity (IMEI), serial number, and certificate.
- [ ] Link facility entry and visitor/device registration to the approved device list, so any device that is not approved is blocked or placed in quarantine.
- [ ] Set up network segmentation and zero trust network access (ZTNA), secure access service edge (SASE), and firewall rules to block all connections from approved (allowlisted) devices to classified areas, and to stop any tunnelling or virtual private network (VPN) access into classified networks.
- [ ] Set mobile device management (MDM) and unified endpoint management (UEM) rules to disable and lock Wi‑Fi, Bluetooth, mobile data, and hotspot/tethering on approved devices while they are in classified facilities.
- [ ] Set up conditional access so that access to unclassified destinations is allowed only when an Authorising Official approval reference or token is provided. Block access to all other destinations by default.
- [ ] Enable and keep audit logs showing allowlist status, facility registration, mobile device management (MDM) compliance, and network or session denials. This supports random checks by the information system security officer (ISSO) and the security operations centre (SOC), and helps with incident response.


---

#### AC-19.5 — Full Device or Container-based Encryption (Enhancement)

This requirement is about keeping sensitive information on work mobile phones and tablets protected by using encrypted “containers”, rather than leaving it exposed. Without this, a lost or misused device could reveal private files, records, or specific data, or allow unauthorised changes—damaging confidentiality and trust.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must use container-based encryption on all Department of Defence (DoD)-managed mobile devices and other endpoints. It must clearly state which specific types of data are covered (for example, files, records, or data fields) and configure the encryption so it both protects secrecy and resists tampering.

The organisation must document how the encryption is set up and what protection mechanisms are used. This must be included in the system design and the system security plan. It must also ensure the device management system produces audit records showing that encryption is enabled and recording any changes related to encryption.

Finally, named individuals must be responsible for setting it up, monitoring it, and managing changes, supported by clear procedures and instructions.

##### MDM/MAM container encryption for DoD-managed mobile endpoints

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Identify and record the population of mobile devices and other endpoint devices managed by the Department of Defense (DoD) that are covered by the mobile device management (MDM) and mobile application management (MAM) deployment.
- [ ] Define which managed-application data containers, files, records, and fields are covered by encryption, and record this scope in the configuration documentation.
- [ ] Set up mobile device management (MDM) and mobile application management (MAM) policies to encrypt the in-scope containers within a protected container, with safeguards to protect both confidentiality (keeping data private) and integrity (preventing unauthorised changes).
- [ ] Apply the encryption settings to the specified device groups and check that devices meet the requirements before allowing access to managed applications and data.
- [ ] Enable mobile device management (MDM) and mobile application management (MAM) audit logs for changes related to encryption and policy setup, and send these logs to the security information and event management (SIEM) system.
- [ ] Update the system security plan to include the container encryption method, its coverage (scope), and the agreed baseline configuration for security policies.
- [ ] Assign named responsibilities for administering encryption policies, monitoring compliance, and approving changes to what data is covered by encryption.


---

### AC-20 — Use of External Systems (Control)

This requirement is about making sure that when people use outside systems to reach the organisation’s services or handle organisation information, it is done safely and under clear, agreed rules. Without this, sensitive information could be exposed, changed, or lost because outside providers or devices may not protect data in the same way, and issues might not be detected or reported quickly.

The organisation must only allow access from external systems when the access and data-handling rules match the trust agreements it has with the owners of those external systems. These agreements must be written and must cover:
- which applications can be used
- the maximum level of information allowed (up to the Secret maximum)
- the access rules
- what activity must be recorded
- how incidents are reported within 24 hours

For any approved use of external systems, those systems must enforce strong protections, including:
- encryption when data is sent and when it is stored
- requiring a second factor to sign in (multi-factor authentication)
- keeping audit records
- managing security weaknesses

The organisation must also prohibit personally owned devices, systems managed by contractors that are not properly managed by the organisation, and public cloud services unless an approved control boundary is in place.

##### External system trust agreements with enforceable access limits

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Create “External System Trust Agreement” template (minimum clauses: allowed applications/APIs, “Secret max” ceiling, access rules, required encryption, MFA, audit logging, vulnerability management annex, and 24-hour incident/breach notification requirement) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define external-system allow-list model and mapping rules (external system type → permitted applications/APIs → maximum data classification “Secret max” → required enforcement points) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement trust agreement execution workflow and evidence pack requirements (signed agreements, register fields, version control, storage location, and audit-ready evidence checklist) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Establish technical enforcement requirements and gating controls for external access (encryption in transit/at rest, MFA policy incl. phishing-resistant where feasible, audit log enablement/forwarding to SIEM, and configuration baselines) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 28h | — |
| Define and operationalise explicit prohibitions for external system types (personally owned devices, unmanaged contractor-managed systems, and public cloud without approved authorisation boundary) including device posture checks and access-block rules | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Configure/validate audit logging and monitoring for external-system access (log sources, retention expectations, alerting/triage hooks, and evidence capture for audits) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement periodic review and configuration drift checks for external systems and trust terms (cadence, sampling approach, re-authorisation triggers, and reporting pack) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 18h | — |
| Define and test incident handling for external-system events to meet 24-hour notification (runbook updates, escalation ownership, tabletop test, and evidence of notification capability) | SOC / Incident Response Lead | Enterprise | 16h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 166h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and get approval for a template for an External System Trust Agreement. The template must set out which applications are allowed, the maximum limits for secrets, the rules for access, the logging that is required, and a requirement to report any incident within 24 hours.
- [ ] Create and keep an external-systems register that links each external system type and owner to (1) its signed trust agreement and (2) the controls it claims to have.
- [ ] Create an allow-list of approved applications and application programming interfaces (APIs), and enforce a maximum limit on how much secret data each application can access during the access approval process.
- [ ] Define which external system types are not allowed, and enforce policy checks so that personally owned devices, systems managed by contractors without approval, and unapproved public cloud services cannot be used.
- [ ] Provide evidence that data is protected while it is being sent and while it is stored (encryption in transit and encryption at rest), that multi-factor authentication (MFA) is used, that audit logs are kept, and that vulnerabilities are managed. Keep this evidence for audit purposes.
- [ ] Update the incident response plan so that, when an incident happens, the right external organisations are notified and any escalation is completed within 24 hours.


---

#### AC-20.1 — Limits on Authorized Use (Enhancement)

This requirement is about ensuring that staff can use an outside service to access your systems or handle your information only when the outside provider has been properly checked or formally agreed. If this is not done, the outside platform may not provide adequate protection or privacy, which could allow sensitive information to be leaked, changed, or used in ways your organisation never intended. This could result in financial loss, legal issues, and reputational damage.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must allow only authorised people to use external systems to access, process, store, or send organisation-controlled information after either:

- verifying that the external system has the right security and privacy protections in place (as set out in the organisation’s own policies and plans), or  
- keeping an approved written agreement with the organisation that hosts the external system.

The organisation must also keep the relevant evidence or approved agreement on file, so it can be shown when access is granted.

| Integrate enforcement signals with identity/authorisation (policy evaluation, attribute/entitlement mapping, service account handling, break-glass/exception path with compensating controls) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 280h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £18,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an external systems register that lists every external system used to access, and to process, store, or transmit organisation-controlled information.
- [ ] Publish an external assurance checklist that matches the organisation’s security and privacy policies and plans
- [ ] Set up an onboarding process that prevents approval of access to external systems unless an assurance record exists and has been approved.
- [ ] Define what evidence is required and the conditions for passing independent assessments or attestations, then match the evidence to the checklist.
- [ ] Set up conditional access and zero trust network access (ZTNA), or an equivalent control, so that access is allowed only when the assurance record status is **Approved** or **Verified**.
- [ ] Store and keep audit-ready assurance records that link each external system to the verification evidence or the approved agreement, including the dates and the reviewer names.

#### AC-20.2 — Portable Storage Devices — Restricted Use (Enhancement)

This expectation is about tightly controlling company USB sticks and other approved portable storage devices when they are connected to other people’s computers or external computers. The goal is to stop them being used to spread harmful software or move data to places where it should not go. Without these controls, a device could bring viruses or other malicious code into a new system, start unwanted software as soon as it is connected, or allow information to be copied onto removable media that has not been approved.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must allow only authorised staff to use these devices for approved work purposes, and only on external systems that have been given written permission for that use. The devices must be encrypted, checked for threats immediately before and after each use, blocked from copying data to any unmanaged removable media, and configured so that auto-start behaviour is turned off when connected.

The organisation should also keep clear written procedures, policies, and records of system settings. These records should name who is responsible and include agreements that set out when and how these devices may be used.

##### Workflow-controlled encrypted USBs with scan-before/after and no auto-run

| Select and configure centrally managed encrypted USB approach (hardware-encrypted USB or centrally managed OS-level encryption), including device inventory model and encryption-status evidence capture | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | £18,000 |
| Implement auto-run/auto-play disablement baseline on issued devices and produce configuration evidence (e.g., registry/firmware settings, validation test results) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Build workflow in ITSM/secure portal for scan-before/after checkout: capture identity, approved mission task reference, external system identifier, written authorisation/ticket ID, time window, and enforce release rules | Project Manager | Enterprise | 56h | £6,000 |
| Implement managed scanning kiosk/endpoint integration: connect/disconnect orchestration, malware scan-before and scan-after, quarantine/block actions, and timestamped scan results export to audit logs/SIEM | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | £25,000 |
| Enforce “no copying to unmanaged media” on external systems used by the workflow: define technical restriction patterns, implement removable-media write restrictions where feasible, and create a gating check for systems that cannot be controlled | Infrastructure Lead | Enterprise | 48h | £10,000 |
| Operationalise audit evidence and reporting: end-to-end evidence pack (encryption active, auto-run disabled, workflow approvals, scan timestamps/results, quarantine actions) plus dashboards and periodic access/control effectiveness reviews | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £4,000 |

| Total Estimated Effort | 282h |  |
|---|---:|---:|
| Total Estimated Cost |  | £63,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set the approved security standards for encrypted portable devices, and publish the approved build and configuration starting points, with automatic start-up disabled.
- [ ] Set up an information technology service management (ITSM) and secure portal process that records: the user’s identity, the approved mission task, the external system identifier, and the written authorisation reference.
- [ ] Set up a secured scanning kiosk, or a managed endpoint, that checks for malware as soon as a device is connected and again as soon as the device is returned.
- [ ] Set up devices so that when they are connected, auto-run or auto-play cannot start software automatically, and so that configuration records are kept for audit purposes.
- [ ] Set up workflow controls so devices can only be checked out by explicitly authorised external systems during approved time windows.
- [ ] Work with the owners of external systems to put in place controls that stop users copying data to unmanaged removable storage, and record confirmation.

#### AC-20.3 — Non-organizationally Owned Systems — Restricted Use (Enhancement)

This requirement is about preventing staff from using other people’s systems, or their own personal devices, to handle the organisation’s information unless it is done in a tightly controlled way. Without this, sensitive information could be exposed, lost, or accessed by the wrong people because external systems may not protect information to the same standard, and personal devices are harder to manage and investigate if something goes wrong.

The organisation must clearly define what counts as a non-organisation-owned system or component. It must only allow such systems to process, store, or send organisational information after getting prior approval, using security protections the organisation has already reviewed and agreed, and limiting access to Confidential or Secret information only. Personally owned devices must not be used to process Classified information.

The organisation must put these rules into written procedures and agreements, document how the systems are set up to enforce the limits, assign named responsibilities, and keep records showing who used which system or device and when.

##### Approval-gated external/non-owned system access with data-class limits

| Create approval-gated ITSM workflow with mandatory prior approvals (Information Security + System/Network/Application owner), including checklist sign-off and evidence capture requirements | Project Manager | Enterprise | 32h | £3,000 |
| Implement IAM authorisation model to bind access to approvals and enforce maximum allowed classification (Confidential/Secret only) via conditional access / authorisation decisions | IAM team | Enterprise | 56h | £10,000 |
| Implement technical enforcement for BYOD and Classified scope: automatically deny/reject requests when device is identified as personally owned for Classified processing | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £5,000 |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 298h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £36,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create an IT service management (ITSM) service request process for systems and components that are not owned by the organisation, and for bring your own device (BYOD). The process must record the system’s identity, its purpose, how it connects, and the data classification being requested.
- [ ] Define and publish a controlled classification (taxonomy) for systems and components that are not owned by the organisation, and link each classification to the required approval route.
- [ ] Set up approval checkpoints so permission cannot be granted unless the Information Security team and the system or network owner have signed off on the approved security controls.
- [ ] Set up identity and access management (IAM) conditional access and application and data authorisation to allow only Confidential and Secret information, and to prevent personally owned devices from being used to process Classified information.
- [ ] For every approved use of a non-owned system or component, require acceptance of the legal-approved usage terms, including expectations for incident handling and digital forensics when using a personal device (bring your own device, BYOD).
- [ ] Store approval records and proof that controls were enforced (checklist sign-off, highest classification level, applied policies, and denial logs) so they are available for audit record retention.

#### AC-20.4 — Network Accessible Storage Devices — Prohibited Use (Enhancement)

This requirement is about preventing staff systems from using any shared storage that can be reached over a network from outside your organisation, including online storage provided through public, hybrid, or community cloud services. If this is not done, sensitive information could be copied, accessed, or exposed using external storage locations that are harder to control, increasing the risk of unauthorised access, data loss, or misuse by partners or other third parties.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly state in its access rules and supporting procedures that all network-accessible storage devices (for example, network-attached storage, storage networks, network file shares, and cloud object storage endpoints) are not allowed in external systems. This must also be reflected in system design, configuration settings, and the organisation’s security plan. The organisation must keep an up-to-date list of the specific storage targets that are prohibited, ensure any external connection or processing agreements include the same ban, and keep audit records showing that prohibited storage was not used.

##### Block and evidence prohibition of external network storage use

- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

| Define and approve the **Prohibited Storage Target Registry** schema (fields, classification, ownership, change workflow) and create initial registry entries for known external storage patterns/endpoints (approved external SaaS domains, partner buckets/containers, SMB/NFS share patterns, object endpoints) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement technical enforcement baseline: egress deny-by-default controls (firewall/proxy rules) for prohibited storage endpoints by FQDN/IP and protocol/port where feasible; ensure application and managed workloads cannot reach prohibited targets | Infrastructure Lead | Business Unit | 40h | £3,000 |
| Implement IAM allow-list enforcement for storage access: remove broad storage permissions, require explicit time-bound approvals for exceptions, and ensure service accounts cannot obtain roles/credentials enabling prohibited external storage access | IAM Lead | Enterprise | 32h | — |

|---|---:|---:|

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Update the access control policy and the application system security plan to clearly forbid “ac-20.04_odp” in external systems, including public, hybrid, and community cloud online storage.
- [ ] Set up and keep a Prohibited Storage Target Register (endpoints, network shares, storage buckets, and containers) with named owners and a process for managing changes.
- [ ] Set up outbound blocking rules in the egress proxy and firewall to prevent access to prohibited storage targets. Block connections to prohibited storage targets by hostname or fully qualified domain name (FQDN), using the specific network protocol and port for Server Message Block (SMB), Network File System (NFS), and object storage.
- [ ] Use an identity and access management (IAM) allow-list for storage access, so application workloads and service accounts cannot connect to external storage endpoints that are not permitted.
- [ ] Set up conditional access and service account restrictions to stop interactive logins and automated workloads from accessing any prohibited storage consoles or application programming interfaces (APIs).
- [ ] Set up and centralise logging for storage access attempts and blocked outbound (egress) network events, then match the results against the prohibited registry to support audit reporting.
- [ ] Add the storage restriction clause to any external connection and processing agreements for partner or vendor integrations that could involve storing data outside the organisation.

#### AC-20.5 — Portable Storage Devices — Prohibited Use (Enhancement)

This requirement is a strict rule: staff must not plug the organisation’s own USB drives or other organisation-managed portable storage into systems that the organisation does not directly control. The real-world risk is that these devices can carry malware or copy sensitive information into partner, customer, contractor, or other external environments, sometimes without anyone noticing until harm has already occurred.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must clearly define what counts as an external system and publish a complete ban in its access rules and supporting procedures, so staff understand what is allowed and what is not. The organisation must also enforce the ban in practice, using a combination of system settings that block portable storage where possible and documented processes such as training and approvals for any required movement of data.

Responsibility must be assigned to named roles, including system and network administrators and information security staff. The organisation must also build the ban into system design and security planning, include it in connection or processing agreements, and keep audit records showing that the rule is being applied.

##### Deny organisation USB use on external systems via endpoint policy

- Priority: Critical

|---|---|---:|---:|---:|

**Total Estimated Effort:** 120h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and publish what counts as an “external system” in the access control policy and the supporting procedure.
- [ ] Create an “external access” device-control policy for endpoints that blocks USB mass storage and other removable media.
- [ ] Apply the “deny” rule only when certain external-access conditions are met (for example, the virtual private network (VPN) security status or the external-access device group).
- [ ] Set up logging to record attempts to connect removable media, including any block or denial results, and send these event records to the security information and event management (SIEM) system.
- [ ] Document and publish approved non-Universal Serial Bus (USB) secure file-transfer options for any required data movement.
- [ ] Set up an exception process that requires approval from Information Security and keeps a written record, so the ban remains the default option.

### AC-21 — Information Sharing (Control)

This expectation is about making sure sensitive information is shared only with the right partners, for the right reasons, and only under the correct legal and access rules. Without it, an organisation could accidentally disclose classified or contract-sensitive material to someone who is not properly authorised, or share it without the required agreements. This could cause serious legal, financial, and reputational harm.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must provide authorised staff with a way to check that the access given to a sharing partner matches the specific restrictions attached to the information. This includes any special access programme or compartment rules, and any non-disclosure agreement requirements.

The organisation must also provide clear, policy-based guidance that uses the information’s sensitivity labels, carries out automated eligibility checks, and prompts the user to confirm that the required agreement and special access conditions are in place before sharing.

Where automation is not sufficient, the organisation must set out when staff must use judgement, and require them to record the decision and the reasons for it.

##### Policy-based sharing workflow with NDA/SAP access-match prompts

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define controlled classification-to-restriction mapping model (tags, allowed actions, partner types, NDA/SAP/compartment flags, discretion circumstances, and rule evaluation logic) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Design information-item metadata binding approach (schema/attributes, validation at ingestion/creation, and enforcement points across document/dataset/message types) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 48h | — |
| Implement partner eligibility & authorisation directory (data model, ingestion from IAM/entitlements and contract/NDA repositories, evidence fields, and reconciliation process) | IAM/Entitlements Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £25,000 |
| Build sharing request workflow with access-match engine (derive required restrictions from tags, evaluate partner eligibility for requested access type, produce pass/fail outcomes, and generate rule evaluation details) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 96h | — |
| Implement mandatory NDA/SAP/compartment prompts/validations (UI/API flows, evidence capture, non-bypass enforcement, and blocking logic until validations succeed) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 64h | — |
| Add guided manual override path for defined discretion (rationale capture, approval/ticket reference linkage, policy-allowed override checks, and audit evidence requirements) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement tamper-evident audit logging & SIEM integration (audit record schema, integrity controls, retention alignment, and dashboards for compliance review) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 56h | £18,000 |
| Execute end-to-end testing & assurance (test cases for pass/fail, prompt blocking, override scenarios, negative tests, performance checks, and evidence pack for AC-21 alignment) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 48h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 440h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £43,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define classification labels and link each label to the access and use restrictions that apply, including requirements related to a non-disclosure agreement (NDA) and SAP systems, including SAP “compartments”.
- [ ] Ensure that all information items that can be shared within the application have machine-readable labels and access restrictions applied.
- [ ] Set up the sharing process so it checks partner eligibility using identity and access management (IAM) and entitlements, and by verifying records in the contract and non-disclosure agreement (NDA) repositories, to enable access to the NDA and SAP (systems, applications and products) compartments.
- [ ] Carry out an access check that compares what the partner is authorised to access with the restrictions required for the requested type of access.
- [ ] Set up mandatory non-disclosure agreement (NDA) checks and SAP and compartment validation prompts, and prevent sharing until all validations are completed.
- [ ] Create a controlled manual override route only for the organisation-approved discretion situations, and require a clear reason plus recorded evidence.
- [ ] Set up audit logs that show whether records have been changed for every sharing decision, including the tags used, the results of automated checks, whether the required prompt was completed, and the reason for any override.


---

#### AC-21.1 — Automated Decision Support (Enhancement)

This requirement is about making sure information is shared only when the right people ask for it, and that the system automatically and consistently checks that the receiving organisation is allowed to receive that specific information. Without this, staff could accidentally (or inappropriately) share sensitive material with the wrong organisation, or share more than they should, which could cause legal, financial, and reputational harm.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must set up rules-based processes and approval checkpoints so that sharing decisions can be triggered only by staff who are authorised to make those decisions. Every request must be automatically checked against two things: (1) whether the partner is currently allowed to receive information, and (2) the specific limits that apply to the information being shared.

The organisation must also keep up-to-date records of who is allowed to make decisions, which partners are allowed to receive information, and what limits apply. The system must be configured to enforce these rules without allowing manual workarounds, and the organisation must document how the automated checks work, so there is evidence that the system’s decisions were based on the correct, up-to-date information.

##### Policy-driven sharing workflow with partner and data restriction checks

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define machine-readable policy model for information restrictions (categories/objects → allowed partner types, required approval tier, expiry/handling constraints) including schema and versioning approach | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Define machine-readable partner authorisation model (partner identity/tenant/SP → authorised information categories and scopes) including ownership/change-control workflow | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Design and implement decision workflow enforcement (only decision-maker/approver role can initiate/approve; remove/disable bypass paths for UI/API; route all sharing requests through workflow engine) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Implement automated evaluation service (pre-activation checks: partner authorisation match + information restriction satisfaction; deterministic allow/deny outcomes; fail-closed behaviour) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 96h | — |
| Implement auditable decision records and SIEM/log forwarding (decision evidence fields, correlation IDs, retention alignment, tamper-evident logging approach) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Build integration points and test harness (connect to IAM for roles, to sharing/ACL provisioning mechanism, and to logging/SIEM; create automated test cases for allow/deny, edge cases, and regression) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 64h | — |
| Operationalise policy data governance (authorisation/restriction ownership process, periodic review cadence, workflow configuration release through change management; runbooks and monitoring/alerting for denied requests) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 400h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £0

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create a machine-readable mapping that links shareable information categories or items to the rules that restrict who can access them.
- [ ] Create a machine-readable list that links each sharing partner to the permissions they have for each information category.
- [ ] Create separate identity and access management (IAM) roles for people who approve sharing decisions, and limit their permissions to the minimum needed (least privilege).
- [ ] Set up a workflow checkpoint so every sharing request must first pass automated checks for partner approval and information access restrictions before it is enabled.
- [ ] Remove or disable direct sharing options (through the user interface or application programming interface) for people who are not authorised decision-makers, to prevent them from bypassing the process.
- [ ] Create system-generated records of decisions that show the rules that were checked, the partner identity, the information identifier and category, the result, and the date and time.
- [ ] Connect decision logs to security information and event management (SIEM) and other logging systems, and check that audit records can be traced from the original request through to the point where sharing is activated.

#### AC-21.2 — Information Search and Retrieval (Enhancement)

This requirement ensures that when people search for documents or information, they only see content they are officially authorised to access, and only in the approved circumstances for sensitive material. Without this, someone could accidentally or deliberately find restricted **Secret** or **Confidential** information, or share it with the wrong customer, partner, country, or programme. This could create serious legal and contractual risk, including breaches of export-control and compliance rules.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must clearly define who can receive **Secret** and **Confidential** information and the approved limits for sharing it. It must then configure its search service to filter results according to the user’s permissions and the item’s sharing rules. The organisation must also follow the applicable export-control and compliance requirements for **Secret** and **Confidential** data, keep documented procedures and design information that explain how these restrictions work, and retain records of searches and the decisions made. This allows the organisation to review and demonstrate what was shown or blocked.

##### ABAC policy-as-code filtering for Secret/Confidential search results

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define authoritative Secret/Confidential metadata model (classification, ITAR/EAR tags, CMMC-L2/L3 requirements, sharing-boundary attributes) and indexing schema for the search service | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Define user/recipient attribute model and ABAC evaluation inputs (clearance/authorisation, permitted programmes, permitted countries/partners, CMMC eligibility) and integration contract with IAM/authorisation service | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement policy-as-code rules for ABAC enforcement (allow/withhold decision logic, reason codes, and mapping of ITAR/EAR + CMMC constraints to sharing boundaries) | Security Engineer | Department | 56h | — |
| Build restriction-list compilation pipeline (compile/version policies + authoritative metadata into an environment-held restriction list; ensure dev/test/prod consistency) | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £8,000 |
| Integrate ABAC decisioning into search query-time and result-time flows (prevent leakage via ranking/snippets/metadata; ensure downstream retrieval/export reuses the same decision context) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 72h | — |
| Implement audit logging for enforcement decisions (capture query context, user identity, item identifiers, decision outcome, reason codes; forward to SIEM with required retention/evidence fields) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 32h | £3,000 |
| Create automated policy validation test suite (representative Secret/Confidential fixtures; boundary mismatch and ITAR/EAR/CMMC denial scenarios; regression tests on policy changes) | Quality Assurance Lead | Department | 48h | — |
| Operationalise change control for policies (versioning, approval workflow, release gating, and rollback strategy for policy-as-code and restriction lists) | Project Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 328h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £11,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and document the rules for sharing Secret/Confidential information across programme, customer, partner, and country boundaries, and link those rules to the United States International Traffic in Arms Regulations (ITAR), the United States Export Administration Regulations (EAR), and the Cybersecurity Maturity Model Certification level 2 and level 3 (CMMC-L2/L3) requirements.
- [ ] Model and label indexed content with its security classification, International Traffic in Arms Regulations (ITAR) and Export Administration Regulations (EAR) tags, the required Cybersecurity Maturity Model Certification (CMMC) level, and boundary attributes.
- [ ] Set user or recipient permission details in the identity layer, including clearance or authorisation level, which programmes they are allowed to access, which countries or partners they are allowed to work with, and whether they are eligible for the Cybersecurity Maturity Model Certification (CMMC).
- [ ] Set up attribute-based access control (ABAC) rules as code, linked to the search service, so every search request is checked and the results are filtered when the query is run.
- [ ] Ensure that any later retrieval or export of data from search results uses the same attribute-based access control (ABAC) decision, and cannot avoid the filtering rules.
- [ ] Create and deploy a restriction list stored within the system, based on approved policies and official metadata, with version control.
- [ ] Set up audit records for all search queries and the decisions made about them (allowed, withheld, or filtered), including reason codes, and send these records to the security information and event management (SIEM) system.

### AC-22 — Publicly Accessible Content (Control)

This requirement is about stopping private or confidential information from being accidentally published on your organisation’s public website or other public-facing pages. Without it, staff could share sensitive material such as private personal details, internal documents, confidential contract information, or proprietary information. This could lead to legal issues, reputational damage, and harm to customers or employees.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must:
- appoint specific people who are authorised to publish public content,
- train them so they clearly understand they must not include any information that is not meant for public release, and
- put a process in place to review every proposed item before it is posted, to confirm it contains nothing that should remain private.

After content goes live, the organisation must check the public-facing pages every day and promptly remove anything that is found to be non-public. It must also keep records of these checks and any actions taken.

##### Authorised public publishing workflow with daily review evidence

- Category: Manual
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define scope of “publicly accessible systems” covered by AC-22 (CMS/web pages, downloads, knowledge bases, landing pages, public portals) and document inclusion/exclusion criteria | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 12h | — |
| Create and maintain the authorised publisher list (source of truth) including roles/named individuals, evidence of training/authorisation, and effective dates; publish governance procedure for updates | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Implement CMS/web workflow gates and RBAC mapping: drafts-only for publishers; production publish restricted to designated approvers; ensure publish actions require a linked pre-publication approval reference created before publish timestamp | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | £3,000 |
| Design and publish the mandatory pre-publication checklist (per item) covering common non-public information categories; configure checklist completion as a required step before approval | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Establish daily review procedure and evidence capture: create daily checklist, define review frequency parameter (“daily”), identify high-risk sections (news/updates, downloads, “latest”, FAQs), and set up ticketing/GRC log template for audit evidence | Service Delivery Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |
| Implement prompt removal/rollback playbook with remediation evidence: define rollback mechanism, ownership for immediate action, required fields (what/when/who), and outcome recording; run a tabletop exercise to validate responsiveness | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 18h | — |
| Validate authorisation drift controls: monthly reconciliation of authorised publisher list vs CMS permissions; produce discrepancy reports and remediation actions with audit trail | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 14h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 144h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £3,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define and document the scope of publicly accessible systems that are managed by the organisation and that are covered by AC-22.
- [ ] Create and keep an up-to-date list of authorised publishers, including the named people and the date of their most recent training and authorisation.
- [ ] Set up content management system (CMS) and website role-based access control (RBAC) so that only approved users can publish to the live (production) site, and other publishers can only create draft content.
- [ ] Introduce a mandatory pre-publication checklist and require a recorded approval reference before anything can be published.
- [ ] Assign a reviewer role to carry out and record a daily review of publicly accessible pages, using a repeatable checklist.
- [ ] Create and practise a documented removal or rollback plan for any discovered non-public information, with records that can be audited.
- [ ] Carry out a regular check to confirm that content management system (CMS) publishing permissions still match the approved list of authorised publishers.

### AC-23 — Data Mining Protection (Control)

This requirement is about preventing people from repeatedly querying sensitive databases to gradually uncover confidential information, even if they are initially allowed to ask questions. Without these protections, someone could automate many queries to identify patterns or extract exact details, which could expose personal data or other highly sensitive secrets, including through misuse by insiders.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must first clearly identify which database records and which specific fields are classified as Confidential or Secret. It must also define and document which types of data analysis are genuinely authorised, including a process to check authorisation before any data mining takes place.

The organisation must then limit how often and how many queries can be run against that sensitive data. It must allow only the minimum access needed for each authorised task, and block or restrict requests that go beyond the permitted scope.

It must also monitor for unusual query behaviour, alert the right people so they can investigate, and keep audit records for review. Where feasible, it should use privacy-preserving ways of sharing results, so that repeated querying is harder to exploit.

##### Policy-enforced query gateway for protected data mining

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Design the policy-enforced query gateway architecture (request flow, enforcement points, decision model, integration boundaries with DB/API) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Create protected-data mapping catalogue (record/field-to-policy identifiers, governance workflow, versioning, and promotion across environments) | Data Protection Officer | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Implement policy-as-code allowlisted query templates/operations (authorised mining techniques, query-shape validation, required predicates, permitted join patterns) | Software Lead | Enterprise | 120h | — |
| Enforce least-privilege at query time (reject/rewrite logic for unauthorised fields/records, scope expansion controls, result cardinality limits, extraction-shape detection) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 96h | — |
| Implement rate limiting/query throttling per identity and per protected object (interactive vs service accounts, adaptive thresholds, backoff, and throttling responses) | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 72h | — |
| Build telemetry, audit logging, and SIEM/SOAR alerting for atypical mining-like behaviour (query hash/shape, targeted objects, estimated cardinality, baselines, alert rules) | Cyber Security Lead | Enterprise | 88h | — |
| Integrate differential privacy (DP) where feasible (DP-enabled endpoints/stored procedures for at least one representative analytics use-case; prevent raw extraction paths; document compensating controls if DP not feasible) | Architect | Enterprise | 80h | £25,000 |
| Execute end-to-end testing & evidence pack (test cases for allow/deny/throttle, performance/load tests, red-team style query attempts, audit-ready evidence: policy config + decision logs + alert coverage) | Quality Assurance Lead | Enterprise | 64h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 616h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £25,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Create and keep up to date a protected-data catalogue that links Confidential and Secret database records and fields to the gateway policy identifiers.
- [ ] Set up a query gateway (service layer) that is the required route for all queries that access protected data storage objects.
- [ ] Encode approved data-mining methods as pre-approved (allowlisted) query templates and required conditions (policy-as-code).
- [ ] Set rate-limiting and query-throttling limits for each user identity and each protected resource, and enforce these limits at the gateway.
- [ ] Apply the principle of least privilege to database queries, so that any query trying to access more data than it is allowed to (unauthorised fields, rows, or an excessive number of results) is rejected or adjusted.
- [ ] Integrate information about database queries with security information and event management (SIEM) and security orchestration, automation and response (SOAR), and set up alerts for unusual query patterns or query volumes aimed at protected objects.
- [ ] Enable differential privacy for analytics endpoints where it is practical, and ensure the gateway routes analytics that use protected fields through differential privacy (DP) controls.

### AC-24 — Access Control Decisions (Control)

This requirement ensures that every time someone tries to use a system or access a resource, the organisation’s permission decision is made first. Access is only allowed or blocked after that decision has been completed. Without this, there is a risk that people could gain access when they should not, or that sensitive actions could occur before the organisation has properly checked whether the person is authorised. This could lead to data loss, fraud, or disruption.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must produce clear, documented procedures that explain how permission decisions are made for every access attempt, and how those decisions are applied before access is enforced. The organisation must also configure its systems so this “decision before access” process applies to all relevant types of access, including logins, files or shared folders, applications, and administrative actions. Finally, it must keep audit records showing the outcome of each access request, so the organisation can demonstrate what happened.

##### Enforce decision-before-access via PDP/PEP for every request

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define the request-time authorisation model (PDP inputs/outputs, decision identifiers, allow/deny semantics, default-deny/unreachable PDP behaviour) and map it to AC-24 evidence requirements | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design PDP/PEP architecture and integration points for all access paths (web/API/admin endpoints, service-to-service calls, background jobs) including interception/gating strategy | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement PDP decision service (policy evaluation, context enrichment from IdP claims, resource/action mapping, decision ID generation, deny reason handling) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 80h | — |
| Implement PEP enforcement across the application/API layer (middleware/gateway/service-mesh/sidecar) to block execution until PDP decision is received; ensure no success/data/privileged action occurs pre-decision | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 96h | — |
| Implement end-to-end audit logging and correlation (request ID, subject, resource, action, PDP decision outcome/ID, enforcement outcome) and forward to SIEM with retention-aligned configuration | SOC/SIEM Engineer | Department | 40h | £6,000 |
| Create documented “decision-before-enforcement” procedure and runbook (scope of access requests, where PDP/PEP sit, failure modes, operational checks, evidence to retain) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Develop automated tests and verification harness (integration tests proving deny requests never reach business logic; allow requests include PDP decision ID; resilience tests for PDP latency/unreachable) | Quality Assurance Lead | Team | 56h | — |

| Total Estimated Effort | 352h | Total Estimated Cost | £6,000 |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the decision inputs and outputs for the personal data processing (PDP) process—subject, resource, action, and context—and set out the rules for when the system will allow or deny the request (the allow/deny decision contract).
- [ ] Set up a policy enforcement point (PEP) at every access route (API gateway, middleware, and service mesh) so requests are checked and stopped before they reach business logic.
- [ ] Set up “request-time gating” so enforcement either returns a success response or carries out the required actions only after a policy decision point (PDP) decision is received.
- [ ] Set “fail closed” behaviour (deny access) when no policy decision is available, or document and put in place an approved alternative control to compensate.
- [ ] Add audit logging that records the request ID, the decision made by the policy decision point, and the final enforcement result for every access request.
- [ ] Document the decision-before-enforcement process for both standard access and administrative access.
- [ ] Create automated tests that confirm the decision is made before any enforcement action, for both “allow” and “deny” scenarios.


---

#### AC-24.1 — Transmit Access Authorization Information (Enhancement)

This requirement is about protecting the permission information your organisation sends to the systems that actually allow or block access. If this is not protected end-to-end, an attacker could intercept the permission message, alter it, pretend it came from a trusted decision-maker, or send it to the wrong destination. This could result in unauthorised access or incorrect denials.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must package the authorisation details into signed authorisation tokens. These tokens must clearly state:
- who is requesting access (the subject),
- what is being accessed (the resource),
- what the requester wants to do (the action),
- and any security or privacy attributes needed to make the decision.

These signed tokens must be sent over a mutually authenticated encrypted connection, where both sides prove they are the correct parties. The connection must also include extra checks to ensure only the expected certificates are accepted, and the message must be protected so any tampering is detected.

The systems that enforce access must verify the token signature before using it to allow or block access. They must also keep evidence in system records, along with documented design and configuration settings.

##### Secure transmission of signed authorisation tokens to API enforcement

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define signed authorisation token schema (claims: subject, resource, action, security/privacy attributes; include audience/target enforcement point; define canonicalisation and expiry/nonce rules) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Select and implement signing approach (JWS/JWT profile, key identifiers, algorithm constraints, claim validation requirements) and produce token specification document for enforcement integration | Architect | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| Provision managed signing keys in KMS/HSM (create key policy, rotation schedule, access controls, audit logging, test keys for non-prod) | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 24h | £12,000 |
| Implement token signing in the authorisation decision service (library integration, deterministic claim mapping, signing/expiry handling, correlation IDs) | Software Lead | Business Unit | 32h | — |
| Implement mutual TLS between decision service and federated API enforcement points (mTLS configuration, trust store management, service identity mapping) | Platform Engineer | Business Unit | 24h | — |
| Implement enforcement point verification-before-decision pipeline (mandatory mTLS peer validation → token signature verification → claim/audience/target validation → allow/deny) with secure failure handling | API/Gateway Engineering Lead | Department | 40h | — |
| Enable certificate pinning and rotation process (pin configuration, staged rollout strategy, rotation runbook, automated validation in CI/CD) | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Produce audit-ready evidence pack (configuration exports, sample signed tokens, verification logs for success/failure cases, test-to-prod integration walkthrough) | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 16h | — |
| **Total Estimated Effort** |  |  | **200h** |  |
| **Total Estimated Cost** |  |  |  | **£12,000** |

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Define the structure for the signed access authorisation token, including the identity of the user (subject), the target system or data (resource), the permitted activity (action), and the security and privacy requirements that must be included.
- [ ] Use key management service (KMS) or hardware security module (HSM) managed keys to sign tokens (JSON Web Signature (JWS), JSON Web Token (JWT), or an equivalent method), and enforce that tokens are only accepted for the intended audience or target by binding this requirement at the enforcement point.
- [ ] Set up mutual Transport Layer Security (mutual TLS) between the authorisation decision service and the federated application programming interface (API) enforcement points, using strict certificate checks.
- [ ] Set up certificate pinning so the system only trusts the expected peer certificate or public key, and put in place a controlled process to rotate those pins when needed.
- [ ] Set up enforcement-point checks to confirm the other party’s identity using mutual Transport Layer Security (mTLS) and to verify the token’s signature and claims before making any allow or deny decision.
- [ ] Add “deny on failure” behaviour and audit logging for token verification and mutual Transport Layer Security (mTLS) validation outcomes, using correlation identifiers to link related events.


---

#### AC-24.2 — No User or Process Identity (Enhancement)

This expectation is about making access decisions without relying on who the person is, or on which system process is acting on their behalf. Instead, the organisation should decide whether someone can read, write, or run something using only agreed information about the item itself. For example, this could include its resource classification label, how the data is meant to be handled, and the access purpose code. Alternatively, the organisation can base decisions on where the item sits in the system and the type of access needed. Where privacy is involved, decisions should use only the privacy purpose and the data minimisation category.

Without this approach, the wrong people could be given access because the decision is quietly influenced by personal identifiers. It could also undermine privacy by collecting and using unnecessary identity details.

To meet this requirement, the organisation must:
- define and document these “identity-free” access decision rules;
- configure systems so the rules are enforced exactly as written;
- ensure staff and developers follow the documented approach; and
- keep clear records showing that decisions were based on these attributes, not on user identity or process identity, including in the organisation’s security and privacy plans where relevant.

##### Identity-free ABAC decision engine using purpose/classification attributes

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|
| Define the identity-free ABAC attribute model aligned to AC-24.2_prm_1 (e.g., resource classification label, data handling category, access purpose code; optional privacy purpose, data minimisation category; optional enclave/zone + required access mode) and document allowed attribute sources and formats | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Design the trusted “access context” contract (e.g., signed JWT claims / mTLS service intent / internal policy-context service) that carries only identity-free attributes; specify integrity protection, expiry, replay protection, and validation rules | Architect | Enterprise | 32h | — |
| Implement policy-as-code for allow/deny rules with explicit exclusion of identity fields (no subject/actor/user/process references in rule conditions); include a reference policy library and rule templates for common decision patterns | Software Lead | Enterprise | 56h | — |
| Configure and integrate the enforcement point (API gateway / service mesh authoriser / application authorisation middleware) so all services evaluate the same identity-free policy and reject requests with missing/invalid identity-free context | Platform Engineer | Enterprise | 40h | — |
| Add CI/CD automated policy checks to prevent merges when allow/deny logic references identity fields (static analysis/linters + unit tests with identity-field fixtures) and provide developer guidance for compliant policy authoring | DevOps Lead | Enterprise | 24h | £6,000 |
| Implement audit evidence generation: log the exact identity-free attribute values used for each decision, with clear separation from any identity metadata; ensure logs are structured for SIEM ingestion and support audit queries | Security Engineer | Enterprise | 32h | £3,000 |
| Produce security & privacy documentation pack for AC-24(2) enhancement: attribute definitions, integrity assurance for access context, enforcement-point consistency, audit evidence mapping, and operational runbook for troubleshooting | Compliance Manager | Enterprise | 20h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 228h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £9,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Set the authorisation attributes that do not rely on a user identity to match **ac-24.2_prm_1** exactly (and any chosen privacy, secure-environment, and access-mode attributes). Then link each resource and application programming interface (API) to those same values.
- [ ] Set up a trusted access-context system that protects data integrity and sends only identity-free information to the policy enforcement point.
- [ ] Set up the policy engine and rules so that any allow or deny conditions use only identity-free attributes, and do not use any user or process identity fields.
- [ ] Add continuous integration and continuous delivery (CI/CD) checks that stop a build from completing if the policy code refers to identity fields (for example, subject or user ID, actor ID, or process ID) anywhere in any allow or deny rules.
- [ ] Apply access checks consistently at the point where requests enter the system (the application programming interface (API) gateway/service mesh/application authorisation layer), so every request follows the same decision process without relying on identity information.
- [ ] Set up audit logging for authorisation decisions that records the attribute values used in each decision, without recording any user identity (separate from any user identity logging).
- [ ] Update the security documentation (and privacy documentation, if used) to explain:

- what each attribute means and how it is defined  
- where the information used for each attribute comes from  
- the controls used to keep that information accurate and unaltered  
- how evidence is produced to show the controls and data are working correctly


---

### AC-25 — Reference Monitor (Control)

This requirement is about having one dedicated “gatekeeper” inside the system that always decides who is allowed to view or use Confidential and Secret information before anything is released. Without this, access rules can be applied inconsistently, accidentally skipped, or an attacker could try to change how decisions are made so unauthorised people gain access.

To meet this expectation, the organisation must apply the Department of Defence access rules for Confidential and Secret data. This includes making access decisions based on a person’s role and attributes, and following the principle of least privilege (only the minimum access needed). The organisation must enforce these decisions through a tamper-resistant gatekeeper that is always consulted for access decisions and cannot be bypassed by any other route.

The gatekeeper must be small and clearly defined so its behaviour can be fully analysed and tested. The organisation must keep documented evidence that it makes the correct allow-or-deny decisions, records the outcome, and blocks and logs unauthorised attempts to interfere with the gatekeeper or its rules.

##### Tamper-resistant always-invoked reference monitor for DoD data

- Category: Software
- Priority: Critical

| Task / Deliverable | Owner Role | Org Level | Effort (Hours) | Cost (GBP) |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Define mediation boundary and “always-invoked” coverage model for Confidential/Secret objects (including deny-by-default for unlabelled/unknown objects) | System Design Authority | Enterprise | 24h | — |
| Implement reference monitor decision engine (bounded allow/deny logic) with RBAC/ABAC policy evaluation context mapping (subject attributes, object labels/classification, requested action) | Software Lead | Department | 80h | — |
| Implement enforcement mechanism to guarantee mediation at the access primitive (e.g., single data-access wrapper/library or OS/kernel MAC mediation integration) and remove/disable bypass routes | Platform Engineer | Department | 96h | — |
| Implement tamper-resistance controls: signed/immutable policy bundles, restricted admin paths, runtime integrity verification, and bypass detection with fail-closed behaviour | Security Engineer | Department | 72h | £15,000 |
| Build audit/decision record pipeline (decision fields: subject, object label/classification, action, allow/deny, correlation identifiers) and integrate with SIEM/central logging | Operations Lead | Enterprise | 40h | £8,000 |
| Create test harness and evidence pack: unit/integration tests with documented test vectors (positive/negative/boundary), completeness review, and repeatable execution for AC-25 | Quality Assurance Lead | Team | 64h | — |
| Produce deployment and operational runbooks (configuration management, release controls, monitoring/alerting for bypass attempts, and periodic evidence refresh) | Service Delivery Manager | Department | 24h | — |

**Total Estimated Effort:** 400h  
**Total Estimated Cost:** £23,000

###### Actions Required for Compliance

- [ ] Choose and document the single “mediation boundary” (the reference monitor enforcement point) that controls access to Confidential/Secret data along the defined access paths.
- [ ] Set up labelling and classification for Confidential and Secret objects so that any eligible object can only be accessed through the mediation boundary.
- [ ] Implement role-based access control (RBAC) and attribute-based access control (ABAC) policy checks using the user’s identity and attributes, the resource’s classification and attributes, and the requested action, and then produce an “allow” or “deny” decision.
- [ ] Protect the reference monitor and policy documents with integrity safeguards, for example by using signed policy bundles, limiting administrator controls, and performing integrity checks while the system is running.
- [ ] Prevent bypass by always using the required mediation step, by blocking any alternative or skip paths and setting a “deny by default” rule for any unlabelled or unknown items.
- [ ] Create a repeatable test setup and produce evidence that the monitor’s decision-making logic is small, has been reviewed, and is covered by unit tests and integration tests.
- [ ] Set up audit logging so that every access attempt that is checked records: the user or subject, the item being accessed (including its label and classification), the action taken, the decision made, and the related correlation identifiers.
